Accidental General via Described Indefinite Nouns: The Oath Example
Ruling example of accidental general with oath and Ila

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a described indefinite noun becomes general ('aam) to determine the legal effect of an oath, distinguishing between perpetual Ila and permissible approach.

Core Idea
An indefinite noun described by a general condition becomes general, preventing oath violation.

In Hanafi usul, an indefinite noun (nakira) does not automatically indicate generality. However, when it is qualified by a description that is general in scope, it becomes 'accidentally general' ('aam 'aaridi). This passage illustrates this principle with a concrete oath scenario: a man swears not to approach his two wives except on a day when he approaches both. Understanding this example is crucial to grasp how textual descriptions can transform the legal effect of an oath and avoid unintended consequences like perpetual Ila.

Guided Path
1
Identify the indefinite noun and its description
Locate the indefinite noun 'a day' (يوما) in the oath. Then find the description attached to it: 'on which I approach you both' (أقربكما فيه). The description is a relative clause that qualifies the day.
The description must be general in scope to trigger the rule.
2
Recognize the default ruling without description
Imagine the oath without the description: 'I will not approach you two except on a day.' Without specification, 'a day' remains indefinite and refers to a single day. Approaching both on any day would break the oath, leading to perpetual Ila (a vow of abstinence).
Ila in law: an oath to abstain from marital relations; its minimum period for a free woman is four months.
3
Apply the rule: description creates generality
The description 'on which I approach you both' is general because it applies to any day that satisfies this condition. Therefore, the indefinite noun 'day' becomes general ('aam), covering every day he approaches both. Each such day is excepted from the oath.
This is the core of accidental general: the noun takes on generality from the description, not from its own form.
4
Derive the legal consequence for Ila
Since every day of approaching both is excepted, the man never breaks his oath by approaching both on any day. Hence, he never becomes guilty of Ila. The oath is not perpetual, and no divorce or expiation is triggered.
Without the description, he would be guilty of Ila after a single approach because the oath would be perpetual.
5
Abstract the usul principle
Formulate the principle: 'Al-nakira al-mawsufa tu'amm bi al-sifa al-'amma' (A described indefinite noun becomes general by virtue of a general description). This principle applies across legal texts where an indefinite noun is qualified by a general condition.
This is a key tool for interpreting oaths, contracts, and other 'amm texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العام العارضي
فلا يحنث بتكلم كل من كان من رجال الكوفة، وقوله: "والله لا أقربكما إلا يوما أقربكما فيه "، مثال ثانٍ لعموم النكرة الموصوفة، وهو خطاب لامرأتين، فإن قوله: "يوما" نكرة موضوعة ليوم واحد، فلو لم يصفه بقوله : أقربكما فيه لكان موليا بعد قربان يوم واحد؛ لأن هذا إيلاء مؤبد وليس مؤقتًا بأربعة أشهر حتى تنقص الأشهر الأربعة بيوم ولما وصفه بقوله: "أقربكما فيه" لم يكن موليًا أبدًا؛ لأن كل يوم يقربهما فيه يكون مستثنى من اليمين لهذه الصفة العامة فلا يحنث به.
أي أقربكما فيه
أي بقربان كل يوم
(القمر) لكان موليا : الإيلاء لغة اليمين، وشرعا: الحلف على ترك قربان الزوجة بالله أو بالطلاق أو العتاق أو غيرهما مطلقًا أو مؤقتاً بوقت وأقله للحرة أربعة أشهر، وللأمة شهران، ولا حد للأكثر ، ولا إيلاء لو حلف على ترك القربان أقل من ذلك، وحكمه: وقوع طلقة بائنة إن بر فلم يطأ، والكفارة أي في الحلف بالله والجزاء أي في الحلف بغير الله وهو المعلق إن حنث بالقربان.

The accidental general. So he does not break his oath by speaking to every man from Kufa. And his statement: 'By Allah, I will not approach you both except on a day on which I approach you both' is a second example of the generality of the described indefinite noun. It is addressed to his two wives. His word 'a day' is an indefinite noun placed for a single day. If he had not described it with his saying 'I approach you both in it', he would have been guilty of Ila after approaching on one day because this is a perpetual Ila and not limited to four months such that the four months are decreased by one day. But when he described it with his saying 'I approach you both in it', he is never guilty of Ila because every day in which he approaches them both is excepted from the oath by this general description, so he does not break his oath by it. Meaning: I approach you both in it. Meaning: by approaching each day. Its ruling: a final divorce occurs if he persists and does not have intercourse, and expiation in the case of swearing by Allah, and penalty in the case of swearing by other than Allah which is conditional if he breaks the oath by approaching. (al-Qamar) This refutes a misunderstanding that decreasing a day from its prescribed period invalidates it, and it is four months. (al-Muhashi)
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a ruling example of 'accidental general' (al-'aam al-'aaridi) in usul al-fiqh. The author presents a scenario: a man swears by Allah that he will not approach his two wives except on a day when he approaches both. The key is that 'a day' is an indefinite noun (nakira) described by the phrase 'I approach you both in it'. Without this description, the oath would be perpetual Ila (a vow to abstain from marital relations) and after one day of approach, he would break the oath. But the description makes the day general: every day that he approaches both is excepted from the oath. The commentary expands on the definition of Ila, its legal conditions, and the refutation of a potential misunderstanding about decreasing the prescribed period. This illustrates the Hanafi rule that a described indefinite noun can be general ('aam) by virtue of the description's generality.

Key Terms
العارضي (al-'aaridi): Accidental general: a term that is not inherently general but becomes general due to an external factor such as a description
النكرة الموصوفة (al-nakira al-mawsufa): An indefinite noun that is qualified by a description, which can make it general if the description is general
الإيلاء (al-iila'): A vow of abstinence from marital relations, with legal consequences including divorce if not fulfilled within a set period

B) Because the description 'أقربكما فيه' makes the day general, so every such day is excepted

Key Takeaway
A described indefinite noun becomes general ('aam 'aaridi) when the description is general in scope, as in the oath example where 'a day' qualified by 'on which I approach you both' prevents perpetual Ila.

When a Description Makes the Indefinite General: The Subject vs Object Distinction
Comparing two conditional manumission phrases to illustrate accidental general

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a description makes an indefinite noun general only when the description is a genuine attribute of the noun (i.e., the noun is the subject), not when the description refers to an external action (i.e., the noun is the object).

Core Idea
A description that is a property of the noun universalizes it; a description of an external action does not.

In usul al-fiqh, we often encounter the rule that an indefinite noun described by a general description becomes general. But does every description trigger generality? The Hanafi school refines this rule: the description must be an attribute of the noun itself, not an external action that happens to the noun. This lesson uses two manumission examples from the classical text to illustrate this critical distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two phrases
The text gives two conditional phrases: (1) 'Any of my slaves who hits you is free' and (2) 'Any of my slaves whom you hit is free'. Note the grammatical role of 'my slaves' in each: in (1) it is the subject (the one doing the hitting), in (2) it is the object (the one being hit).
The description in each case is 'hits you' and 'you hit' respectively.
2
Apply the Hanafi principle
The Hanafi position: a description makes an indefinite noun general only if the description is a genuine attribute of the noun (wasf nati). In (1), 'hits you' is an act performed by the slaves – it is their attribute. In (2), 'you hit' is an act performed by the addressee – it is not an attribute of the slaves. Therefore, only (1) triggers generality.
The description in (2) is external (wasf khariji) and does not spread to all instances.
3
Derive the ruling for each case
For (1): if all slaves hit the addressee, all are freed – the description is general and applies to every slave. For (2): even if the addressee hits all slaves, only one is freed (the first if sequential, or chosen by the master if simultaneous). The description does not make the noun general, so only one individual is affected.
The result in (2) is to avoid injustice; since the condition is not general, only one slave is freed.
4
Understand the linguistic nuance
The word 'ayy' (any) is not grammatically indefinite because it is annexed to a definite ('my slaves'), but it resembles an indefinite in ambiguity (ibham). The description lifts that ambiguity partially. In (1) the description is general and so the ambiguity is resolved to all; in (2) the description is particular (attributed to the speaker's action) so ambiguity remains, and only one is specified.
This nuance explains why the Hanafi school treats these examples differently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا إذا قال: "أي عبيدي ضربك فهو حر ، فضربوه فإنهم يعتقون، مثال ثالث لكون النكرة عامة بعموم الوصف على سبيل التشبيه للقاعدة، فإن قوله: "أي عبيدي" ليس بنكرة نحوية؛ لكونه مضافًا إلى المعرفة، ولكن يشبه النكرة في الإبهام وصف بصفة عامة، وهو قوله: "ضربك" فيعم بعموم الصفة، فيعتق كل منهم إن ضربوا المخاطب جملة مجتمعين أو متفرقين، بخلاف ما إذا قال: "أي عبيدي ضربته فهو حر" بإضافة الضرب إلى المخاطب، وجعل العبيد مضروبين، فإنهم لا يعتقون كلهم إذا ضرب المخاطب جميعهم، بل إن ضربهم بالترتيب عتق الأول؛ لعدم المزاحم، وإن ضربهم دفعة يخير المولى في تعيين واحد منهم.
(المحشي) على سبيل التشبيه إلخ : أي ليس مثالاً حقيقيًا بل هو بمنزلة المثال للقاعدة الكلية، وهي: أن كل نكرة موصوفة بصفة عامة تعم في الإثبات فإن إلخ. (القمر) ليس بنكرة نحوية إلخ قيل: إن كلمة "أي" تبقى نكرة وإن أضيفت إلى المعرفة؛ لأنه أريد بها بعض غير معين تدبر . (القمر)
And likewise, if he says: 'Any of my slaves who hits you is free,' and they hit him, then all of them are freed. This is a third example of the indefinite noun being general by the generality of the description, by way of simile to the rule. For his saying 'any of my slaves' is not an indefinite noun grammatically because it is annexed to a definite, but it resembles the indefinite in ambiguity; it is described with a general description, which is his saying 'hits you', so it becomes general by the generality of the description, and each of them is freed if they hit the addressee collectively, whether simultaneously or separately. In contrast to if he says: 'Any of my slaves whom you hit is free,' attributing the hitting to the addressee and making the slaves the object of hitting; then they are not all freed if the addressee hits all of them. Rather, if he hits them in order, the first is freed due to the absence of competition; if he hits them simultaneously, the master chooses which one to free. (al-Muhashi) 'by way of simile etc.': Meaning it is not a real example but is like an example of the universal rule, which is that every indefinite noun described by a general description is general in affirmation, etc. (al-Qamar) 'not an indefinite noun grammatically etc.' It is said that the word 'any' remains indefinite even when annexed to a definite, because it intends some unspecified individuals; consider carefully. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of accidental general with two contrasting examples from manumission. In the first, 'Any of my slaves who hits you is free,' the indefinite pronoun 'any' is described by the general description 'hits you' (the slave is the subject). Because the description is general, all slaves who hit are freed. The commentary notes that 'any' is not grammatically indefinite but resembles it. In the second example, 'Any of my slaves whom you hit is free,' the description attaches to the object (the slave is the one hit). Here, the description does not make the noun general because the hitting is attributed to the master, not the slave; thus only one slave is freed. The Hanafi distinction is based on whether the description is a property of the noun in question (subject) or external (object). The commentator (al-Muhashi) clarifies this is a simile example of the rule that a described indefinite noun is general in affirmation.

Key Terms
أي (ayy): An interrogative or conditional particle that, when annexed to a definite, resembles an indefinite noun and can become general through description
الوصف (al-wasf): The description that qualifies the indefinite noun; it may be general or particular, affecting the scope of the noun

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the phrase 'Any slave of mine whom you hit is free', if the master hits all slaves sequentially, how many slaves are freed?
A) All slaves are freed because the description is general.
B) The first slave hit is freed.
C) None are freed because the word 'any' is not indefinite.
D) The master can choose which one to free only if hit simultaneously.

Key Takeaway
A description makes an indefinite noun general only when it is a genuine attribute of the noun (subject position); otherwise, the ambiguity remains and only one individual is affected.

The Distinction Between Subject and Object Descriptions in Generality
Responding to objection that both examples have meaningful description

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction that only descriptions inherent to the noun (e.g., agent) produce generality, while object descriptions do not, even when both are meaningful.

Core Idea
Only descriptions that are inherent attributes of the noun create generality; object descriptions are superfluous and break the chain.

This passage addresses a subtle objection: if both 'any of my slaves who hits you' and 'any of my slaves whom you hit' have meaningful descriptions ('being a hitter' vs 'being hit'), why does only the first yield generality? The Hanafi school answers by distinguishing between inherent attributes of the noun and accidental ones, and between essential and superfluous grammatical components. Understanding this distinction sharpens your ability to identify when a description truly attaches to the named entity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two examples and the ruling
Recognize the pair: 'any of my slaves who hits you is free' (subject-description gives generality) vs 'any of my slaves whom you hit is free' (object-description does not give generality; defaults to one).
This difference is the core of the dispute.
2
Examine the objection
The objector argues that both examples have a meaningful description (hitter vs hit), so either both should generalize or neither. They support this by citing the locative adverb 'a day' which generalizes despite not being a subject.
The objector uses qiyas from the locative adverb.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response has two parts: (a) hitting is an attribute of the agent, not the patient—it is impossible for a single attribute to reside in both; (b) the direct object is superfluous (fadla) and not integral to the verb, unlike the locative adverb which is essential.
This is a qiyas ma'a al-fariq (analogy with a difference).
4
Apply the distinction to another case
Consider: if you say 'any slave I hit is free', the description 'hit' does not inhere in the slave, so no generality. Only when the description is an inherent property of the noun (like being the doer) does it generalize.
Test with other verbs like 'sees' or 'helps'.
5
Summarize the usul principle
The Hanafi rule: for a description to make a noun general, the description must be an attribute of the noun itself (sifah dhatiyyah), not merely a relational attribute that points to an external agent.
This principle prevents over-extension of 'amm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووجه الفرق على ما هو المشهور أن في الأول وصفه بالضاربية، فيعم بعموم الصفة، وفي الثاني قطع عن الوصفية؛ لكونه مسندًا إلى المخاطب دون أي فلا يعم ويصار إلى أخص الخصوص. وهو الواحد؛ لأنه متيقن

لأنه في كونه فضلة يشاركه المجيب صاحب "الكشف"
يخير المولى إلخ لأن نزول العتق من جهته فكان الخيار في التعيين له لا للمخاطب. (القمر)
ووجه الفرق: أي بين أي عبيدي ضربك فهو حر، وأي عبيدي ضربته فهو حر. (السنبلي) لا فاعلا إلخ أي ليس الفعل وهو أقرب مسندا إلى اليوم بل إلى ضمير المتكلم، واليوم مفعول فيه فإذا كان المفعول فيه عاما بعموم الصفة، فينبغي أن يكون في المفعول به كذلك أي العموم. (القمر) فلا يقوم بالمضروب لاستحالة قيام الصفة الواحدة بالشخصين فليس للمفعول به وصف في المثال الثاني، كذا قال صاحب " الكشف " ، وأنت لا يذهب عليك أن الضرب صفة إضافية، وكل صفة إضافية لها تعلق بالطرفين فالضرب له تعلق بالفاعل وبالمفعول به أيضًا ولا امتناع في تعلق الإضافيات بالمضافين تأمل.(القمر) والمفعول به إلخ جواب عن القياس على المفعول فيه . (القمر) لا يتوقف إلخ فإن الفعل لازم لا يحتاج إلى المفعول به إنما يحتاج إليه ضرورة تعدى الفعل، بخلاف المفعول فيه فإنه موقوف عليه لكل فعل، فقياس المفعول به على المفعول فيه قياس مع الفارق . (القمر) مفعول فيه فلا يقاس المفعول به على المفعول فيه. (المحشي)
And the distinction according to what is well-known is that in the first [example], he described him (the slave) with the attribute of being a hitter, so it generalizes by the generality of the description. In the second, he cut off from description because the hitting is attributed to the addressee, not to 'any', so it does not generalize, and one falls back to the most specific of specifics, which is one, because it is certain. And an objection was raised against it: if you intend grammatical description, then neither of the two examples is a case of description because 'any' is either relative or conditional; if you intend meaningful description, then both examples have it because, by agreement of grammarians, in the first he is described as being a hitter and in the second as being hit. Do you not see that in his saying 'except a day on which I approach you both' generality is found even though 'a day' occurs as a locative adverb, not a subject? So it should be the same for the object. And the answer is that hitting is attributed to the hitter, not to the one hit, and the object is superfluous and the verb does not depend on it, unlike the day which is a locative adverb; indeed it is part of the verb. Because in being superfluous, the answerer, the author of al-Kashf, agrees. 'The master chooses' etc. because the freeing comes from him, so the choice of designation is his, not the addressee's. (al-Qamar) 'And the distinction': i.e., between 'any of my slaves who hits you is free' and 'any of my slaves whom you hit is free'. (al-Qamar) 'Relative or conditional': what comes after 'any' is either a relative clause or a condition, so the statement that the first is description and the second is cut from description is arbitrary. (al-Muhashi) 'Generality is found' etc. i.e., due to the generality of the description, so that even if he said this to his wife and had intercourse with her, it would not be Ila; rather he may have intercourse with her whenever he wishes, unlike if the day were particular, whereupon he would be guilty of Ila after the first approach because then the single day is specified and the oath after approach would be binding. (al-Sunbuli) 'Not a subject' etc. i.e., the verb 'I approach' is not attributed to the day but to the speaker, and the day is a locative adverb. So if the locative adverb is general by the generality of the description, then the object should also be general. (al-Qamar) 'It does not apply to the one hit' because it is impossible for a single attribute to belong to two persons; so in the second example the object has no description, as stated by the author of al-Kashf. And you should note that hitting is a relational attribute, and every relational attribute relates to both parties: hitting relates to the subject and also to the object, and there is no impossibility in relational attributes relating to both. Consider carefully. (al-Qamar) 'And the object' etc. is an answer to the analogy with the locative adverb. (al-Qamar) 'It does not depend' etc. for the verb is intransitive and does not need the object; it only needs it due to transitivity, unlike the locative adverb which is dependent for every verb. So analogizing the object to the locative adverb is an analogy with a difference. (al-Qamar) 'Locative adverb': so the object cannot be analogized to the locative adverb. (al-Muhashi)
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a dispute and its resolution. The author first presents the well-known Hanafi distinction: in 'who hits you', the slave is described as a hitter (agent), so the description generalizes; in 'whom you hit', the description is cut off because the hitting is attributed to the addressee, not the slave. An objector argues that both have meaningful description ('being a hitter' vs 'being hit'), citing the first example's locative adverb 'a day' which is general even though it is not a subject. The response, given by the commentator, explains the difference: hitting is an attribute of the agent, not the patient; the object is superfluous to the verb, while the locative adverb is integral. Therefore, the object cannot be analogized to the locative adverb. This critical refinement shows the depth of Hanafi usul reasoning, distinguishing between essential and accidental attributes.

Key Terms
الوصف المعنوي (al-wasf al-ma'nawi): Meaningful description: a description that indicates a real attribute of the noun, as opposed to merely grammatical description
المفعول به (al-maf'ool bihi): The direct object: the entity on which the action falls; it is considered 'superfluous' (fadla) because the verb does not depend on it for completion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the locative adverb 'a day' (يوما) in the first example able to be general despite not being a subject, while the direct object 'whom you hit' cannot be general?
A) Because the locative adverb is an integral part of the verb's meaning, while the direct object is superfluous
B) Because the locative adverb is indefinite and the direct object is definite
C) Because the Hanafi school does not consider descriptions of objects valid
D) Because the verb 'approach' requires a time, while hitting does not

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a description generalizes only when it is an inherent attribute of the noun; object descriptions and other non-inherent attributes do not produce generality.

Accidental General: Subject vs Object Distinction
Defining accidental general through paired examples and refuting initial objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between accidental generality arising from a description of the subject versus the object, and apply the ruling to conditional manumission phrases.

Core Idea
A description attached to the subject yields generality; attached to the object, it does not.

In Hanafi usul, the accidental general ('amm 'aridi) arises when a descriptive phrase attaches to the subject of an action, making the ruling apply to all individuals meeting that description. The classic examples involve conditional manumission: 'Any of my slaves who strikes you is free' versus 'Any of my slaves you strike is free.' Understanding the crucial difference between subject and object description is key to determining whether the master retains a choice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two examples
Recognize the paired phrases: 'ayy 'abidi darabaka' (any slave who strikes you) and 'ayy 'abidi darabtahu' (any slave you strike). Determine the grammatical subject and object in each.
In the first, 'slave' is the subject; in the second, 'slave' is the object.
2
Determine the description
In the first, the slave is described as the striker (subject). In the second, the slave is described as the one struck (object). Identify who or what the description attaches to.
The description 'striking' attaches to the subject in the first, and to the object in the second.
3
Apply the generality rule
If the description attaches to the subject, generality arises: all slaves who strike are freed. If to the object, no generality: master chooses one slave.
This is the well-known position.
4
Analyze the first objection
The critic claims neither example has a grammatical description because 'ayy is a relative pronoun/conditional. Understand the distinction between grammatical and conceptual description.
Hanafis accept conceptual description even if not grammatically an adjective.
5
Understand the Hanafi response
Conceptual description exists in both examples, but only the first yields generality because the description is of the subject (the agent of striking). The description of the object does not generate generality.
This distinguishes Hanafi usul from a purely grammatical approach.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مبحث العام
العام العارضي
بالترتيب عتق الأول؛ لعدم المزاحم، وإن ضربهم دفعة يخير المولى في تعيين واحد منهم.
ووجه الفرق على ما هو المشهور أن في الأول وصفه بالضاربية، فيعم بعموم الصفة، وفي الثاني قطع عن الوصفية؛ لكونه مسندًا إلى المخاطب دون أي فلا يعم ويصار إلى أخص الخصوص. وهو الواحد؛ لأنه متيقن
واعترض عليه بأنكم إن أردتم الوصف النحوي، فليس شيء من المثالين من قبيل الوصف؛ لأن أيا موصولة أو شرطية، وإن أردتم الوصف المعنوي، ففي كل من المثالين حاصل؛ لأنه باتفاق النحاة في الأول وصفه بالضاربية وفي الثاني بالمضروبية، ألا ترى أن في قوله: "إلا يوما أقربكما فيه" وجد العموم مع أن يومًا وقع مفعولاً فيه لا فاعلاً، فينبغي أن يكون في المفعول به كذلك وأجيب بأن الضرب يقوم بالضارب، فلا يقوم بالمضروب، والمفعول به فضلة لا يتوقف الفعل عليه، بخلاف يوماً وهو مفعول فيه، فإنه جزء من الفعل؛ لأنه عبارة عن الحدث مع الزمان فيتلازمان وقيل في الفرق بينهما: إن في الصورة الأولى لما علّق العتق بضرب العبيد يسارع كل منهم إلى ضربه لأجل عتقه، فلا يمكن التخير فيه للمولى بلا مرجح فيعم، بخلاف الصورة الثانية؛ فإنه علق فيها على ضرب المخاطب، فلا ينبغي له أن يضربهم جميعا ليُعتقوا، فيخير فيه المولى بين واحد منهم. وكذا إذا دخلت لام التعريف فيما لا يحتمل التعريف بمعنى العهد، أو جبت العموم، يعني كما أن النكرة إذا وصفت بصفة عامة تعم كذلك إذا دخلت لام المعرفة في صورة لا يستقيم التعريف العهدي أو جبت العموم، سواء كان العموم مع الزمان أي مع النسبة إلى الزمان فيتلازمان أي الفعل والمفعول فيه. (القمر) فلا يمكن التخير فيه إلخ ونظيره في كلام الفقهاء: "أيما إهاب دبغ فقد طهر" فإن طهارته متعلقة بدباغة من غير أن يكون له فاعل معين يمكن منه التخير فيدل على العموم (السنبلي) فيخير فيه إلخ ونظيره "كل أي خبز تريد" فإن التخير من الفاعل المخاطب ممكن فيه، فلا يتمكن من أكل كل واحد بل أكل واحد لكن يتخير فيه المخاطب. (السنبلي) فيما لا يحتمل إلخ لفظ "ما" كناية عن اللفظ مفردًا كان أو جمعًا، والتخصيص بالمفرد يأباه قول المصنف حتى يسقط إلخ، وإلى التعميم أشار الشارح بقوله : في صورة إلخ. (القمر) بمعنى إلخ : أي بسبب معنى العهد.(القمر) سواء كان إلخ تحقيقه : أن اللام بالإجماع لتعريف مدخولها، فإما أن يشار بها إلى الحقيقة من حيث هي هي من غير نظر إلى الأفراد فهي لام الجنس، وإما أن يشار بها إلى حصة معينة من الحقيقة وهي لام العهد الخارج أو إلى حصة غير معينة من الحقيقة وهي لام العهد الذهني أو إلى جميع أفراد الحقيقة فهي لام الاستغراق، فالأول: مثل: الرجل خير من المرأة، والثاني: مثل: جاءني رجل فقال الرجل: كذا، والثالث: مثل: أدخل السوق، والرابع: مثل: ﴿إِنَّ الْإِنْسَانَ لَفِي خُسْرٍ إِلَّا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ﴾ (العصر:٣،٢) فهذه أربعة أقسام. ثم أنهم اختلفوا في أن التعين المعتبر في لام العهد الخارجي أعم من التعين في الخارج والذهن، أو هو مخصوص بالتعين في الخارج، فافترقوا فرقتين فعلى الثاني المراد من عدم التعين في لام العهد الذهني عدم التعين الخارجي وإن تحقق التعين الذهني، ولتطويل الكلام في الألف واللام موضع آخر وهذا القدر في هذا المقام يكفي لطالب المرام. (القمر)
Topic of the General: The Accidental General: If they strike in sequence, the first is freed due to no competition; if they strike simultaneously, the master may choose which one to free. And the aspect of the difference according to what is well-known is that in the first [example], the slave is described as striking, so it becomes general due to the generality of the description, while in the second, it is disconnected from being a description because it is attributed to the addressee and not to 'ayy, so it does not become general and one resorts to the most specific of specifics, which is one, because it is certain. And it was objected: If you mean the grammatical description, then neither of the two examples is of the type of description, because 'ayy is a relative pronoun or conditional; and if you mean the conceptual description, then it is present in both examples, because according to the consensus of grammarians, in the first it is described as striking, and in the second as being struck. Do you not see that in his statement: 'except a day on which the nearer of you two is in it,' generality is found even though 'day' occurs as an adverb of time, not as a subject? So it should be similarly in the case of the object [of the verb]. And it was answered: Striking subsists in the striker, so it does not subsist in the one struck, and the object is an extra element upon which the verb does not depend, unlike 'day' which is an adverb, for it is part of the verb because it expresses the event together with time, so they are inseparable. And it was said regarding the difference between them: In the first form, since emancipation is conditioned upon the striking of the slaves, each one hastens to strike him for the sake of his emancipation, so the master cannot choose without a preponderant factor, thus it becomes general. In contrast to the second form: because it is conditioned upon the striking of the addressee, so he should not strike all of them to have them freed; thus the master may choose among them one. And similarly, when the definite article 'lam' enters upon what does not admit definition in the sense of specific reference, it necessitates generality. That is, just as an indefinite noun when described with a general description becomes general, similarly when the definite article enters in a situation where specific reference is not valid, it necessitates generality, whether the generality is with time—meaning with relation to time—so they are inseparable, i.e., the verb and the adverb. (Al-Qamar) So he cannot choose etc. — and its parallel in the speech of jurists: 'Any hide that is tanned has become pure,' for its purification is tied to tanning without having a specific agent who can choose, so it indicates generality. (Al-Sanbalī) So he chooses etc. — and its parallel: 'Any bread you want,' for choice by the addressee (the agent) is possible in it, so he cannot eat every one but rather one, but the addressee chooses among them. (Al-Sanbalī) In what does not admit etc. — the word 'ma' is a representation of the word, whether singular or plural, and specification to the singular is rejected by the author's statement 'until it falls' etc., and the commentator pointed to generality by his saying: 'in a situation' etc. (Al-Qamar) Meaning 'as specific reference' etc. — i.e., due to the meaning of specific reference. (Al-Qamar) 'Whether it is' etc. — its verification: That the 'lam' by consensus defines its object of entry. It either points to the essence in itself without regard to individuals, and that is the lam of genus; or it points to a specific portion of the essence, and that is the lam of external specific reference or to an unspecified portion of the essence, and that is the lam of mental specific reference; or it points to all individuals of the essence, and that is the lam of universal inclusion. The first is like: 'Man is better than woman'; the second like: 'A man came to me, so the man said such-and-such'; the third like: 'Enter the market'; the fourth like: 'Indeed, mankind is in loss, except those who believe and do righteous deeds' (103:2-3). These are four divisions. Then they disagreed whether the specifiedness considered in the lam of external specific reference is more general than external and mental specification, or is specific to external specification, so they split into two groups. According to the second, what is meant by the absence of specification in the lam of mental specific reference is the absence of external specification even if mental specification is realized. And to lengthen discourse on the 'alif and lam is another place, and this amount suffices the seeker herein. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a defining discussion of the concept of 'accidental general' ('amm 'aridi) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author presents two key examples: (1) 'Any of my slaves who strikes you is free' and (2) 'Any of my slaves you strike is free.' In the first, the slave is described as the striker, so the description of striking attaches to each slave collectively, making the phrase general (all slaves who strike are freed). If they strike simultaneously, the master normally would have a choice, but here due to the generality of the description, all are freed. In the second, the description of being struck attaches to the addressee, not to the slave individually; the slave is merely the object of the action, so the description does not generate generality, and the master may choose any one slave to free. The author then addresses an objection from a critic (likely al-Kashshaf or a grammarian) who argues that grammatical description is absent in both examples because 'ayy is a relative pronoun or conditional; the author responds by distinguishing between grammatical and conceptual description. A further objection is raised by analogy to an adverb of time where generality occurs despite the word being an adverb, not a subject. The author answers that the verb depends on the adverb (since action requires time) but does not depend on the object, so the analogy fails. A different explanation is then given: in the first example, each slave hastens to strike to gain freedom, making choice impractical, so generality follows; in the second, the addressee may not strike all, so the master chooses. The passage also discusses the definite article 'lam' and its types (genus, external specific reference, mental specific reference, universal inclusion), noting that when 'lam' cannot indicate specific reference, it necessitates generality. Finally, a dispute among scholars about the nature of specification in the lam of external specific reference is mentioned.

Key Terms
العام العارضي (al-‘āmm al-‘āriḍī): The accidental general: a phrase that acquires generality not by its inherent wording but due to an attached description (ṣifa) that encompasses all individuals.
الصفة (al-ṣifa): The description that provides the basis for generality; in this context, the description of the subject (e.g., being the striker) that applies to all individuals.
الوصف المعنوي (al-waṣf al-ma‘nawī): Conceptual description – the underlying attribution of an action to a noun, even if the grammatical form is not an adjective. For example, in 'any slave who strikes', the conceptual description is 'striker'.
فضلة (fuḍla): An extra element (e.g., the object of a verb) that is not essential to the completeness of the verbal sentence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the second example 'Any of my slaves you strike is free', why does the master have a choice?
A) Because the slave is described as the striker, so generality would force freeing all.
B) Because the description of striking attaches to the addressee, not the slave, so no generality arises.
C) Because 'ayy is always a relative pronoun and thus does not indicate generality.
D) Because the verb is in the past tense, which restricts the ruling to a single action.

Key Takeaway
In accidental generality, the description must attach to the subject of the action; if it attaches to the object, generality fails.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
The Role of the Definite Article in Generating Generality
Extension of accidental general to the definite article and classification of its types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four types of the definite article 'lam' in Arabic and determine when it necessitates generality in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
The definite article 'lam' necessitates generality when it cannot indicate specific reference.

In addition to accidental general arising from descriptions, the Hanafi school also recognizes that the definite article 'lam' itself can generate generality. This occurs when the context does not allow for a specific reference ('ahd). The passage classifies four types of 'lam' and highlights a scholarly dispute regarding the lam of external specific reference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
Understand that when the definite article 'lam' enters upon a noun that does not admit specific reference (ta'rif bi ma'na al-'ahd), it necessitates generality.
This is analogous to an indefinite noun described with a general description becoming general.
2
Understand the analogy
Just as an indefinite noun (nakira) when described with a general description becomes general, similarly the definite article in a context where specific reference is invalid yields generality.
The 'lam' itself acts as a generalizing element.
3
Learn the four types of 'lam'
1) Lam al-Jins (genus) – points to the essence without regard to individuals. 2) Lam al-'Ahd al-Khariji (external specific) – points to a specific external referent. 3) Lam al-'Ahd al-Dhihni (mental specific) – points to an unspecified mental referent. 4) Lam al-Istighraq (universal inclusion) – points to all individuals.
The fourth type is the one that necessitates generality.
4
Note the scholarly dispute
Scholars differ on whether the specification in lam al-'ahd al-khariji is limited to external specification or includes mental specification. There are two opinions.
This dispute affects the interpretation of certain texts.
5
Apply to examples
The passage gives examples: 'Any hide that is tanned becomes pure' (the 'lam' is not on 'hide' but the context shows no specific hide, so it indicates generality). Another: 'Any bread you want' – here the addressee can choose, so no generality.
The hide example parallels the first type of accidental general (subject description), while the bread example parallels the second (object description).

Commentary
This passage is a defining discussion of the concept of 'accidental general' ('amm 'aridi) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author presents two key examples: (1) 'Any of my slaves who strikes you is free' and (2) 'Any of my slaves you strike is free.' In the first, the slave is described as the striker, so the description of striking attaches to each slave collectively, making the phrase general (all slaves who strike are freed). If they strike simultaneously, the master normally would have a choice, but here due to the generality of the description, all are freed. In the second, the description of being struck attaches to the addressee, not to the slave individually; the slave is merely the object of the action, so the description does not generate generality, and the master may choose any one slave to free. The author then addresses an objection from a critic (likely al-Kashshaf or a grammarian) who argues that grammatical description is absent in both examples because 'ayy is a relative pronoun or conditional; the author responds by distinguishing between grammatical and conceptual description. A further objection is raised by analogy to an adverb of time where generality occurs despite the word being an adverb, not a subject. The author answers that the verb depends on the adverb (since action requires time) but does not depend on the object, so the analogy fails. A different explanation is then given: in the first example, each slave hastens to strike to gain freedom, making choice impractical, so generality follows; in the second, the addressee may not strike all, so the master chooses. The passage also discusses the definite article 'lam' and its types (genus, external specific reference, mental specific reference, universal inclusion), noting that when 'lam' cannot indicate specific reference, it necessitates generality. Finally, a dispute among scholars about the nature of specification in the lam of external specific reference is mentioned.

Key Terms
لام الجنس (lām al-jins): The definite article that points to the essence of a noun without regard to individuals.
لام العهد الخارجي (lām al-‘ahd al-khārijī): The definite article that points to a specific portion of the essence known externally.
لام العهد الذهني (lām al-‘ahd al-dhihnī): The definite article that points to an unspecified portion of the essence known mentally.
لام الاستغراق (lām al-istighrāq): The definite article that points to all individuals of the essence, indicating universal inclusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for the definite article to necessitate generality?
A) It always necessitates generality regardless of context.
B) When it is lam al-istighraq only.
C) When it enters a noun that does not admit specific reference in the sense of 'ahd.
D) When it is lam al-jins.

Key Takeaway
The definite article generates generality when the context precludes specific reference, as in lam al-istighraq.

Types of Alif Lam and Their Priority in Indicating Generality
Classifying the definite article and its role in general and specific reference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four types of alif lam and apply the Hanafi priority rule to determine the intended meaning of a definite noun in a given text.

Core Idea
The definite article primarily indicates external covenant; only when that fails do we consider genus or comprehensive generality.

In Hanafi usul, the definite article (alif lam) is not merely a marker of generality—it carries a nuanced priority system. This lesson unpacks the four categories of lam and the hierarchical method for choosing between them, with emphasis on the Quranic evidence that supports lam al-istighraq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four types of lam
Recall the consensus that lam introduces definition. It can point to the essence (lam al-jins), a specific individual (external covenant), an unspecified individual (mental covenant), or all individuals (comprehensive).
2
Understand the default priority
Hanafi usul holds that the primary meaning of lam is external covenant, because it gives the clearest specification. Mental covenant is like an indefinite and is not preferred over comprehensive.
Opponents like the author of al-Tawdih give mental covenant priority over comprehensive.
3
Apply the exception test
When no external covenant is possible, examine whether the context allows an exception. If an exception is valid, the lam likely indicates comprehensive generality (istighraq), as in the verse 'Indeed mankind is in loss' except those who believe.
The validity of exception is a key test for generality.
4
Recognize the scholarly dispute
Some usulists (e.g., al-Tawdih) argue that mental covenant takes priority over comprehensive. The Hanafi response is that mental covenant is like an indefinite, so it does not precede istighraq.
This affects interpretation of phrases like 'Enter the market' where the market is any market (mental covenant) but not all markets.
5
Evaluate the evidence
Analyze the Quranic proof: 'Indeed mankind is in loss' with the exception 'except those who believe' shows that 'mankind' must comprehend all individuals, proving istighraq is intended when covenant fails.
The exception would be invalid if lam indicated genus or mental covenant.

Section on the General ('Amm). Page 225: The incidental general ('amm al-'aridi) because it is an expression of the event with time, so they are inseparable. It was said regarding the difference between the two: in the first form of the two mentioned examples, since the emancipation was attached to striking the slaves, each of them hastens to strike him for his emancipation, so the master cannot choose without a preference, so it becomes general. Unlike the second form, where it was attached to the striking of the addressee, so he should not strike all of them to free them; thus the master chooses among one of them. Similarly, when the definite article (lam) enters upon something that does not admit definition by way of specified covenant ('ahd), it necessitates generality. Meaning, just as an indefinite noun (nakira) when qualified by a general attribute becomes general, similarly when the definite article enters in a manner that the definition by covenant is not sound, it necessitates generality, whether the generality is with time, i.e., with relation to time, so they are inseparable, i.e., the verb and the object of time. (al-Qamar) So choice is not possible, etc. Its parallel in the speech of jurists: 'Any hide that is tanned, it becomes pure' — its purity is attached to tanning without a specific agent capable of choice, so it indicates generality. (al-Sanbali) 'So he chooses among them' etc. Its parallel is 'Every bread you desire' — the choice of the addressee is possible in it; so he cannot eat each one but one, but the addressee chooses among them. (al-Sanbali) 'Regarding what does not admit' etc. The word 'ma' is a metonymy for the word, whether singular or plural. The specification by the singular is precluded by the author's statement 'until it falls' etc. (al-Qamar) 'By meaning of covenant' etc.: i.e., because of the meaning of covenant. (al-Qamar) 'Whether it is' etc. Its verification: that the lam, by consensus, is for defining its object. It either points to the essence as it is, without regard to individuals — that is lam al-jins (the genus lam); or points to a specific portion of the essence — that is lam al-'ahd al-khariji (external covenant lam); or points to an unspecified portion — that is lam al-'ahd al-dhihni (mental covenant lam); or points to all individuals of the essence — that is lam al-istighraq (comprehensive lam). The first: like 'Man is better than woman.' The second: like 'A man came to me, and the man said such-and-such.' The third: like 'Enter the market.' The fourth: like 'Indeed, mankind is in loss, except those who believe and do righteous deeds' (Surah al-'Asr, 103:2-3). These are four divisions. Then they differed regarding whether the specifiedness considered in the external covenant lam is more general than specification in externality and mind, or is specific to specification in externality, so they split into two groups. According to the second, the intended meaning of the absence of specification in the mental covenant lam is the absence of external specification, even if mental specification is realized. (al-Qamar) Page 226: The incidental general ('amm al-'aridi) is for the genus as held by Fakhr al-Islam and his followers, or for comprehensive generality (istighraq) as held by the Arabic scholars and the majority of usulists. In it is a notification that the covenant is the primary use of the lam: as long as the covenant interpretation is sound, one does not move to another meaning, whether it is external or mental covenant as held by some. It was said: only external covenant, because it is the basis in definition, and the mentally covenanted is in meaning like the indefinite. If the covenant is not sound — because there are no covenanted individuals or its mention did not precede — it is taken to mean genus, which can mean the minimum or the whole depending on the context, or to comprehensive generality, which encompasses all individuals with certainty, as in the verse 'Indeed, mankind is in loss' (al-'Asr). The essence: For the genus etc., for in the genus there is a meaning of generality in that it applies to the true individual and to the totality of its individuals, because it is one legal entity. (al-Qamar) 'In it' i.e., in the author's statement 'regarding what does not admit' etc. (al-Qamar) 'That the covenant is primary': the detail as in al-Talwih: that the pointing by lam is either to a specific portion by way of covenant definition, or to the essence itself, and that may be such that it does not need consideration of individuals — that is definition of the essence, quiddity, and nature — or may need it, and then either there exists a contextual indication of partiality as in 'Enter the market' — that is the mental covenant — or not, and that is comprehensive generality. Thus mental covenant and comprehensive generality are branches of definition of the essence. Therefore the verifiers held that the lam is only for definition of the essence and covenant. However, the scholars took the result and made it four divisions for clarification and facilitation. Once this is established, we say: the primary (i.e., the preponderant) is the external covenant; because it is the reality of specification and complete distinction, then comprehensive generality; because the ruling on the essence itself without consideration of individuals is very rare. Then he said after that, 'And in what the author (i.e., the author of al-Tawdih) mentioned there is consideration, because he gave priority to the mental over comprehensive generality.' (al-Sanbali) As held by some, including the author of al-Tawdih. (al-Qamar) It was said: the proponent is the author of al-Talwih. (al-Qamar) 'For it is the primary': i.e., the preponderant; because it is the reality of specification and complete distinction. (al-Qamar) 'Like the indefinite': hence the mentally covenanted is described as indefinite and as a whole. (al-Qamar) 'Depending on the context': the absolute stripped of indicators is carried on the minimum; because it is certain. When indicators like intent etc. exist, it is carried on the whole, as in al-Kashf. (al-Qamar) 'Indeed, mankind is in loss': this is taken to mean comprehensive generality, and the evidence is the validity of the exception 'except those who believe' etc. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul rule defining the types of the definite article (alif lam) and their priority in indicating generality ('umum). The commentator begins by distinguishing between true general ('amm haqiqi) and incidental general ('amm 'aridi) through examples: when emancipation is attached to striking all slaves, each slave hastens to be struck, so the master has no choice; but when attached to the addressee's striking, the master chooses one. This illustrates how the form of the condition affects generality. Then the focus shifts to the definite article. It is established by consensus that lam is for definition (ta'rif). Four types are identified: (1) lam al-jins (genus lam) pointing to the essence disregarding individuals, e.g., 'Man is better than woman'; (2) lam al-'ahd al-khariji (external covenant) pointing to a specific known individual, e.g., 'the man' referring to one previously mentioned; (3) lam al-'ahd al-dhihni (mental covenant) pointing to an unspecified individual of a type, e.g., 'Enter the market' (any market); (4) lam al-istighraq (comprehensive) encompassing all individuals, e.g., 'Indeed mankind is in loss'. There is disagreement on priority: the preponderant view (external covenant first, then comprehensive) is preferred because external covenant gives the clearest specification. The mental covenant is like an indefinite, so it is not primary. If no covenant is possible, the lam is taken for genus or comprehensive depending on context. The Qur'anic example of istighraq is validated by the exception. This analysis is key to understanding how Hanafi usul handles textual ambiguity.

Key Terms
العام العارضي (al-'amm al-'aridi): The incidental general: generality that arises from attaching a ruling to a general description of the action (like time) rather than the subject itself.
لام العهد الخارجي (lam al-'ahd al-khariji): The definite article that refers to a specific individual known externally, e.g., 'the man' meaning a particular man previously seen or mentioned.
لام الاستغراق (lam al-istighraq): The definite article that embraces all individuals of a genus, equivalent to 'all'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, which type of lam is given priority (al-asl) when interpreting a definite noun?
A) Lam al-jins (genus lam)
B) Lam al-'ahd al-khariji (external covenant lam)
C) Lam al-'ahd al-dhihni (mental covenant lam)
D) Lam al-istighraq (comprehensive lam)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the definite article's primary function is external covenant; comprehensive generality is only adopted when covenant fails and the context supports it.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Hierarchy of Lam: 'Ahd, Istighraq, and Jins
Exploring the functions of lam: 'ahd, jins, istighraq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi hierarchy of meanings for the definite article (lam) to identify whether a text indicates specific reference ('ahd), universal coverage (istighraq), or genus (jins), and to derive the resulting legal ruling.

Core Idea
The lam primarily indicates specific reference ('ahd); only when 'ahd is impossible does it shift to universal coverage or genus.

In this passage, we delve into the nuanced functions of the definite article (alif lam) in Arabic. While many assume it always signals generality, Hanafi usul teaches that its primary role is to point to a particular referent ('ahd). Only when such specification is impossible does the lam expand to indicate the entire genus or universal coverage. This hierarchy is essential for correctly interpreting Quranic verses and legal texts, and its misapplication can lead to erroneous rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term with lam and its context
Locate the noun carrying the definite article and consider the broader speech situation—is there a specific referent known externally or through prior mention?
For example, 'al-rajul' in a story where a specific man was previously mentioned suggests mental 'ahd.
2
Determine if 'ahd (specific reference) is possible
Check for external 'ahd (e.g., pointing to a person) or mental 'ahd (e.g., previously mentioned or commonly known). If either exists, the lam indicates that specific referent.
External 'ahd is the strongest; mental 'ahd is like an indefinite.
3
If 'ahd is not possible, check for universal coverage (istighraq) or genus (jins)
When 'ahd fails, the lam may indicate the whole genus (jins) applying to any individual, or universal coverage (istighraq) applying to every individual. Look for contextual clues such as exceptions or feasibility.
Universal coverage is proven by valid exception (e.g., 'except those who believe' in al-Asr).
4
Apply the hierarchy: external 'ahd > universal coverage > mental 'ahd > genus
The preponderant order is: external 'ahd first, then istighraq, then mental 'ahd, then jins. This determines the lam's meaning.
Some scholars (e.g., author of al-Tawdih) place mental 'ahd before istighraq, but the preponderant view critiqued in the text favors istighraq above mental 'ahd.
5
For plural nouns with lam, note that the lam overrides the plural meaning
When lam enters a plural noun, the literal meaning of plurality (minimum three) drops. The lam must then indicate genus, so the term applies to even one individual.
Oath: 'I will not marry al-nisa'' is broken by marrying one woman, not three.

مبحث العام
العام العارضي للجنس كما ذهب إليه فخر الإسلام ،وتابعوه أو للاستغراق كما ذهب إليه أهل العربية، وجمهور الأصوليين.
وفيه تنبيه على أن العهد هو الأصل في اللام، فما دام يستقيم العهد لا يصار إلى معنى آخر، سواء كان عهدًا خارجيًا أو ذهنيًا كما ذهب إليه البعض، وقيل: عهدًا خارجيًا فقط، فإنه الأصل في التعريف، والمعهود الذهني في المعنى كالنكرة، فإن لم يستقم العهد بأن لم يكن ثمه أفراد معهودة أو لم يجر ذكره فيما سبق حُمِل على الجنس، فيحتمل الأدنى، والكل على حسب قابلية المقام، أو على الاستغراق، فيستوعب الكل يقينًا كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ الْإِنْسَانَ لَفِي خُسْرٍ إِلَّا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ (العصر : ٢ ، ٣ ) .
الحقيقة وهو للجنس إلخ فإن في الجنس معنى العموم من حيث أنه يقع على الواحد الحقيقي، وعلى مجموع أفراده؛ لأنه واحد حكمي البتة كما مر (القمر) وفيه أي في قول المصنف فيما لا يحتمل إلى آخره. (القمر) على أن العهد هو الأصل: التفصيل كما في "التلويح : أن الإشارة باللام إما إلى حصة معينة من تعريف العهد، وإما إلى نفس الحقيقة وذلك قد يكون بحيث لا يفتقر إلى اعتبار الأفراد وهو تعريف الحقيقة والماهية والطبيعة، وقد يكون بحيث يفتقر إليه، وحينئذ إما أن يوجد فيه قرينة البعضية كما في "أدخل السوق" وهو العهد الذهني أو لا وهو الاستغراق، فالعهد الذهني والاستغراق من فروع تعريف الحقيقة، ولذا ذهب المحققون إلى أن اللام لتعريف الحقيقة والعهد لا غير، إلا أن القوم أخذوا بالحاصل وجعلوه أربعة أقسام توضيحا وتسهيلاً، إذا تمهد هذا فنقول: الأصل أي الراجح هو العهد الخارجي؛ لأنه حقيقة التعين وكمال التميز، ثم الاستغراق؛ لأن الحكم على نفس الحقيقة بدون اعتبار الأفراد قليل جدا، ثم قال بعد ذلك وفيما ذكره المصنف أي صاحب "التوضيح نظر ؛ لأنه جعل الذهنى مقدمًا على الاستغراق . (السنبلي)
كما ذهب إليه البعض ومنهم صاحب "التوضيح " . (القمر) وقيل: القائل صاحب "التلويح". (القمر) فإنه الأصل: أي الراجح؛ لأنه حقيقة التعيين وكمال التمييز. (القمر) كالنكرة ولذا يوصف المعهود الذهني بالنكرة وبالجملة. (القمر) على حسب قابلية المقام فالمطلق المجرد عن الدلائل يحمل على الأدنى؛ لأنه متيقن، وإذا وجدت الدلائل كالنية وغيرها يحمل على الكل كذا في "الكشف". (القمر) إن الإنسان لفي خسر: هذا محمول على الاستغراق والعموم، والدليل عليه صحة الاستثناء بقوله: إلا الذين إلخ. (القمر)
وقوله: ﴿وَالسَّارِقُ وَالسَّارِقَةُ والزَّانِيَةُ وَالزَّانِي وأمثاله.
"أوجبـ (المائدة: ۳۸) (النور: ٢)
حتى يسقط اعتبار الجمعية إذا دخلت على الجمع عملاً بالدليلين تفريع على قوله: جبت العموم أي هذا القدر إذا كان دخول اللام في المفرد، وأما إذا كان على الجمع فثمرة عمومه أنه يسقط معنى الجمع، فلا تكون أقله الثلاث؛ إذ لو بقي جمعا لم يظهر للام فائدة؛ إذ لا عهد ولا استغراق ولا جنس فيجب أن يحمل على الجنس ليكون ما دون الثلاثة معمولا للجنس، وما فوقه للجمع.
هذا هو العمل بالدليلين
فيحنث بتزوج امرأة واحدة إذا حلف لا يتزوج النساء ولو كان معنى الجمع باقيا لما حنث بما دون الثلاثة، ومثله قوله تعالى : ولا يَحِلُّ لَكَ النِّسَاءُ مِنْ بَعْدُ، وقوله تعالى: (الأحزاب: ٥٢) إِنَّمَا الصَّدَقَاتُ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ وَالْمَسَاكِينِ ﴾ (الآية)، فتكفي الصدقة لجنس الفقير والمسكين، (التوبة: ٤٠)
والسارق إلخ : إنما أورد هذا المثال إيماء إلى أن المراد ههنا باللام أعم من حرف التعريف واسم الموصول، فإن معنى السارق والسارقة الذي سرق والتي سرقت (القمر) عملاً بالدليلين أي دليل التعريف وهو اللام، ودليل الصيغة، والمراد بالدليل: الدال لا المعنى المصطلح كما هو الظاهر. (القمر)
الجمعية وهي
هذا القدر: يعني أن دخول اللام مفيد للعموم. (القمر) إذ لا عهد لأن الكلام فيما لا يحتمل التعريف بمعنى العهد. (القمر) ولا استغراق لعدم الفائدة إما في قوله "لا أتزوج النساء فلأن اليمين يكون للمنع، وتزوج جميع نساء الدنيا خارج عن طوق البشر، فمنعه يكون لغوا، وإما في قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّمَا الصَّدَقَاتُ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ (التوبة: ٦٠)، فلأنه لا يمكن صرف جميع الصدقات إلى جميع فقراء الدنيا، وقس على هذا فليس ههنا استغراق. (القمر) ولا جنس لأن الكلام على تقدير بقاء الجمعية، وحينئذ فلا أثر للجنسية. (القمر) فيجب إلخ: أي إذا كان بقاء
الجمعية موجبًا للغوية اللام، فيجب أن يحمل اللام على الجنس، ويسقط اعتبار الجمعية ليكون إلخ. (القمر) فيحنث إلخ بخلاف ما إذا حلف لا أتزوج نساء بدون اللام، فيحنث حينئذ بتزوج ثلاث نسوة عملاً بصيغة الجمع، ولا يحنث بتزوج امرأة أو امرأتين. (القمر) لا يحل لك إلخ الخطاب إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أي لا يحل لك النساء أي واحدة من النساء من بعد التسع، فهو في حقه الا الله كالأربع في حقنا كذا قال البيضاوي.(القمر) للفقراء والمساكين الفقير من له أدنى شيء، والمسكين من لا شيء له، وهو المروي عن الإمام الأعظم الله وروي عن الزهري الفقير: الساكن في بيته ولا يسأل الناس والمسكين من يخرج ويسأل الناس.
Section on the General (al-‘Aam)
The accidental general (al-‘aam al-‘aaridi) is for the genus (jins) as held by Fakhr al-Islam and his followers, or for universal coverage (istighraq) as held by the Arabic grammarians and the majority of usul scholars.
In it is a reminder that the specific reference (‘ahd) is the origin in the lam (definite article). So long as the specific reference is valid, no other meaning is resorted to, whether it is external specific reference (khariji) or mental specific reference (dhihni) as held by some. And it is said: only external specific reference, because it is the origin in definition, and the mentally specified is like the indefinite (nakirah). If the specific reference is not valid—because there are no specified individuals or it was not previously mentioned—then it is carried upon the genus, so it admits the least (individual), and all according to the capacity of the context, or upon universal coverage, so it encompasses all with certainty as in His saying: 'Indeed, mankind is in loss, except those who believe and do righteous deeds' (al-‘Asr 2-3).
The reality is that it is for the genus, etc., for in the genus there is a meaning of generality from the perspective that it applies to the single true individual and to the sum of its individuals because it is a single legal entity as mentioned (al-Qamar). And in it—i.e., in the author's statement 'in what does not admit' etc. (al-Qamar)—that specific reference is the origin: the detail as in al-Talwih: that the indication of the lam is either to a specific portion through definition of specific reference, or to the reality itself, and that may be such that it does not require considering individuals—that is the definition of reality, essence, and nature—and may be such that it requires considering individuals. Then either there is a contextual indication of partiality as in 'Enter the market,' which is mental specific reference, or not, which is universal coverage. Thus mental specific reference and universal coverage are branches of the definition of reality. Therefore the verifiers held that the lam is for defining reality and specific reference only, except that the people adopted the outcome and made it four categories for clarification and facilitation. When this is established, we say: The origin (i.e., the preponderant) is external specific reference because it is the reality of determination and perfection of distinction, then universal coverage because ruling upon reality itself without considering individuals is very rare. Then he said afterwards: In what the author (i.e., the author of al-Tawdih) mentioned there is a point of consideration; because he made mental specific reference precede universal coverage (al-Sunbuli).
As held by some including the author of al-Tawdih (al-Qamar). And it is said: the one who said it is the author of al-Talwih (al-Qamar). For it (external specific reference) is the origin (i.e., preponderant) because it is the reality of determination and perfection of distinction (al-Qamar). Like the indefinite (nakirah), therefore the mentally specified is described as indefinite and in summary (al-Qamar). According to the capacity of the context: the absolute stripped of indications is carried upon the least because it is certain, and if indications exist like intention and others, it is carried upon the whole—as in al-Kashshaf (al-Qamar). 'Indeed, mankind is in loss': this is carried upon universal coverage and generality, and the proof for it is the validity of the exception by His saying 'except those who believe' etc. (al-Qamar).
And His saying: 'And the thief, male and female, and the adulterer, male and female' and similar examples (al-Ma'idah 38, al-Nur 2).
'It necessitates...' until the consideration of plural drops when it (the lam) enters the plural, acting upon two indicators. This is a branching upon his saying 'it necessitated generality': that is, this capacity if the lam enters a singular; but if it enters a plural, then the benefit of its generality is that it drops the meaning of plurality, so it (the plural) is not at its minimum of three; for if it remained plural, there would be no benefit for the lam, because there is no specific reference, nor universal coverage, nor genus. So it must be carried upon the genus so that what is below three is operated by the genus, and what is above it (three) by the plural.
This is the operation of the two indicators.
Thus he breaks his oath by marrying one woman if he swore 'I will not marry women' (al-nisa'), whereas if the meaning of plurality remained, he would not break it by marrying less than three. Similar is His saying: 'Women are not permissible for you from now on' (al-Ahzab 52), and His saying: 'Indeed the charities are for the poor and the needy' (al-Tawbah 60); then giving charity to one of the genus of the poor or the needy suffices.
'And the thief, etc.': This example is only given to indicate that the meaning here of the lam is more general than the definite article and the relative pronoun, for the meaning of 'al-sariq' and 'al-sariqah' is 'the one who stole' and 'the one who stole (female)' (al-Qamar). Acting upon two indicators: i.e., the indicator of definition which is the lam, and the indicator of the form; and by 'indicator' is meant the indicator not the technical meaning as is apparent (al-Qamar).
'This capacity': means that the entry of the lam is beneficial for generality (al-Qamar). 'Because there is no specific reference': because the speech is about what does not admit definition in the sense of specific reference (al-Qamar). 'And no universal coverage' due to lack of benefit. For example in his saying 'I will not marry women' (without lam), the oath is for prohibition, and marrying all women of the world is beyond human capacity, so forbidding it would be meaningless. And in His saying: 'Indeed the charities are for the poor' (al-Tawbah 60), because it is impossible to distribute all charities to all the poor of the world; and analogize to this; thus there is no universal coverage here (al-Qamar). 'And no genus': because the speech assumes the continuation of plurality, and then there is no effect of genus (al-Qamar). 'So it must': i.e., if the continuation of plurality causes the lam to be meaningless, then the lam must be carried upon the genus, and the consideration of plurality drops (al-Qamar). 'Thus he breaks his oath, etc.': contrary to if he swore 'I will not marry nisa' (without lam); then he breaks by marrying three women acting upon the plural form, and does not break by marrying one or two women (al-Qamar). 'Women are not permissible for you, etc.': the address is to the Prophet (peace be upon him), i.e., no woman is permissible for you after the nine, so it is in his case like the four in our case—thus said al-Baydawi (al-Qamar). 'For the poor and the needy': the poor (faqir) is one who has the least thing, and the needy (miskin) is one who has nothing; this is narrated from the Great Imam (Abu Hanifa). And it is narrated from al-Zuhri: the faqir is the one who stays in his house and does not ask people, and the miskin is the one who goes out and asks people.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is an expanded commentary on the topic of al-'Aam al-'Aaridi (the accidental general) from the perspective of the functions of the definite article 'alif lam'. It begins by recording a disagreement: Fakhr al-Islam and his followers hold that the lam in such cases indicates the genus (jins), while Arabic grammarians and most usul scholars hold that it indicates universal coverage (istighraq). The author then clarifies that the primary function of the lam is to indicate 'ahd (specific reference), whether external (as when pointing to something specific) or mental (as when the speaker and hearer have a particular instance in mind). Only when 'ahd is impossible or impractical does the lam shift to indicating the genus or universal coverage. The passage delves into a detailed hierarchy: the most preponderant is external 'ahd, then universal coverage, then mental 'ahd, and finally genus. It notes that the author of al-Tawdih prioritized mental 'ahd over universal coverage, which is critiqued by others. The discussion then turns to cases where the lam enters plural nouns. In such cases, the benefit of the lam is that it drops the literal meaning of plurality (minimum three), because if the plural meaning remained, the lam would have no workable function (since 'ahd and istighraq are often impossible with plurals in certain contexts, e.g., swearing not to marry women). So the lam is interpreted as indicating the genus, and the plural form is ignored. Thus, if someone swears 'I will not marry al-nisa' (with lam), he breaks the oath by marrying just one woman. But if he swears 'I will not marry nisa' (without lam), he only breaks the oath after marrying three women, because the plural form alone (without lam) retains its meaning of at least three. The passage then applies this principle to Quranic examples: in 'Inna al-insana lafi khusr' the lam indicates universal coverage, proven by the valid exception; in 'al-sariq wa al-sariqah' the lam functions like a relative pronoun, meaning 'the one who stole'; and in 'innama al-sadaqatu lil-fuqara'i wa al-masakin' the lam indicates the genus, so giving to one poor person suffices. The passage concludes with definitions of faqir and miskin according to Imam Abu Hanifa and al-Zuhri.

Key Terms
العهد (al-‘ahd): Specific reference, either external (known by pointing) or mental (known by prior mention or common knowledge)
الاستغراق (al-istighraq): Universal coverage, where the lam indicates that the ruling applies to every individual of the genus
الجنس (al-jins): The genus or kind, where the lam indicates the essence without considering individuals
العام العارضي (al-‘aam al-‘aaridi): The accidental general: a term that becomes general due to the entry of the lam, not due to its own form

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone swears 'لا أتزوج النساء' (with اللام on النساء), by marrying how many women does he break his oath according to this passage?
A) Three women
B) One woman
C) Two women
D) He never breaks the oath

Key Takeaway
The lam's primary function is 'ahd; it shifts to universal coverage or genus only when 'ahd is impossible, and on plurals it overrides the literal plural meaning.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
6 min
The Definite Article on Plurals: Indicating Genus
Explaining how the definite article makes a plural noun refer to the genus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when the definite article on a plural noun indicates the genus (al-jins) and apply this principle to derive the Hanafi ruling for cases like oaths and zakat distribution.

Core Idea
The definite article on a plural noun negates the plural count—it indicates the genus, so one instance fulfills the requirement.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar introduces a key usul al-fiqh concept: the accidental general (al-'amm al-'aridi). When the definite article (alif lam) attaches to a plural noun, the question arises whether it retains its collective meaning or shifts to something else. The Hanafi position, grounded in the principle of acting on both proofs, argues that the lam indicates the genus, thereby dropping the requirement of three for the plural. This has practical consequences for oaths and the distribution of zakat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the textual phenomenon
Observe that a plural noun (e.g., 'al-nisa', 'al-fuqara'') is preceded by the definite article 'al-'. This is your starting point.
The noun must be a sound or broken plural, not a dual or singular.
2
Recognize the three possible functions of 'al-'
Recall that the lam can indicate covenant (ʿahd), comprehensiveness (istighrāq), or genus (jins). Covenant refers to a previously mentioned group; comprehensiveness covers all individuals; genus refers to the kind in general.
Hanafi usul distinguishes these three; the Shafi'i school may add a fourth (al-mahdha).
3
Eliminate the first two functions contextually
Check if the context supports covenant (e.g., a specific group mentioned earlier) or comprehensiveness (e.g., possible to include all). In the examples given, such as 'la atazawwaju al-nisaa' or 'innama al-sadaqatu lil-fuqara'', both are impossible: covenant is absent, and comprehensiveness is impossible (cannot marry all women or give to all poor). Thus, only genus remains.
This elimination is the core reasoning behind the Hanafi position.
4
Conclude that the lam indicates genus
Since the lam must have a function, and the other two are ruled out, it indicates the genus. This means the plural meaning (requiring at least three) is dropped; the word refers to the kind, and a single individual of that kind fulfills the requirement.
This is the meaning of 'sqt i'tibar al-jam'iyyah'—the consideration of collectivity falls away.
5
Apply to examples: oaths and zakat
If someone swears 'I will not marry women' (with 'al-'), he breaks the oath by marrying one woman, because 'al-nisaa'' means the genus 'women', not a plural. Similarly, giving zakat to one poor person suffices because 'al-fuqara'' indicates the genus of poor people.
Contrast with the Shafi'i position: they retain the plural meaning, requiring at least three.
