(القمر) فيحنث إلخ بخلاف ما إذا حلف لا أتزوج نساء بدون اللام، فيحنث حينئذ بتزوج ثلاث نسوة عملاً بصيغة الجمع، ولا يحنث بتزوج امرأة أو امرأتين. (القمر) لا يحل لك إلخ الخطاب إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أي لا يحل لك النساء أي واحدة من النساء من بعد التسع، فهو في حقه الا الله كالأربع في حقنا كذا قال البيضاوي.(القمر) للفقراء والمساكين الفقير من له أدنى شيء، والمسكين من لا شيء له، وهو المروي عن الإمام الأعظم الله وروي عن الزهري الفقير: الساكن في بيته ولا يسأل الناس والمسكين من يخرج ويسأل الناس.
وعند الشافعي له لابد أن يصرف إلى الفقراء الثلاثة والمساكين الثلاثة عملاً بالجمع، هذا غاية ما قيل في هذا المقام، وفيه تأمل.
Section on General - 227 - The Accidental General. And His saying: 'And the male thief and the female thief, and the female adulterer and the male adulterer' and similar examples. ...until the consideration of collectivity is dropped when it enters upon the plural, acting on both proofs, as a branch on his saying: 'The general is established' – that is, this extent when the entry of the lam is upon the singular. But if it is upon the plural, then the fruit of its generality is that it negates the meaning of the plural, so it does not require a minimum of three; because if it remained plural, no benefit would appear for the lam, because there is no covenant, no comprehensiveness, and no genus. So it must be carried upon the genus, so that less than three is acted upon by the genus, and above it by the plural. This is acting on both proofs. So he breaks the oath by marrying one woman if he swore 'I will not marry women,' and if the meaning of plural remained, he would not break the oath with less than three. And similar is His saying: 'And women are not lawful for you after that,' and His saying: 'Indeed the charities are for the poor and the needy' – so charity suffices for the genus of the poor and the needy. And 'the thief, etc.': He only mentioned this example to indicate that the intended meaning of lam here is more general than the definite article and the relative pronoun, for the meaning of 'the thief' and 'the female thief' is 'the one who stole' and 'the one who stole' (female) – acting on both proofs, i.e., the proof of definition which is the lam, and the proof of the form, and the intended meaning of 'proof' is the indicator, not the technical meaning, as is apparent. This extent: meaning that the entry of lam is beneficial for generality. Because there is no covenant, for the speech is in what does not admit definition by way of covenant. And no comprehensiveness because of lack of benefit – either in his saying 'I will not marry women,' for the oath is for prevention, and marrying all the women of the world is beyond human capacity, so preventing it would be futile; or in His saying 'Indeed the charities are for the poor,' because it is not possible to distribute all charities to all the poor of the world, and similarly. So there is no comprehensiveness here. And no genus because the speech is on the assumption of the persistence of collectivity, and then there is no effect for genus. So it is necessary, etc.: i.e., if the persistence of collectivity necessitates the futility of the lam, then it is necessary to carry the lam upon the genus and drop the consideration of collectivity. So he breaks the oath, etc., unlike if he swore 'I will not marry women' without the lam, then he breaks the oath by marrying three women acting on the plural form, and does not break by marrying one or two women. 'Not lawful for you, etc.': the address to the Prophet (peace be upon him), i.e., no woman is lawful for you after the nine, so for him it is except Allah, like the four for us, as stated by al-Baydawi. 'For the poor and the needy': the poor is one who possesses the least thing, and the needy is one who possesses nothing – this is narrated from the Imam al-A'zam (Abu Hanifa), and from al-Zuhri: the poor is one who stays in his house and does not ask people, and the needy is one who goes out and asks people. And according to al-Shafi'i, he must distribute to three poor and three needy, acting on the plural. This is the utmost that has been said in this place, and in it there is contemplation.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the 'accidental general' (al-'āmm al-'āriḍī). The author explains that when the definite article (alif lām) enters a plural noun, it negates the collective meaning (ma'nā al-jam') so that the plural no longer requires a minimum of three. Instead, the lam is interpreted as indicating the genus (jins). This is based on acting on both proofs: the proof of the lam (which indicates generality) and the proof of the plural form. If the plural meaning persisted, the lam would have no benefit because it cannot indicate covenant (ʿahd), comprehensiveness (istighrāq), or genus (jins) in that context. Therefore, the lam is taken for the genus, and what is less than three is acted upon by the genus, while above three is acted upon by the plural. The Hanafi position is illustrated with examples: if someone swears 'I will not marry women' (with the definite article), he breaks the oath by marrying just one woman, because the lam indicates the genus of women, not the plural. In contrast, if he swears 'I will not marry women' without the definite article (i.e., 'nisā'), he would break the oath only by marrying three women because the plural form requires a minimum of three. Similarly, the Quranic verse 'Indeed the charities are for the poor and the needy' means that giving charity to one poor person or one needy person suffices, because 'the poor' and 'the needy' with the lam indicate the genus. The passage then contrasts the Hanafi view with the Shafi'i view, which holds that the plural retains its collective meaning, so one must give to at least three poor and three needy. The author notes that there is contemplation (ta'ammul) regarding this difference.

Key Terms
اللام (al-lām): The definite article (alif lām) that enters nouns, which in this context indicates the genus (jins) rather than covenant, comprehensiveness, or plural meaning.
الجمعية (al-jam‘iyyah): The collective meaning of a plural noun, which in Arabic requires a minimum of three individuals.
الجنس (al-jins): The genus or class, as opposed to the plural count; when the lam indicates genus, the word refers to the kind itself, not to a specific number.
الاستغراق (al-istighrāq): Comprehensiveness, meaning that the definite article indicates all individuals of the category; rejected here because it is impossible to fulfill in the context.
العام العارضي (al-‘āmm al-‘āriḍī): The accidental general: a word that is not intrinsically general but becomes so due to an external factor, such as the definite article.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man swears 'I will not marry women' (using the definite article 'al-nisā''), how many women must he marry to break his oath according to the Hanafi view?
A) One woman
B) Three women
C) Nine women
D) All women in the world

Key Takeaway
When the definite article enters a plural noun and cannot indicate covenant or comprehensiveness, it indicates the genus, dropping the requirement of three and allowing a single instance to fulfill the obligation.

The Rule of the Indefinite Noun Repeated as Definite
Stating and explaining the usul rule about indefinite nouns repeated as definite

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that determines whether a repeated noun refers to the same or a different entity, and identify its scope and exceptions.

Core Idea
If a noun is repeated as definite, it refers to the same entity; if repeated as indefinite, it refers to a different entity.

This lesson examines a foundational linguistic rule in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the rule of 'an-nakira idha u'idat ma'rifah' (the indefinite noun when repeated as definite). This rule helps us determine when a repeated noun in Quranic or legal texts refers back to the same entity or introduces a different one. Understanding this rule is crucial for accurately deriving rulings from divine texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first and second occurrences
Locate the noun in its first indefinite (or definite) form and then its second occurrence. Note the definiteness status of each.
2
Check the method of definiteness
The rule applies only when definiteness is achieved through the definite article (al-) or construct state (idafa). Proper nouns, relative pronouns, and demonstratives are excluded.
3
Apply the rule
If the second occurrence is definite, it refers to the same entity as the first ('ayn al-ula). If indefinite, it refers to a different entity (ghayr al-ula).
4
Consider exceptions
The rule is akthari (majority) but not absolute. Some contexts may override it, as in the verse 'Inna ma'a al-'usri yusran' where the indefinite 'yusran' appears twice but refers to the same type of ease, not necessarily the same instance. Also, the verse 'wa huwa alladhi fi al-sama'i ilahun' uses 'ilah' twice as indefinite but refers to the same God (an exception noted by some).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(القمر) كانت الثانية غير الأولى كاليسرين في قوله: ﴿فَإِنَّ مَعَ الْعُسْرِ يُسْراً إِنَّ مَعَ الْعُسْرِ يُسْرا (الانشراح: ٦،٥) وهو أكثري، فخرج عنه قوله تعالى: ﴿وَهُوَ الَّذِي فِي السَّمَاءِ إِلَهُ وَفِي الْأَرْضِ إِلَهُ (الزخرف:٨٤) [فتح الغفار ١٣٢] غير الأولى إلخ لأن النكرة يتناول واحدا غير معين، فلو انصرفت الثانية إلى الأولى لتعينت من وجه فلا يكون مطلقة. (السنبلي)
Then, when he mentioned the benefit of indefinite and definite nouns in generalization, he introduced in its approximation an explanation of what occurs of indefinite and definite nouns in one context, even if that is not from the topics of the general. So he said: And when an indefinite noun is repeated as definite, the second is the same as the first. And this cannot be conceived except in definition by the lam or the construct, not by proper nouns and the like. So when it is repeated with the lam, that is a reference to what preceded, so it is the same, like His saying: 'As We sent to Pharaoh a messenger, and Pharaoh disobeyed the messenger.' And when it is repeated as indefinite, the second is different from the first; because if it were the same as the first, it would become specified. There is contemplation: The commentator said in al-Munhiyah: The aspect of contemplation is that the observance of three may be due to its falling under the genus, so nothing is acted upon but the genus. (al-Qamar) 'There is contemplation, etc.' i.e., regarding the author's saying 'acting on both proofs,' or our saying 'so that less than three is acted upon by the genus and above it by the plural.' (al-Sunbulī) 'The second, etc.' i.e., if the first is general, the second is general; if the first is particular, the second is particular; so it is said. (al-Qamar) 'Same as the first': so the consideration is the definiteness or indefiniteness of the second; i.e., if the second is definite, it is the same as the first, whether the first was indefinite or definite; and if the second is indefinite, it is different from the first, whether the first was indefinite or definite. So memorize this. (al-Sunbulī) 'And this cannot be conceived except in, etc.' The author of al-Talwīḥ said: The speech is concerning when the first word is repeated either with its modality of definiteness or indefiniteness or without them; and then the way of definiteness is by the lam or the construct, so that it is valid to repeat the definite as indefinite by dropping the lam or the construct, and vice versa. And some commentators said: There is a discussion in the restriction due to the possibility of it being by way of connection (al-wuṣūl) rather than by knowledge (al-ʿilm). (al-Qamar) 'And the like' i.e., relative pronouns and demonstratives. (al-Qamar) 'To Pharaoh a messenger' i.e., Moses, peace be upon him. Then do not miss that this is an error, and the ordering of the verse is like this: 'As We sent to Pharaoh a messenger' (73:15) the verse. (al-Qamar) 'The second is different from the first' like the two 'ease' in His saying: 'For indeed, with hardship [comes] ease. Indeed, with hardship [comes] ease.' (94:5-6) and this is the majority. So excluded from it is His saying: 'And He is the one who in the heaven is God and on the earth is God.' (43:84) [Fath al-Ghaffār 132] 'Different from the first, etc.' because the indefinite refers to a single unspecified individual; so if the second refers to the first, it would become specified in a way, so it would not be absolute. (al-Sunbulī)
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental usul rule: when an indefinite noun (nakira) is repeated with the definite article (ma'rifah), the second occurrence refers to the same entity as the first; but if it is repeated as indefinite, it refers to a different entity. The rule is illustrated by the Quranic verse about Pharaoh: 'We sent to Pharaoh a messenger (rasūlan), and Pharaoh disobeyed the messenger (ar-rasūla).' The first 'rasūl' is indefinite, the second is definite, so it is the same messenger (Moses). The rule applies specifically to definition by the lam or by idāfa (construct state), not by proper nouns (a'lām) or other definite markers like relative pronouns or demonstratives. The commentary adds important nuances: the definiteness/indefiniteness of the second word determines the identity, regardless of the state of the first. Also, the rule is the majority (aktharī), with exceptions like the verse 'He is the one who in heaven is God and on earth is God' where the same word is repeated with the definite article but refers to the same entity (Allah) even though it is the same? Actually that example is given as an exception: 'ilāh' is indefinite, but the context is different. The commentator (al-Sunbulī) clarifies that the indefinite refers to a single unspecified entity, so if the second referred to the first, it would become specified, contradicting its indefinite nature.

Key Terms
النكرة (an-nakira): An indefinite noun that refers to an unspecified individual or instance of a class.
المعرفة (al-ma'rifa): A definite noun that refers to a specific entity, made definite by the definite article, construct state, proper noun, etc.
عين الأولى ('ayn al-ūlā): The same entity as the first occurrence; identity of reference.
غير الأولى (ghayr al-ūlā): A different entity from the first occurrence; non-identity of reference.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the rule 'an-nakira idhā u'īdat ma'rifah kānat al-thāniyah 'ayn al-ūlā', what is the ruling if the second occurrence is indefinite?
A) It is the same as the first
B) It is different from the first
C) It could be either the same or different
D) The rule does not apply

Key Takeaway
The definiteness or indefiniteness of the second occurrence of a noun determines reference identity, subject to the condition that definiteness is achieved through lam or idāfa.

Repetition of Nakira and Ma'rifa: Same or Different?
Explaining the rules of repetition of indefinite and definite nouns in Quranic context

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for repetition of indefinite/definite nouns to determine whether a repeated Quranic noun refers to the same or different entity and derive the interpretive consequence.

Core Idea
Indefinite to definite is same; indefinite to indefinite is different.

In interpreting the Quran, one often encounters a noun repeated in consecutive verses. The Hanafi school establishes a precise rule to determine whether the second occurrence refers back to the same entity or introduces a new one. This rule is foundational for deriving correct legal and theological meanings from the divine text. We will unpack the rule, see it applied in the Quran, and address a subtle counter-argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first occurrence
Locate the noun in its first occurrence and note whether it is indefinite (nakira) or definite (ma'rifa). In the Quranic example 'rasulan' is indefinite.
2
Identify the second occurrence and its definiteness
Find the same noun in the following verse and determine if it is repeated as definite (with al- or idafa) or indefinite. In the example, it becomes 'al-rasul' (definite).
3
Apply the rule
If the second is definite (by al- or idafa), it is the same entity (ayn al-ula). If indefinite, it is a different entity (ghayr al-ula). Apply to the example: 'al-rasul' is the same messenger (Moses).
4
Consider exceptions and counterarguments
Note that the rule applies only to definition by al- or idafa, not to proper nouns or demonstratives. Also, consider the possibility that the repetition could be emphasis (ta'kid), as suggested by Fakhr al-Islam. However, the Hanafi preference is for original significance (ta'sis) over emphasis.
5
Derive the interpretive consequence
Based on the ruling, determine the meaning: for example, in Surah al-Inshirah, 'al-usr' (hardship) is the same, while 'yusran' (ease) repeated as indefinite indicates two eases, yielding the principle 'hardship cannot overcome two eases.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

العام العارضي
وعند الشافعي له لابد أن يصرف إلى الفقراء الثلاثة والمساكين الثلاثة عملاً بالجمع، هذا غاية ما قيل في هذا المقام، وفيه تأمل. ثم أنه لما ذكر إفادة النكرة والمعرفة التعميم، أورد في تقريبه بيان ما ورد النكرة والمعرفة في مقام واحد وإن لم يكن ذلك من مباحث العام ، فقال : والنكرة إذا أعيدت معرفة كانت الثانية عين الأولى وهذا لا يتصور إلا في التعريف باللام أو الإضافة دون الأعلام ونحوها، فإذا أعيدت باللام كان ذلك إشارة إلى ما سبق، فيكون عينه كقوله تعالى: كَمَا أَرْسَلْنَا إِلَى فِرْعَوْنَ رَسُولاً فَعَصَى فِرْعَوْنُ الرَّسُولَ ، وإذا أعيدت نكرة كانت (المزمل: ١٦،١٥) الثانية غير الأولى؛ لأنها لو كانت عين الأولى لتعينت
وفيه تأمل: قال الشارح في "المنهية": وجه التأمل أن رعاية الثلاثة يجوز أن تكون لأجل دخوله تحت الجنس فلا يكون المعمول إلا الجنس. (القمر) وفيه تأمل إلخ أي في قول المصنف عملاً بالدليلين، أو في قولنا: ليكون ما دون الثلاثة معمولاً للجنس، وما فوقه للجمع. مطلقة. (السنبلي)

العام العارضي
نوع تعين، ولم تبق فيها نكارة والمقدر خلافه والمعرفة إذا أعيدت معرفة كانت الثانية
علي الثانية
عين الأولى؛ لأن اللام يشير إلى معهود مذكور فيما سبق، ومثال هاتين القاعدتين: قوله تعالى: فَإِنَّ مَعَ الْعُسْرِ يُسْراً إِنَّ مَعَ الْعُسْرِ يُسْراً، فإن العسر أعيد معرفًا فيكون عين الأول، (الانشراح : ٦،٥) واليسر أعيد منكرًا فيكون غير الأول، فعلم أن مع كل عسر واحد يسرين، وهو معنى
قول ابن عباس هما مرويًا عن النبي عليه : "لن يغلب عسر يسرين"، وقال الشاعر: شعر إذا اشتدت بك البلوى ففكّر في ألم نشرح
فعسر بین يسرين إذا فكرته فافرح
وقال فخر الإسلام عندي في هذا المقام نظر ؛ لأنه يحتمل أن تكون الجملة الثانية تأكيدًا للأولى كما أن قولنا: إن مع زيد كتابًا إن مع زيد كتابًا لا يدل على أن معه كتابين،
فيكون العسر واحدا واليسر واحدا.
والمقدر خلافه لأنه قدر أنها أعيدت نكرة. (القمر)
هاتين القاعدتين: أي إعادة النكرة نكرة وإعادة المعرفة معرفة. (القمر)
يسرين هما إما يسر الفتوح في زمن الرسول عليه، ويسر الفتوح في أيام الخلفاء، أو يسر الدنيا والآخرة. (القمر) مرويًا إلخ: رواه سعيد بن منصور وعبد الرزاق من حديث مسعود كذا قال القسطلاني، وأخرجه ابن مردويه عن جابر كذا في "التوشيح شرح الصحيح". (القمر)
إذا اشتدت إلخ : قيل: كان رجل مغموماً في البادية فسمع بالليل هاتفًا يقول هذا الشعر. (القمر) وقال فخر الإسلام إلخ قلت هذا القول مبني على العرف لكن حمل الكلام على التأسيس أولى من التأكيد على كل حال. (السنبلي) تأكيدًا للأولى لتقرير الأولى في النفس وتمكينها في القلب. (القمر)
* أخرجه رزين في حديث طويل عنه أنه قال : إن مع العسر يسراً ولن يغلب عسر يسرين، وكتبه عمر إلى أبي عبيدة، أخرجه مالك في الموطأ رقم ٩٦١ ، في كتاب الجهاد، وأخرجه البغوي في تفسيره من غير سند،
وقال ابن مسعود ولو كان العسر في حجر لطلبه اليسر حتى يدخل فيه ذكره المفسرون . [إشراق الأبصار ٩]
Section on the General Term. 228. The Accidental General. According to al-Shafi'i, he [holds that] it is necessary to direct [the distribution] to the three poor and the three needy, acting upon the collective [interpretation]. This is the utmost that has been said in this regard, but it merits consideration. Then, when he mentioned the benefit of the indefinite and definite nouns in indicating generality, he brought up in its explanation a clarification of what occurs of indefinite and definite in a single context, even though that is not from the topics of the general term. He said: The indefinite noun, if it is repeated as definite, the second is the very same as the first. And this is conceivable only with definition by the definite article (al-) or by addition (idafa), not with proper nouns and the like. So if it is repeated with the definite article, that indicates what preceded, so it is the very same, as in His statement: "As We sent to Pharaoh a messenger, then Pharaoh disobeyed the messenger" (73:15-16). And if it is repeated as indefinite, the second is other than the first; because if it were the same as the first, it would have been specified. There is consideration in it: The commentator said in al-Munhiyya: The aspect of consideration is that observing the three [categories] could be because of its inclusion under the genus, so the operative [factor] is only the genus. (al-Qamar) "And in it is consideration" etc., meaning either in the author's statement "acting upon the two proofs", or in our statement: "So that what is less than three is operative for the genus, and what is above it for the collective." (al-Sunbuli) "The second" etc., so if the first is general, the second is general; and if the first is specific, the second is specific. So it is said. (al-Qamar) "The very same as the first": So the criterion is the definiteness or indefiniteness of the second. That is, if the second is definite, it is the same as the first, whether the first is indefinite or definite; and if the second is indefinite, it is other than the first, whether the first is indefinite or definite. So memorize this. (al-Sunbuli) "And this is conceivable only with" etc. The author of al-Talwih said: The discussion concerns when the first word is repeated either with its modality of definition or indefiniteness or without it. In that case, the means of definition is the definite article or idafa to allow the repetition of a definite as indefinite by dropping the definite article or idafa, and vice versa. Some marginal glossators said: There is a discussion about the restriction, because it is possible to be by way of [؟] rather by way of knowledge. (al-Qamar) "And the like" such as relative pronouns and demonstrative pronouns. (al-Qamar) "To Pharaoh a messenger" i.e., Moses, upon our Prophet and him peace. Then do not be unaware that this is a slip; the order of the verse is: "As We sent to Pharaoh a messenger" (73:15). (al-Qamar) "The second is other than the first" like the two cases of ease in His statement: "For indeed, with hardship comes ease. Indeed, with hardship comes ease" (94:5-6). And this is the majority. Excluded from it is His statement: "And He is the One who in the heaven is God and in the earth is God" (43:84). [Fath al-Ghaffar 132] "Other than the first" etc., because the indefinite refers to a non-specific individual; if the second referred to the first, it would have become specific from some aspect and thus would not be absolute. (al-Sunbuli). Section on the General Term. 229. The Accidental General. A type of specification, and no indefiniteness remains in it, and the implied [meaning] is contrary. And the definite noun, if repeated as definite, the second is the very same as the first, because the definite article points to a previously mentioned known referent. An example of these two rules: His statement: "For indeed, with hardship comes ease. Indeed, with hardship comes ease" (94:5-6). For "hardship" is repeated as definite, so it is the same as the first, and "ease" is repeated as indefinite, so it is other than the first. Thus it is known that with every single hardship there are two eases. This is the meaning of the saying of Ibn 'Abbas, narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him): "Hardship will never overcome two eases." And the poet said: "If distress intensifies for you, then reflect on 'Did We not expand?' So hardship between two eases if you think about it, then rejoice." And Fakhr al-Islam said: I have a consideration in this place; because it is possible that the second sentence is an emphasis of the first, just as our statement: "Indeed, with Zayd is a book. Indeed, with Zayd is a book" does not indicate that he has two books. So hardship is one and ease is one. And the implied [meaning] is contrary because he assumed it was repeated as indefinite. (al-Qamar) "These two rules": i.e., repeating an indefinite as indefinite and repeating a definite as definite. (al-Qamar) "Two eases": They are either the ease of conquests in the time of the Messenger (peace be upon him) and the ease of conquests in the days of the Caliphs, or the ease of this world and the Hereafter. (al-Qamar) "Narrated" etc.: Sa'id ibn Mansur and 'Abd al-Razzaq narrated it from the hadith of Mas'ud, as al-Qastalani said, and Ibn Mardawayh narrated it from Jabir, as in al-Tawshih Sharh al-Sahih. (al-Qamar) "If distress" etc.: It is said that a man was distressed in the desert and heard a caller at night reciting this poetry. (al-Qamar) And Fakhr al-Islam said... I say: This statement is based on custom, but preferring the interpretation of original significance over emphasis is always better. (al-Sunbuli) "Emphasis of the first" to establish the first in the soul and strengthen it in the heart. (al-Qamar) * Ruzayn narrated it in a long hadith from him that he said: "Indeed, with hardship comes ease, and hardship will never overcome two eases." And 'Umar wrote it to Abu 'Ubayda. Malik narrated it in al-Muwatta', no. 961, in the Book of Jihad, and al-Baghawi narrated it in his Tafsir without a chain. And Ibn Mas'ud said: Even if hardship were in a rock, ease would seek it until it enters it. The commentators mentioned it. [Ishraq al-Absar 9]
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul al-fiqh discussion on the rules governing the repetition of nouns in terms of their definiteness or indefiniteness, and the implications for the general (al-amm) and specific (al-khass). The author begins by noting a point of disagreement with al-Shafi'i regarding the distribution of charity to three poor and three needy persons, but then moves to the main topic: when a noun is repeated, whether it refers to the same entity or a different one. The key rule is: if a noun is first mentioned as indefinite (nakira) and then repeated as definite (ma'rifa) using the definite article (al-) or idafa, the second occurrence refers to the very same entity as the first. Conversely, if it is repeated as indefinite, it refers to a different entity. The author provides Quranic examples: in Surah al-Muzammil (73:15-16), 'rasulan' (a messenger) is repeated as 'al-rasul' (the messenger), indicating the same messenger (Moses). In Surah al-Inshirah (94:5-6), 'yusran' (ease) is repeated as indefinite, so there are two different eases, while 'al-usr' (hardship) is repeated as definite, so it is the same hardship. This leads to the celebrated principle that one hardship cannot overcome two eases. The passage includes commentary from later scholars (al-Sunbuli, al-Qamar) who refine the rule, discussing cases where the second noun might be an emphasis (ta'kid) rather than indicating a separate entity. Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi suggests that the second occurrence of 'ease' could be merely an emphasis, but the preferred view (and the one indicated by the majority) is that it indicates a different entity (ta'sis) because the original significance is preferred over emphasis. The passage also clarifies that these rules apply only to definition by al- or idafa, not to proper nouns or demonstratives. The overall aim is to equip the student with the tools to correctly interpret Quranic repetition and derive legal rulings accordingly.

Key Terms
النكرة (an-nakira): A noun that does not designate a specific individual; it is indefinite.
المعرفة (al-ma'rifa): A definite noun that refers to a specific entity, often with the definite article (al-) or idafa.
عين الأولى ('ayn al-ula): The second occurrence refers to the exact same entity as the first.
غير الأولى (ghayr al-ula): The second occurrence refers to a different entity from the first.
التأسيس (at-ta'sis): The principle of giving a new meaning (original significance) rather than mere emphasis.
التأكيد (at-ta'kid): Emphasis, repeating a word to reinforce rather than introduce new information.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the rule discussed, when a noun is first mentioned as indefinite and then repeated as definite with the definite article (al-), what does the second occurrence indicate?
A) A different entity than the first.
B) The very same entity as the first.
C) It could be either the same or different depending on context.
D) It is always an emphasis of the first.

Key Takeaway
The definiteness or indefiniteness of a repeated noun in the Quran determines whether it refers to the same or a different entity, a key tool for correct interpretation.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
12 min
Rule of Repeating Definite and Indefinite Nouns
Explaining the usul rule for repeated nouns and its legal implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on noun repetition to distinguish ta'sis from tawkid and determine legal consequences in textual interpretation.

Core Idea
Same definiteness in repetition = same entity; different definiteness = different entity.

This lesson examines a foundational Hanafi usul rule: when a noun is repeated, its definiteness determines whether the second occurrence refers to the same or a different entity. This principle has profound implications for interpreting Qur'anic verses and legal declarations (iqrar). We will explore the rule through the famous example of Surah al-Inshirah and address the scholarly debate between ta'sis (new meaning) and tawkid (emphasis).

Guided Path
1
Identify the nouns in the repeated expression
Locate the noun(s) that appear more than once in the text. Note each occurrence and its form.
For example, in 'al-usr yusran' repeated, we have 'al-usr' (definite) and 'yusr' (indefinite).
2
Determine definiteness of each occurrence
Check if the noun has the definite article 'al-' or is indefinite (tanwin or without 'al-').
Al-usr has 'al-', so definite; yusr does not, so indefinite.
3
Apply the rule
If both occurrences have the same definiteness (both definite or both indefinite), the second refers to the same entity. If definiteness differs, the second refers to a different entity.
Thus, al-usr repeated definite = same hardship; yusr repeated indefinite = new ease.
4
Consider exceptions and context
Context can override the rule, as seen in examples where an indefinite is repeated as definite with a different referent (e.g., 'kitab' in Quran 6:155-156).
The rule applies 'when there is no context' (عند الإطلاق).
5
Analyze the dispute: ta'sis vs tawkid
Fakhr al-Islam suggests the repetition could be tawkid (emphasis) rather than ta'sis (new meaning). Evaluate the Hanafi preference for ta'sis based on the hadith 'lā yaghlibu 'usrun yusrayn'.
The Hanafi position is that ta'sis is always preferred over tawkid.

العام العارضي
نوع تعين، ولم تبق فيها نكارة والمقدر خلافه والمعرفة إذا أعيدت معرفة كانت الثانية عين الأولى؛ لأن اللام يشير إلى معهود مذكور فيما سبق، ومثال هاتين القاعدتين: قوله تعالى: فَإِنَّ مَعَ الْعُسْرِ يُسْراً إِنَّ مَعَ الْعُسْرِ يُسْراً، فإن العسر أعيد معرفًا فيكون عين الأول، واليسر أعيد منكرًا فيكون غير الأول، فعلم أن مع كل عسر واحد يسرين، وهو معنى قول ابن عباس مرويًا عن النبي عليه : "لن يغلب عسر يسرين"، وقال الشاعر: إذا اشتدت بك البلوى ففكّر في ألم نشرح فَعُسْر بين يسرين إذا فكرته فافرح
وقال فخر الإسلام عندي في هذا المقام نظر ؛ لأنه يحتمل أن تكون الجملة الثانية تأكيدًا للأولى كما أن قولنا: إن مع زيد كتابًا إن مع زيد كتابًا لا يدل على أن معه كتابين، فيكون العسر واحدا واليسر واحدا.
والمقدر خلافه لأنه قدر أنها أعيدت نكرة.
هاتين القاعدتين: أي إعادة النكرة نكرة وإعادة المعرفة معرفة.
يسرين هما إما يسر الفتوح في زمن الرسول عليه، ويسر الفتوح في أيام الخلفاء، أو يسر الدنيا والآخرة.
مرويًا إلخ: رواه سعيد بن منصور وعبد الرزاق من حديث مسعود كذا قال القسطلاني، وأخرجه ابن مردويه عن جابر كذا في "التوشيح شرح الصحيح". 
إذا اشتدت إلخ : قيل: كان رجل مغموماً في البادية فسمع بالليل هاتفًا يقول هذا الشعر. 
وقال فخر الإسلام إلخ قلت هذا القول مبني على العرف لكن حمل الكلام على التأسيس أولى من التأكيد على كل حال. (السنبلي) تأكيدًا للأولى لتقرير الأولى في النفس وتمكينها في القلب.
* أخرجه رزين في حديث طويل عنه أنه قال : إن مع العسر يسراً ولن يغلب عسر يسرين، وكتبه عمر إلى أبي عبيدة، أخرجه مالك في الموطأ رقم ٩٦١ ، في كتاب الجهاد، وأخرجه البغوي في تفسيره من غير سند، وقال ابن مسعود ولو كان العسر في حجر لطلبه اليسر حتى يدخل فيه ذكره المفسرون.
وإذا أعيدت نكرة كانت الثانية غير الأولى؛ لأنها لو كانت عين الأولى لتعينت بلا إشارة حرف يدل عليه، وهو باطل ولم يوجد لهذا مثال في النص، وقد جعلوا في مثاله: ما إذا أقر بألف مقيد بصك بحضرة شاهدين في مجلس ثم بألف غير مقيد بصك بحضرة شاهدين آخرين في مجلس آخر يكون الثاني غير الأول، ويلزمه ألفان، وينبغي أن يعلم أن هذا كله عند الإطلاق، وخلو المقام عن القرائن وإلا فقد تعاد النكرة معرفة مع المغايرة كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَهَذَا كِتَابٌ أَنْزَلْنَاهُ مُبَارَكٌ فَاتَّبِعُوهُ وَاتَّقُوا لَعَلَّكُمْ تُرْحَمُونَ أَنْ تَقُولُوا إِنَّمَا أُنْزِلَ الْكِتَابُ عَلَى طَائِفَتَيْن مِنْ قَبْلِنَا﴾ فالكتاب الأول القرآن والثاني التوراة والإنجيل، وقد تعاد النكرة نكرة مع عدم المغايرة كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَهُوَ الَّذِي فِي السَّمَاءِ إِلَهُ وَفِي الْأَرْضِ إِلَهُ﴾،
كانت الثانية إلخ قيل: إن المعرفة تستغرق الجنس والنكرة تتناول البعض فالثانية داخلة في الأولى لدخول الجزء في الكل، وفيه أن التعريف لا يلزم أن يكون للاستغراق بل جاز أن يكون للعهد، فحينئذ يكون المعرفة للمعهود، والثانية نكرة تكون غير المعهود لتعينت إلخ فيه أنه إذا صرفت الثانية إلى غير الأولى تعينت أنه غير الأول بلا إشارة حرف يدل عليه، فالأولى أن تكون الثانية مطلقة محتملة، لأن تكون أيضا نوع تعين وهو عين الأولى وغيرها وهو أي التعين بلا إشارة حرف يدل على التعيين. ولم يوجد لهذا إلخ: هذا مشعر بعدم تتبع الشارح له، وإلا فالأمثلة لإعادة المعرفة نكرة مع مغايرة الثاني للأول موجودة في النص، قال الله تعالى: اهْبِطُوا بَعْضُكُمْ لِبَعْضٍ عَدُوٌّ (البقرة: ٣٦)
بألف مقيد بصك إلخ : قال شيخ الإسلام: إن المتبادر منه أن تقييد الألف المقربة بالصك يوجب كونه معرفة وليس كذلك، فإن هذا ممكن مع التنكير أيضا كان يقر بألف مكتوب في هذا الصك. وأجيب بأن هذا ليس مثالاً حقيقيًا بل على سبيل التشبيه فلا ضير ورأيت في نسخة مكتوبة بيد الشارح بألف بصك مقيد إلخ، والمآل واحد. شاهدين آخرين في مجلس آخر إلخ إنما قال آخرين؛ لأنه لو كان الإقرار الثاني في مجلس آخر لكن بحضور الشاهدين الأولين يكون الإقرار الثاني بحضور الشاهدين الأولين تأكيدًا للأول، فلا يلزم الألفان، وإنما قال في مجلس آخر؛ لأن الإقرار الثاني لو كان في مجلس واحد ولو بحضور الشاهدين الآخرين يكون الإقرار الثاني تأكيدا للأولى، فلا يلزم الألفان بل ألف واحد (السنبلي) آخرين: ليس هذا القيد في أكثر الكتب. في مجلس آخر إشارة إلى أنه عند اتحاد المجلس ينبغي أن يلزمه ألف؛ لأن للمجلس تأثيراً في جمع المتفرقة وجعلها في حكم كلمة واحدة. أن تقولوا :إلخ أي كراهية أن تقولوا.
Topic of the General. The Accidental General. A type becomes specified, and there remains no obscurity in it, and the opposite is assumed. And when a definite noun is repeated as definite, the second is the same as the first because the 'lam' refers to something previously mentioned. Example of these two rules: His statement, the Exalted: 'For indeed, with hardship [there is] ease; indeed, with hardship [there is] ease.' So 'al-usr' is repeated as definite and thus is the same as the first, and 'yusr' is repeated as indefinite and thus is different from the first. So it is known that with every one hardship there are two eases. This is the meaning of Ibn 'Abbas's statement, narrated from the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'A hardship will never overcome two eases.' And the poet said: 'When your affliction intensifies, then reflect on "Did We not expand"? For a hardship between two eases, when you reflect on it, rejoice.' Fakhr al-Islam said: I have a consideration at this point because it is possible that the second sentence is an emphasis (tawkid) of the first, just as when we say: 'Indeed with Zayd is a book; indeed with Zayd is a book' does not indicate that he has two books, so the hardship is one and the ease is one. And the opposite is assumed because he assumed that it was repeated as indefinite. These two rules: i.e., repeating an indefinite as indefinite and repeating a definite as definite. The two eases are either the ease of conquests in the time of the Prophet and the ease of conquests in the days of the Caliphs, or the ease of this world and the Hereafter. Narrated etc.: Sa'id ibn Mansur and 'Abd al-Razzaq narrated it from the hadith of Mas'ud; al-Qastallani said so, and Ibn Mardawayh narrated it from Jabir; this is in 'al-Tawshih Sharh al-Sahih'. When it intensifies etc.: It is said that a man was distressed in the desert and heard a caller reciting this poetry at night. And Fakhr al-Islam said etc.; I say: this statement is based on custom, but to interpret the speech as establishing a new meaning (ta'sis) is more appropriate than emphasizing (tawkid) in all cases (al-Sanbali). Emphasis of the first to establish the first in the mind and make it firm in the heart. *Razin narrated in a long hadith that he said: 'Indeed with hardship is ease, and a hardship will never overcome two eases.' 'Umar wrote it to Abu 'Ubayda. Malik narrated it in al-Muwatta' no. 961 in the book of Jihad, and al-Baghawi narrated it in his Tafsir without a chain. Ibn Mas'ud said: 'If hardship were in a rock, ease would seek it until it enters it.' The commentators mentioned it. And when an indefinite noun is repeated, the second is different from the first because if it were the same as the first, it would be specified without a sign of a letter indicating it, which is false. And no example of this exists in the text. They have made as its example: if someone acknowledges a thousand restricted by a document in the presence of two witnesses in a session, then acknowledges a thousand unrestricted by a document in the presence of two other witnesses in another session, then the second is different from the first, and two thousand are incumbent upon him. It should be known that all this is in the case of absolute statements and the absence of contextual indications; otherwise, sometimes an indefinite is repeated as definite with difference, as in His statement: 'And this is a Book which We have sent down, blessed, so follow it and fear Allah that you may receive mercy, lest you say, "The Book was only sent down to two sects before us."' So the first 'book' is the Quran and the second is the Torah and Gospel. And sometimes an indefinite is repeated as indefinite without difference, as in His statement: 'And He it is Who in the heaven is God, and in the earth is God.' The second is etc.: It is said that the definite encompasses the genus and the indefinite covers a part, so the second is included in the first because the part enters into the whole. But there is a consideration: definiteness is not necessarily for generality (istighraq) but is allowed to be for prior mention ('ahd). Then the definite is for what is previously mentioned, and the second indefinite is different from what is previously mentioned. It would be specified etc.: There is that if the second is directed to something other than the first, it becomes specified as other than the first without a sign of a letter indicating it. So it is more appropriate that the second is absolute and possible, because it could also be a type of specification: it is the same as the first or different. And that (i.e., specification without a letter indicating specification) is what is meant. And no example of this exists etc.: This suggests that the commentator has not followed it, otherwise examples of repeating a definite as indefinite with the second being different from the first exist in the text: Allah said: 'Descend, [some of you] enemies to another.' (al-Baqarah:36) With a thousand restricted by a document etc.: Shaykh al-Islam said: The obvious understanding is that restricting the thousand mentioned with a document makes it definite, but it is not so, because this is possible with indefiniteness as well, e.g., he acknowledges a thousand written in this document. It was answered: This is not a real example but rather by way of analogy, so no harm. And I saw in a copy written by the hand of the commentator: 'with a thousand with a document restricted...' and the outcome is the same. Two other witnesses in another session etc.: He said 'others' because if the second acknowledgment is in another session but in the presence of the first two witnesses, the second acknowledgment in the presence of the first two witnesses is an emphasis of the first, so two thousand are not obligatory. He said 'in another session' because if the second acknowledgment is in one session, even with other witnesses, the second acknowledgment is an emphasis of the first, so one thousand is obligated, not two thousand (al-Sanbali). 'Others': This condition is not in most books. 'In another session' indicates that when the session is unified, one thousand should be obligated because the session has an effect in gathering separate things and making them in the ruling of one word. 'Lest you say' etc.: i.e., out of dislike that you say.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary explains a fundamental rule regarding the repetition of nouns and its legal implications. The rule is: when a noun is repeated with the same definiteness (both definite or both indefinite), the second refers to the same entity as the first; when definiteness differs, the second refers to a different entity. The author provides the Qur'anic example from Surah al-Inshirah (94:5-6): 'For indeed, with hardship [there is] ease; indeed, with hardship [there is] ease.' Here, 'al-usr' (the hardship) is repeated as definite, so it is the same hardship; 'yusr' (ease) is repeated as indefinite, so it is a different ease, implying two eases. This is supported by a hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'A hardship will never overcome two eases.' However, Fakhr al-Islam (a Hanafi scholar) raises a valid objection: the repetition could be for emphasis (tawkid) rather than establishing a second ease, similar to saying 'Indeed Zayd has a book; indeed Zayd has a book' which does not mean two books. The commentator resolves this by noting that foundational (ta'sis) interpretation is preferred over emphasis. The passage then discusses the variant cases: when an indefinite is repeated as indefinite, the second is different; when definite is repeated as definite, the second is the same. A fiqh example illustrates: if a person acknowledges (iqrar) a debt of one thousand dirhams restricted by a document in the presence of two witnesses in one session, then later acknowledges another thousand without a document in another session with different witnesses, two separate acknowledgments are valid and two thousand must be paid. If the session or witnesses are the same, it is considered emphasis and only one thousand is owed. This shows how the rule applies to legal declarations. The passage also notes exceptions where context overrides: in Surah al-An'am (6:155-156), 'kitab' (book) is repeated as definite but refers to different books (Quran vs. Torah/Gospel). Similarly, in Surah al-Zukhruf (43:84), 'ilah' (God) is repeated as indefinite but refers to the same God. The commentary also addresses an objection regarding the use of 'document' as a marker of definiteness, clarifying that it is a metaphorical example.

Key Terms
العام العارضي (al-'āmm al-'āriḍī): A general term that becomes specified by being repeated in a definite form, losing its obscurity.
إعادة النكرة نكرة (i'ādat al-nakira nakira): Repeating an indefinite noun with the same indefinite form, indicating a different entity.
تأسيس (ta'sīs): Interpreting a second occurrence as establishing a new meaning rather than emphasizing the first.
تأكيد (tawkīd): Emphasis; interpreting repetition as reinforcing the first occurrence without adding a new entity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rule, if a definite noun is repeated as definite, the second occurrence refers to:
A) The same entity
B) A different entity
C) Either depending on context
D) The same entity only if the context is absent

Key Takeaway
The definiteness of a repeated noun determines whether it refers to the same or a new entity, with ta'sis (new meaning) being the default over tawkid (emphasis) in Hanafi usul.

The Furthest Extent of Specification of General Terms
Explains the maximum number of individuals to which a general term can be specified

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two types of general terms regarding their specification limit, apply the Hanafi rule that indefinite plurals specify to three, and evaluate the Shafi'i/Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
The minimum of a plural is three by linguistic consensus; the hadith about two is restricted to inheritance.

This lesson examines a key rule in Hanafi usul: the furthest number of individuals to which a general term can be specified. The author distinguishes terms that can specify to one from those that must retain at least three. Understanding this rule is essential for correctly interpreting general texts in the Quran and Sunnah, especially when disagreement arises about the minimum for a plural.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Types
Read the passage and distinguish between the first type (singular-form expressions) and the second type (indefinite plurals). Note the examples given for each.
First type includes 'man', 'ma', 'ta'ifah', and definite singulars with al-; second type includes 'rijal', 'nisa', 'qawm', 'raht'.
2
Extract the Rule for Each Type
For the first type, specification can go down to one individual. For the second type, specification stops at three. Explain why this limit is set by referring to linguistic consensus.
If a singular term is specified to zero, it loses meaning; if a plural is specified to less than three, it violates the linguistic definition of plural.
3
Examine the Dispute
Some Shafi'i and Maliki scholars argue that the minimum plural is two, citing the hadith 'Two and above are a group'. Identify their position and their evidence.
The hadith is 'al-ithnani fama fawqahuma jama'ah'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi school responds that this hadith is contextually restricted to inheritance rulings. Explain why this interpretation is adopted and how it protects the linguistic consensus.
In inheritance, two individuals (e.g., two daughters) receive the same share as a group, so the hadith applies only there.
5
Apply the Rule to a New Example
Consider a general Quranic verse that uses an indefinite plural, e.g., 'Wa min al-nasi man yushriku' (Some people associate). According to the Hanafi rule, to how many can this be specified?
At least three individuals must remain after specification.

مبحث العام
بيان أقصى ما ينتهي إليه التخصيص في العام
ثم بعد ذلك ذكر المصنف الله أقصى ما ينتهي إليه التخصيص في العام، وكان ينبغي أن يذكره في مباحث التخصيص لكن لما كان موقوفًا على بيان ألفاظه أخره عنها.
وما ينتهى إليه الخصوص نوعان أي المقدار الذي لا يتعدي إلى ما تحته نوعان. النوع الأول: الواحد فيما هو فرد بصيغته كـ"من" و"ما" والطائفة، واسم الجنس المعرف باللام أو ملحق به كالجموع المعرفة بلام الجنس، فإنهما لو خليا عن الواحد أيضا لفات اللفظ عن مدلوله.
النوع الثاني الثلاثة فما كان جمعًا صيغة ومعنى كرجال ونساء منكرًا مما لم يدخله لام الجنس ويلحق به ما كان معنى فقط كقوم ورهط، وإنما ينتهي تخصيص هؤلاء كلها إلى الثلاثة؛ لأن أدنى الجمع الثلاثة بإجماع أهل اللغة فلو لم يبق تحته ثلاثة أفراد لفات اللفظ عن مقصوده. وقال بعض أصحاب الشافعي ومالك : إن أقل الجمع اثنان، فينتهي التخصيص إليه تمسكًا بقوله عليه: "الاثنان فما فوقهما جماعة"، فأجاب عنه المصنف حله بقوله: وقوله عليه: "الاثنان فما فوقهما جماعة محمول على المواريث والوصايا، فإن في باب الميراث للاثنين حكم الجماعة استحقاقا وحجبًا، فإن للبنتين والأختين الثلثين كما للبنات والأخوات، أي من مال الميت
Section on General Terms
Explanation of the furthest extent to which specification of the general term reaches
Then after that, the author (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned the furthest extent to which specification of the general term reaches, and he should have mentioned it in the topics of specification, but since it depends on the explanation of its wording, he delayed it after them.
And what the specification reaches is of two types, meaning the amount that does not go beyond what is under it is of two types. The first type: one, in what is a singular in its form, like 'man' and 'ma' and 'ta'ifah', and the noun of species defined by al- or what is annexed to it, like the plurals defined by the al- of species, for these two, if they were also devoid of the one, the wording would miss its meaning.
The second type: three, and that is when it is a plural in form and meaning, like 'rijal' and 'nisa' as indefinite, which have not been entered by the al- of species, and what is annexed to it, like 'qawm' and 'raht', is only a plural in meaning. And the specification of all these ends at three, because the minimum of the plural is three by consensus of the linguists; if there did not remain under it three individuals, the wording would miss its intended meaning. And some of the followers of al-Shafi'i and Malik said: the minimum of the plural is two, so specification ends at it, clinging to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Two and above are a group.' So the author answered it with his saying: His saying (peace be upon him): 'Two and above are a group' is carried on inheritances and bequests, for in the chapter of inheritance, two have the ruling of a group in entitlement and blocking, for the two daughters and two sisters get two-thirds, just as daughters and sisters, i.e., from the property of the deceased.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage from the section on general terms (mabhas al-amm) explains the furthest extent to which a general term (amm) can be specified (takhsis). The author, likely Mulla Jeevan or another Hanafi commentator, notes that this topic was delayed because it depends on prior knowledge of wording. He then states that the end point of specification is of two types.

The first type covers expressions that are singular in form, such as 'man' (whoever), 'ma' (whatever), and 'ta'ifah' (a group, but often interpreted as singular by some). Also included are definite singular nouns with al- and plurals that have been made definite with the lam of species (e.g., 'al-rijal' meaning men in general). In all these, specification can reduce the general term down to a single individual. For example, 'al-insan' (mankind) can be specified to one person, as in the Quranic verse 'Indeed, mankind has been created…' but then the context may specify a particular person. The reason is that if these terms are not allowed to specify to one, the wording would lose its meaning when the intended referent is actually one.

The second type involves indefinite plural words that are plural in both form and meaning, like 'rijal' (men) and 'nisa' (women), as well as words that are plural only in meaning like 'qawm' (people) and 'raht' (group). For these, the furthest extent of specification is three individuals, because by the consensus of linguists (ahl al-lughah), the minimum for a plural is three. If the general term is specified to fewer than three, it would contradict its linguistic meaning.

The passage then addresses a disagreement with some Shafi'i and Maliki scholars who argue that the minimum plural is two, citing the hadith: "Two and above are a group" (al-ithnani fama fawqahuma jama'ah). The Hanafi response is that this hadith is specific to the context of inheritance and bequests (mawarith wa wasaya), where two individuals indeed have the same ruling as a group in terms of entitlement and blocking (e.g., two daughters receive two-thirds like three or more daughters). It does not establish a linguistic rule that the plural starts at two. Thus, for general terms in other contexts, the Hanafi position stands: indefinite plurals can only be specified to three.

Key Terms
العام (al-amm): A general term that applies to all individuals of its category
التخصيص (al-takhsis): The act of restricting a general term to some of its individuals
أقل الجمع (adna al-jam'): The minimum number of individuals that a plural word can denote

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, to how many individuals can an indefinite plural general term (like 'rijal') be specified?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) No limit

Key Takeaway
The limit of specification for indefinite plurals is three, based on the linguistic consensus that the minimum plural is three.

Takhsis to Two: Usul Applications in Inheritance, Bequest, and Prayer
Demonstrating the rule of takhsis to two via three examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of takhsis of a general term to two by identifying its operation in inheritance, bequest, and congregational prayer rulings.

Core Idea
A general plural in Hanafi law can be specified to mean just two, as seen in inheritance, bequests, and the imam's position.

This passage from Nur al-Anwar demonstrates how the general term in Arabic can be specified (takhsis) to the minimum number of two in various legal contexts. The author presents three concrete examples – uterine brothers blocking inheritance, bequests to a group, and the imam's position in congregational prayer – all showing that when the text uses a plural, it can be interpreted as applying to two persons. This is a key usul principle in Hanafi jurisprudence, based on the understanding that the plural in Arabic can be used for two and above. The passage also highlights a disagreement with Abu Yusuf on the positioning of the imam, illustrating how the principle is applied in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general term in each example
The key terms are 'al-ikhwan' (the brothers), 'mawali' (clients), and 'al-muqtada' (followers). All are plural. Identify the specific legal context: inheritance for uterine brothers, bequest for clients, and prayer for followers.
The general term is 'amm' and its specification (takhsis) is at issue.
2
Understand the base ruling for three or more
For three uterine brothers, they take one-third of inheritance. For bequests, if there are three or more clients, they share. For prayer with three followers, the imam stands ahead. This is the general rule from which specification will be made.
This establishes the original hukm for the plural as three or more.
3
Apply the takhsis to two
For two uterine brothers, they still block others from a share, just like three. For bequest, if there are two clients, they receive the entire bequest. For prayer with two followers, the imam stands ahead because he is counted as one of the congregation, making three. Thus the plural is specified to two.
The illa (effective cause) in the prayer case is that the imam is part of the congregation, making the total three.
4
Note the exception for Jumu'ah
The general principle (imam counting) does not apply to Jumu'ah because the imam is a condition for the validity of Jumu'ah and thus cannot be counted among the required three. The Quranic verse 'So proceed to the remembrance of Allah' implies at least three listeners besides the imam.
This is an exception based on specific dalil, not analogy.
5
Contrast with Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf holds that with two followers, the imam stands between them rather than ahead. This shows that even within the Hanafi school, the application of the takhsis principle can differ.
The relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that of Abu Hanifa.

Source Text

٢٣٣
بيان أقصى ما ينتهي إليه التخصيص في العام
ويحجب الإخوان للأم من الثلاث إلى السدس كالإخوة الثلاثة، والوصية أخت الميراث في كونها استخلافا بعد الموت وتتبع الميراث تبعية النفل للفرض، فإن أوصى لموالي فلان وله مولان أو لإخوة زيد وله أخوان يستحقان الكل.
أو على سنة تقدم الإمام إذا كان المقتدي اثنين يتقدمهما الإمام كما يتقدم على الثلاثة خلافًا لأبي يوسف الله، فإنه عنده يتوسطهما؛ وذلك لأن الإمام محسوب في الجماعة
الإمام
أي تقدم الإمام
كلها إلا في الجمعة، فإن فيها تشترط ثلاثة رجال سوى الإمام خلافا لأبي يوسف له ؛ إذ عنده يكفي اثنان سوى الإمام، ولم يذكر المصنف ليه الجواب الثالث الذي ذكره أنه محمول على المسافرة بعد قوة الإسلام، فإنه علي نهى أولا عن مسافرة
غيره، وهو الواحد والاثنين؛ لضعف الإسلام وغلبة الكفار،
استخلافًا إلخ : فإن كل واحد من الوارث والموصى له خليفة الميت.(القمر) وتتبع أي الوصية الميراث فإن الإرث ثابت قطعا بلا اختيار والوصية نافلة اختيارية، فتكون الوصية تبعًا للميراث كتبعية النوافل للفرائض، فلما حمل الجمع على الاثنين في المتبوع يحمل عليه في التابع، وقد غلط من قال : إن المعنى أنه يتبع الميراث الوصية كتبعية النفل للفرض؛ لأن الوصية مقدمة على الميراث. (القمر) وتتبع الميراث إلخ: أي بالإجماع؛ لأن الإرث فرض والوصية نافلة وكلاهما بعد الموت، فكان الوصية تبعاً للميراث كما أن النفل تبع للفرض (السنبلي) اثنين ولو كان واحدا يقوم إلى يمين الإمام قيل: إنه إذا كان المقتدي اثنين لا يأمرهما الإمام بالتأخر بل يتقدم بنفسه، وإذا كان واحدًا يأمره الإمام بأن يقوم عن يمين الإمام. (القمر) وذلك : تقدم الإمام إذا كان المقتدي اثنين. (القمر) الإمام أي إذا كان المقتدي اثنين. (المحشي) محسوب إلخ فإذا كان المقتدي اثنين والإمام محسوب في الجماعة، فيتحقق الثلاثة فكملت الجماعة، فيثبت حكمها، وهو تقدم الإمام، فيتقدمهما الإمام كما يتقدم إذا كان المقتدي ثلاثة (القمر) إلا في الجمعة فإن الإمام شرط لصحة أداء، الجمعة فلا يمكن أن يجعل من جملة الجماعة، بخلاف سائر الصلوات، فإن الإمام ليس بشرط لصحة أدائها فيمكن أن يجعل فيها من جملة الجماعة، وقال ابن الملك: شرطنا لصحة أداء الجمعة ثلاثة سوى الإمام بدليل قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاسَعَوْا إِلَى ذِكْرِ الله (الجمعة: ٩) فلابد من الذاكر وهو الخطيب، وثلاثة سواه بقوله تعالى: فَاسَعَوْا (الجمعة: 9). (القمر)
Section on the General Term. Statement of the furthest extent to which specification of a general term can reach. And uterine brothers exclude [their siblings] from one-third to one-sixth like three brothers. And the bequest is the sister of inheritance in being a deputyship after death and follows inheritance as supererogatory follows obligatory. So if one bequeaths to the clients of so-and-so and he has two clients, or to the brothers of Zayd and he has two brothers, they deserve all. Or according to the sunna: the imam, when the followers are two, advances ahead of them as he advances ahead of three, contrary to Abu Yusuf, for with him he stands between them. That is because the imam is counted in the congregation. All [prayers] except Jumu'ah, for it requires three men besides the imam, contrary to Abu Yusuf, for with him two besides the imam suffice. [Marginalia: explanation of deputyship, that bequest follows inheritance, etc.]
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the extent of specification of general terms, providing concrete applications from inheritance and congregational prayer. The first application: the term 'ikhwan' (brothers) in inheritance law. Uterine brothers (from the same mother) when there are three or more share one-third equally; but when there are two, they also get one-third? Actually the text says 'two brothers from the mother exclude from the third to the sixth' meaning that two uterine brothers inherit one-sixth each? The marginal notes clarify that two are treated like three in terms of blocking others from some shares. More clearly, the point is that the word 'ikhwah' (brothers) in the Qur'anic inheritance verses is interpreted to include two when specifying shares. The second application: bequest (wasiyya). If someone makes a bequest 'to the clients of so-and-so' and he has two clients, or 'to the brothers of Zayd' and he has two brothers, they receive the entire bequest. This shows that the general term 'clients' or 'brothers' can be specified to two in the context of bequests, analogous to inheritance. The third and most detailed application: the prayer of the congregation (jama'ah). The imam's position when there are two followers: Abu Hanifa says the imam stands ahead of them, just as when there are three or more. Abu Yusuf disagrees, saying the imam stands between the two followers. The Hanafi reasoning is that the imam himself is counted as part of the congregation; with the two followers, the total becomes three, which is the minimum for the rulings of jama'ah (like the imam advancing ahead). An exception is made for Jumu'ah prayer, where the imam is not counted among the three required for the validity of Jumu'ah. Thus three men besides the imam are necessary, based on the verse 'so proceed to the remembrance of Allah' (al-Jumu'ah 9), which implies at least three listeners (the addressees) besides the speaker. This shows that the general rule about plural being two in certain contexts is applied consistently in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
الحجب (al-hajb): Exclusion of some heirs from inheritance due to the presence of others
الوصية (al-wasiyya): A bequest made by the deceased for a portion of his wealth
الإمامة (al-imama): Leading the congregational prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Between them
C) Behind them
D) At the side of the front row

Key Takeaway
General terms in legal texts can be specified to a minimum of two in Hanafi usul, as demonstrated in inheritance, bequests, and congregational prayer rulings.

The Maximum Extent of Takhsis: Imam's Position with Two Followers
Textual analysis of takhsis using a fiqh example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that al-'amm is binding in its generality unless specified, and evaluate the takhsis argument regarding the imam's position with two followers.

Core Idea
The imam is counted in the congregation; thus, two followers plus the imam constitute a valid congregation of three, justifying the imam's advance.

This passage demonstrates how a general ruling can be specified (takhsis) using a hadith. The ruling on the imam's position in congregational prayer with two followers is derived from the hadith about riders, showing that the minimum for a group is three, and the imam is included in the count. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that al-'amm is qat'i until specified, but specification must be based on a valid dalil.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling and the specification
First, recognize the general ruling that a congregation requires at least three people. The passage specifies that the imam is counted, so two followers plus the imam satisfy three.
The general concept is 'jama'ah' (congregation) and its minimum number.
2
Examine the hadith proof
Analyze the hadith: 'الراكب شيطان، والراكبان شيطانان، والثلاثة ركب' (The single rider is a devil, the two riders are two devils, and the three riders are a group). The hadith indicates that three constitute a sufficient group (ركب).
The hadith is ahad with zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Understand the counting principle
The imam is counted as part of the congregation for non-Friday prayers. Thus, with two followers, the total becomes three, satisfying the requirement of a group. This is why the imam advances in front.
For Friday prayer, the imam is not counted because he is a condition for the prayer's validity.
4
Compare with Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf holds that the imam should stand between the two followers, not in front. The Hanafi response is that the imam is counted, so the ruling for three applies.
The difference leads to a practical variation in prayer positioning.
5
Note the exception for Friday prayer
The passage explicitly excludes Friday prayer from this counting principle, requiring three men besides the imam. This is based on the verse {فَاسَعَوْا إِلَى ذِكْرِ اللَّهِ}.
This shows that takhsis can be limited by additional conditions.

(القمر) وتتبع الميراث إلخ: أي بالإجماع؛ لأن الإرث فرض والوصية نافلة وكلاهما بعد الموت، فكان الوصية تبعاً للميراث كما أن النفل تبع للفرض (السنبلي) اثنين ولو كان واحدا يقوم إلى يمين الإمام قيل: إنه إذا كان المقتدي اثنين لا يأمرهما الإمام بالتأخر بل يتقدم بنفسه ، وإذا كان واحدًا يأمره الإمام بأن يقوم عن يمين الإمام. (القمر) وذلك : تقدم الإمام إذا كان المقتدي اثنين. (القمر) الإمام أي إذا كان المقتدي اثنين. (المحشي) محسوب إلخ فإذا كان المقتدي اثنين والإمام محسوب في الجماعة، فيتحقق الثلاثة فكملت الجماعة، فيثبت حكمها، وهو تقدم الإمام، فيتقدمهما الإمام كما يتقدم إذا كان المقتدي ثلاثة (القمر) إلا في الجمعة فإن الإمام شرط لصحة أداء الجمعة فلا يمكن أن يجعل من جملة الجماعة، بخلاف سائر الصلوات، فإن الإمام ليس بشرط لصحة أدائها فيمكن أن يجعل فيها من جملة الجماعة، وقال ابن الملك: شرطنا لصحة أداء الجمعة ثلاثة سوى الإمام بدليل قوله تعالى: {فَاسَعَوْا إِلَى ذِكْرِ اللَّهِ} (الجمعة: ٩) فلابد من الذاكر وهو الخطيب، وثلاثة سواه بقوله تعالى: فَاسَعَوْا (الجمعة: 9). Topic of the General, 233. Statement of the maximum extent to which specification reaches in the general. And the brothers from the mother are blocked from a third to a sixth like three brothers, and the will is the sister of inheritance in being a succession after death, and it follows inheritance as supererogatory follows obligatory. So if he bequeaths to the clients of so-and-so and he has two clients, or to the brothers of Zayd and he has two brothers, they deserve all. Or on the sunnah, the imam advances when the followers are two: the imam advances in front of them as he advances in front of three, contrary to Abu Yusuf, for in his view he stands between them. That is because the imam is counted in the congregation. The imam: meaning the imam advances. All except in Friday prayer, for in it three men besides the imam are required, contrary to Abu Yusuf, for in his view two besides the imam suffice. And the author did not mention the third answer which was mentioned, that it is applied to traveling after the strength of Islam, for he [the Prophet] first forbade traveling alone? and being two because of the weakness of Islam and the preponderance of the disbelievers. "Succession" etc.: for each of the heir and the legatee is a successor of the deceased. (Al-Qamar) "And it follows" i.e., the will follows inheritance, for inheritance is established definitively without choice, and the will is supererogatory and optional, so the will becomes a follower of inheritance like the following of supererogatory to obligatory. When the plural is applied to two in the principal, it is applied to them in the subordinate. He who said that the meaning is that inheritance follows the will like the following of supererogatory to obligatory has erred, because the will is prior to inheritance. (Al-Qamar) "And it follows inheritance" etc.: i.e., by consensus, because inheritance is obligatory and will is supererogatory, and both are after death, so the will is a follower of inheritance as supererogatory is a follower of obligatory. (Al-Sunbuli) Two: and if there was one, he stands to the right of the imam. It is said: when the followers are two, the imam does not command them to step back, but rather he advances himself; and when there is one, the imam commands him to stand to the right of the imam. (Al-Qamar) "That": the imam's advance when the followers are two. (Al-Qamar) "The imam": i.e., when the followers are two. (Al-Muhashshi) "Counted" etc.: so if the followers are two and the imam is counted in the congregation, the three are realized, so the congregation is complete, so its ruling is established, which is the imam's advance, so he advances in front of them as he advances if the followers were three. (Al-Qamar) Except in Friday prayer, for the imam is a condition for the validity of performing Friday prayer, so he cannot be made part of the congregation, unlike other prayers, for the imam is not a condition for their valid performance, so he can be made part of the congregation in them. Ibn al-Malik said: We conditioned for the valid performance of Friday prayer three besides the imam based on the saying of Allah Most High: {So hasten to the remembrance of Allah} (Friday 9). So the one who remembers, who is the preacher, is necessary, and three besides him by His saying: "So hasten" (Friday 9). (Al-Qamar) He [the Prophet] said: "The single rider is a devil, and the two riders are two devils, and the three riders are a group" i.e., a sufficient congregation. Then when Islam became strong, he permitted for two, and the one remained as he was. And 'Ali said: "The two and above are a congregation." And the remaining arguments of the opponent with their answers are mentioned in the lengthy works.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the topic of the general (al-'amm) and the maximum extent of specification (takhsis). The author first gives an example from inheritance: brothers from the mother are blocked from a third to a sixth, similar to the case of three brothers, illustrating how the general term is specified. Then he discusses the will following inheritance as supererogatory follows obligatory. The main focus shifts to the ruling of the imam's position in congregational prayer when there are two followers. The Hanafi position states that the imam stands in front of them, just as he would with three followers, because the imam himself is counted as part of the congregation, making a total of three. Abu Yusuf disagrees, holding that the imam should stand between the two followers. The hadith of the Prophet: 'The single rider is a devil, two riders are two devils, three riders are a group' is used as a proof. The explanation is that initially, when Islam was weak, travelling alone or in pairs was discouraged because of hardship; later, with the strength of Islam, two were permitted, but one remained discouraged. 'Ali's statement that 'Two and above are a congregation' is also cited. Thus, the maximum extent of specification here is that the minimum for a valid congregation is three (including the imam), and the imam leads from the front. The exception is Friday prayer, where three men besides the imam are required due to the condition of the preacher and the verse. The commentator adds that the author did not mention a third answer about traveling, but it is understood that the hadith is applied to traveling after the strength of Islam. The opponent's arguments are not detailed here but are relegated to larger works.

Key Terms
العام (al-'amm): A general word that covers all individuals of its category without limitation.
التخصيص (al-takhsis): The restriction of a general word to some of its individuals, removing the generality.
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): A group of people praying together behind an imam; the minimum number for a valid congregation is three (including the imam) according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the imam is counted as part of the congregation, making three.
C) Because Abu Yusuf ruled it so.
D) Because the followers are required to stand behind.

Key Takeaway
The imam is counted in the congregation for the purpose of determining the minimum number for a valid congregation, except in Friday prayer.

Definition of al-Mushtarak and Its Application to the Dual-Plural Dispute
Defining al-mushtarak and using the hadith to argue its applicability to both dual and plural

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-mushtarak, distinguish it from other word categories, and explain the Hanafi position that 'fa'alna' is shared between dual and plural using the two responses from al-Tanqih.

Core Idea
A mushtarak word covers multiple realities, but only one meaning is intended at a time; context decides.

After completing the discussion of the general (al-amm), the author introduces the shared word (al-mushtarak). He provides a precise definition and then immediately applies it to a live dispute: whether the word 'fa'alna' (we did) is exclusively plural or shared between dual and plural. The proof comes from a hadith about travelling alone, in pairs, or as a group. Understanding mushtarak is essential for interpreting texts where a single word can carry multiple meanings, a common scenario in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of al-mushtarak
Read the author's definition: 'ما يتناول أفراداً مختلفة الحدود على سبيل البدل'. Note the key elements: different realities (different definitions), and the use is on an alternative basis (badal), not simultaneous (ijtimā').
The term 'individuals' here refers to the named things (musammayāt).
2
Distinguish alternation from conjunction
Understand that when a mushtarak word is used absolutely, only one of its meanings is intended. It cannot mean all meanings together. This is the core of the definition.
Contrast with the general (al-amm) which covers all its individuals simultaneously.
3
Analyze the dispute over 'fa'alna'
The opponents (Maliki and some Shafi'is) claim that 'fa'alna' is specific to the plural and that since it applies to two, the minimum plural is two. Identify their proof and the Hanafi counter-arguments.
The Hanafi response has two parts: verbal sharing (mushtarak lafẓī) and meaning sharing (mushtarak ma‘nawī).
4
Evaluate the two Hanafi responses
First: 'fa'alna' is a mushtarak lafẓī between dual and plural, so it does not force the plural upon the dual. Second: it is mushtarak ma‘nawī, denoting the speaker with another (one or more), a general concept covering two and three.
Both responses preserve the Hanafi position that dual is not necessarily plural.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The dispute affects the minimum number for jam‘ (plural) in Arabic grammar and legal interpretation. Hanafis allow dual to be considered a form of plural in certain contexts, influencing how general words are understood.
The hadith about the rider reinforces that 'three are a group', but 'fa'alna' can still refer to two.

(القمر) أخرجه مالك في الموطأ رقم: ١٧٦٤ ، باب ما جاء في الوحدة في السفر للرجل والنساء، وأبوداود رقم: ٢٦٠٧ ، باب في الرجل يسافر وحده، والترمذي رقم: ١٦٧٤ ، باب ما جاء في كراهية أن يسافر الرجل وحده قال الترمذي حديث حسن وأحمد في مسنده" رقم: ٦٧٤٨ ، عن عمرو بن شعيب عن أبيه عن جده بهذا اللفظ أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم :قال الراكب شيطان، والراكبان شيطانان، والثلاثة ركب. أخرجه ابن ماجه رقم: ۹۷۲ باب الاثنان ،جماعة، عن أبي موسى الأشعري ، والدار قطني في "سننه" ۲۸۱،۲۸۰/۱ ، باب الاثنان جماعة عن أبي موسى وعمرو بن شعيب عن أبيه عن جده، والهيثمي في مجمع الزوائد" ٤٥/٢ باب فيمن تحصل بهم فضل الجماعة، وفيه مسلمة بن علي وهو ضعيف، عن أبي أمامة له. وقال في المقاصد في إسناده (أي رواية ابن ماجة) الربيع بن بدر وهو ضعيف لكن له شاهد هكذا في الفوائد المجموعة لشوكاني. [إشراق الأبصار ٩]
Then when he finished from the topic of the general, he began to explain the shared word. Statement of the shared word. He said: As for the shared word, it is what covers individuals of different definitions on the basis of alternation. "Devil" because life is hard for the one (Al-Qamar). "Two devils" because if one of them dies or falls ill, the other is forced (Al-Qamar). "And three are a group" i.e., a sufficient congregation, because if one goes for a need, the remaining two feel comfortable, and if a delay occurs in his transaction, the other goes for his news and ascertaining his condition, and the goods do not remain empty. So it is in "al-Lum'at". (Al-Qamar) "And the one remained as he was" then traveling alone was permitted after the dominance of Islam and the emergence of its people, as al-Qari said. (Al-Qamar) The arguments of the opponent: i.e., the Maliki and some of the Shafi'is include that the word 'fa'alna' is a form specific to the plural and applies to two, so it is known that the minimum plural is two. The answer is in two ways: First: what the author of al-Tanqih chose, that 'fa'alna' is not specific to the plural but is a verbal shared word between the dual and the plural, so it does not necessitate that the dual is plural. Second: it is shared between them in meaning, for it is used for the speaker with others, whether the other is one or more, and this concept is general, applying to two, three, and above. (Al-Qamar) As for the shared word, it is linguistically from sharing, 'what covers' etc., i.e., it is placed for different realities by multiple placements, and it covers those realities in usage on the basis of alternation, not on the basis of conjunction. So what comes to mind when uttered absolutely is one of the meanings alternatively, and by individuals the named things are meant. (Al-Qamar) It was narrated by Malik in al-Muwatta', no. 1764, chapter on what came regarding traveling alone for men and women; and Abu Dawud no. 2607, chapter on a man traveling alone; and al-Tirmidhi no. 1674, chapter on the dislike of a man traveling alone; al-Tirmidhi said it is a hasan hadith; and Ahmad in his Musnad no. 6748, from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather with this wording that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The single rider is a devil, the two riders are two devils, and the three riders are a group.' It was also narrated by Ibn Majah no. 972, chapter on two being a congregation, from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari; and al-Daraqutni in his Sunan 1/280-281, chapter on two being a congregation, from Abu Musa and 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb; and al-Haythami in Majma' al-Zawa'id 2/45, chapter on by whom the virtue of congregation is achieved; and in it is Maslamah ibn 'Ali who is weak, from Abu Umamah. And he said in al-Maqasid concerning its chain (i.e., Ibn Majah's narration): al-Rabi' ibn Badr is weak, but it has a witness. Thus in al-Fawa'id al-Majmu'ah by al-Shawkani. [Ishraq al-Absar 9]
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage begins the discussion on the shared word (al-mushtarak) after completing the topic of the general. The definition given is: 'A word that covers individuals of different definitions on the basis of alternation.' This means that the word is used for multiple different meanings, but in each use, only one meaning is intended, not all at once. The text then returns to the hadith about the rider to illustrate a related principle: the opponent (Maliki and some Shafi'is) argue that the word 'fa'alna' (we did) is a plural form that applies to two, so the minimum plural is two. The Hanafi response, from the author of al-Tanqih, is twofold. First, the word 'fa'alna' is not exclusively plural; it is a shared word between dual and plural. Second, it is shared in meaning: it denotes the speaker with another, whether the other is one or more, so it applies to two, three, and beyond. This preserves the Hanafi position that the word 'fa'alna' does not necessitate that the minimum plural is two, but rather it can be a dual. The commentator then provides the full definition of al-mushtarak: it is placed for different realities by multiple placements, and in usage, only one meaning is intended at a time. The passage ends with a citation of the hadith from multiple sources to establish its authenticity, noting that some chains are weak but there are supporting narrations.

Key Terms
المشترك (al-mushtarak): A word that is placed for multiple different realities by multiple linguistic placements and is used on an alternative basis, not simultaneously.
الجمع (al-jam'): In this context, the plural number; the opponent argues that the minimum for jam' is two, but the Hanafis argue that jam' can start from three.
