Key Takeaway
Al-mushtarak is a word that covers multiple realities on an alternative basis, and its application to 'fa'alna' shows that a word can be shared between dual and plural, affecting the interpretation of general texts.

Definition of Mushtarak and the Dispute over 'Qur'
Definition of mushtarak with the 'qur' example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mushtarak, identify its key characteristic of substitution (badal), and explain how the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ in interpreting the word 'qur'.

Core Idea
Mushtarak denotes multiple distinct meanings, but only one at a time—never all at once.

In this passage, the author defines the term mushtarak (common/homonym) and uses the famous example of the word 'qur' to illustrate how differing interpretations lead to different legal rulings. Understanding mushtarak is crucial for proper textual interpretation in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the definition
Understand the precise wording 'ما يتناول أفراداً مختلفة الحدود على سبيل البدل'. Note the emphasis on substitution (بدل).
The phrase 'different definitions' excludes general terms ('amm).
2
2. Distinguish from 'amm
The phrase 'أفراداً مختلفة الحدود' excludes general terms which cover individuals with the same definition.
General terms are not mushtarak.
3
3. Grasp the Shafi'i objection
The phrase 'على سبيل البدل' guards against the Shafi'i view that mushtarak includes all meanings simultaneously (على سبيل الشمول).
This is a key point of contention.
4
4. Apply to the example of 'qur'
See how the same word can have two possible meanings (menstruation or purity) and how each school chooses one based on context and usul principles.
The schools' choices affect 'iddah calculations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المشترك: فما يتناول أفراداً مختلفة الحدود على سبيل البدل. فالمتبادر عند الإطلاق واحد من المعاني بدلاً. والمراد بالأفراد المسميات. وقوله: على سبيل البدل لبيان الواقع أو احتراز عن قول الشافعي محله: إنه على سبيل الشمول كما سيأتي. وقيل: إنه احتراز لفظ الشيء، فإنه باعتبار كونه بمعنى الموجود مشترك معنوي خارج عن هذا المشترك، وباعتبار كون أفراده مختلفة الحقائق داخل في المشترك اللفظي. وقد أوله الشافعي بالطهر، وأبو حنيفة بالحيض كما عرفت.
As for the common (mushtarak): it is that which applies to individuals with different definitions on the basis of substitution. So what is immediately understood upon absolute usage is one of the meanings by substitution. By 'individuals' is meant the named entities. His saying 'on the basis of substitution' is to state the reality or to guard against the view of al-Shafi'i, namely that it is on the basis of inclusion as will come. And it is said that it guards against the word 'thing' (shay'), for in consideration of its meaning of existence it is a common in meaning outside this mushtarak, and in consideration of its individuals having different realities it falls under verbal mushtarak. And al-Shafi'i interpreted it (qur') as purity, while Abu Hanifa interpreted it as menstruation, as you have known.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the usul term 'mushtarak' (common/homonym). The author defines it as a word that applies to multiple distinct meanings (with different legal definitions) but only one meaning at a time in usage (ala sababil badal). This excludes words that apply to multiple individuals of the same definition (like general terms). The phrase 'ala sababil badal' emphasizes that it is used for one meaning alternatively, not inclusively. This is a rebuttal to the Shafi'i view that mushtarak can mean all its meanings simultaneously (ala sababil shumul). The passage then discusses the example of the word 'qur' (قرء) which can mean either menstruation (Hayd) or purity (Tuhur). Al-Shafi'i interprets it as purity, while Abu Hanifa interprets it as menstruation, demonstrating a concrete fiqh implication of the usul principle.

Key Terms
مشترك (mushtarak): A word that is coined for multiple distinct meanings and denotes them on a substitution basis (not simultaneously).
بدل (badal): Substitution; meaning that only one of the possible meanings is intended in a given usage.
قرء (qur'): A word that can mean either menstruation or purity; an example of mushtarak.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does 'ala sababil badal' mean in the definition of mushtarak?
A) That the word includes all its meanings at once.
B) That the word denotes its meanings on a substitution basis, one at a time.
C) That the word has only one meaning.
D) That the word applies to individuals with the same definition.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of mushtarak emphasizes that it denotes meanings on a substitution basis, not inclusively, as seen in the dispute over 'qur'.

Definition and Ruling of al-Mushtarak (The Shared Word) in Hanafi Usul
Defining al-mushtarak and its ruling of tawaqquf with example of al-qur'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-mushtarak, distinguish it from al-'aam and al-khaas, and apply the Hanafi ruling of tawaqquf and ta'ammul to a given mushtarak word.

Core Idea
A mushtarak word requires suspension (tawaqquf) until reflection (ta'ammul) preponderates one meaning for action.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi definition of al-mushtarak (the shared/ambiguous word) from Noorulanwar. You will learn how it differs from general ('aam) and specific (khaas), and why the Hanafi school insists on suspending judgment and actively seeking contextual evidence before applying any one meaning. The classic example of the word 'qur'' (menstruation vs. purity) illustrates the practical stakes: the iddah of a divorced woman depends on which meaning is chosen.

Guided Path
1
Dissect the definition
The passage defines mushtarak as 'a word placed for individuals with different boundaries on an alternating basis'. Break this down: 'individuals' means more than one meaning; 'different boundaries' means the meanings are distinct; 'on an alternating basis' means you use it for one meaning at a time, not all at once.
This definition excludes al-khaas (one meaning) and al-'aam (multiple individuals under a single meaning).
2
Identify the example and the dispute
The word 'al-qur'' is given. Abu Hanifa interprets it as menstruation (hayd), al-Shafi'i as purity (tuhr). Note that these two meanings are contradictory and cannot be simultaneously true.
This is a real ikhtilaf affecting Islamic law.
3
Understand the ruling: tawaqquf and ta'ammul
The ruling of mushtarak is tawaqquf (suspension) of definitive belief, combined with ta'ammul (reflection) to determine which meaning is more likely for action. This is not for certainty but for preponderance.
Contrast with 'aam: an 'aam text is definitive until evidence specifies it; mushtarak has no definitive meaning without reflection.
4
Apply the reflection to the example
The passage lists three aspects of ta'ammul for 'qur': (1) the word 'three' in the verse, (2) the principle that the minimum of a plural is three, (3) the linguistic root meaning of 'collection and transition'. These preponderate the meaning of menstruation.
This illustrates how contextual evidence (qara'in) is used to tarjih one meaning.
5
State the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi iddah is three menstrual periods; Shafi'i iddah is three purity periods. This difference stems from the interpretation of a single mushtarak word.

Source Text

Section on al-Mushtarak. Explanation of al-Mushtarak: He meant by 'individuals' what is more than one, so that it includes the mushtarak between two meanings only, and it excludes the specific (al-khas). And his statement: 'different boundaries' excludes the general ('aam) as has passed. And his statement: 'on an alternating basis' is to explain the reality or to guard against the statement of al-Shafi'i, its place: that it is on a comprehensive basis as will come. For example, al-qur' for menstruation and purity, for it is mushtarak between these two contradictory meanings that cannot be combined; al-Shafi'i interpreted it as purity, and Abu Hanifah as menstruation, as you know. And its ruling: suspension (tawaqquf) in it on condition of reflection (ta'ammul) so that some of its aspects become preponderant for acting by it, meaning suspension from believing a specific meaning among the meanings and reflection for the sake of some aspects becoming preponderant for action, not for certain knowledge, as we reflected on al-qur' with several aspects: one is by the word 'three', the second is that the least of a plural is three, the third is that it means collection and transition, and what is collected is blood during the days of purity, and similarly what transitions is blood during menstruation, and its verification: that menstruation if it is blood.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage from Noorulanwar, a Hanafi commentary on Usul al-Bazdawi, defines the term 'al-mushtarak' (the shared or ambiguous word). It explains that mushtarak is a word placed for more than one individual (meaning) with different boundaries (i.e., distinct concepts) on an alternating basis (i.e., used for one meaning at a time, not simultaneously). This distinguishes it from 'al-khas' (specific) which covers only one individual, and 'al-'aam' (general) which covers individuals sharing a common meaning. The example given is the word 'al-qur'' which has two contradictory meanings: menstruation (hayd) and purity (tuhr). The passage notes the ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam al-Shafi'i: Abu Hanifa interprets it as menstruation, while al-Shafi'i interprets it as purity. The ruling (hukm) of mushtarak is tawaqquf (suspension) of definitive judgment until ta'ammul (reflection) is made to determine which meaning is more likely for action. This reflection is based on contextual evidence, not for certainty but for preponderance. The passage illustrates this with the example of al-qur' in the Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 2:228), citing three aspects of reflection: the word 'three' (implying the iddah of three quru'), the principle that the minimum of a plural is three, and the linguistic meanings of 'collection' and 'transition'. The legal effect is that the iddah period for a divorced woman differs based on which meaning is adopted.

Key Terms
المشترك (al-mushtarak): لفظ وضع لأفراد مختلفة الحدود على سبيل البدل
البدل (al-badal): الاستعمال لمعنى واحد في كل مرة لا الجمع
التوقف (al-tawaqquf): الامتناع عن الجزم بأحد المعاني حتى يترجح بدليل
التأمل (al-ta'ammul): النظر في الصيغة والأدلة الخارجية لترجيح أحد المعاني للعمل به لا للعلم القطعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It must be taken in both meanings simultaneously.
B) One must suspend judgment and reflect to determine the preponderant meaning for action.
C) It is treated as 'aam (general) until evidence specifies it.
D) It is considered unambiguous and applied to all meanings.

Key Takeaway
A mushtarak word requires suspension (tawaqquf) and reflection (ta'ammul) to preponderate one meaning for action, distinguishing it from 'aam which is definitive until evidence specifies it.

Ruling of the Mushtarak and the Condition of Reflection
States the ruling of mushtarak and the condition for action

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of tawaqquf (suspension) to a mushtarak word and explain how ta'ammul (reflection) is a condition for acting on a preponderant meaning.

Core Idea
A mushtarak has no generality; suspend judgment until reflection tips the scale for action, not certainty.

In Hanafi usul, a mushtarak (homonym) is a word with multiple possible meanings but no inherent preference. The Lawgiver uses such words without specifying which meaning is intended. This creates a challenge: how can a jurist act upon such a word? The answer is tawaqquf (suspension) paired with ta'ammul (reflection) to determine the preponderant meaning. This lesson unpacks that rule, clarifies a common misunderstanding about the condition of reflection, and applies it to the classic example of 'qur''.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling of mushtarak
The text states that the ruling (hukm) of a mushtarak is tawaqquf (suspension). This means one does not immediately assign a specific meaning but withholds judgment.
Tawaqquf applies only when no external evidence (qarina) indicates one meaning.
2
Understand the condition of reflection
Tawaqquf is accompanied by a condition: ta'ammul (reflection). The commentator clarifies that the condition is attached to the permissibility of acting on a meaning, not to the suspension itself. Reflection is for preponderance (tarjih) of one meaning for practice, not for certain knowledge.
The condition is not that suspension requires reflection; rather, after suspension, one reflects to act.
3
Apply to the example of 'qur''
The word 'qur'' (in Quran 2:228) is mushtarak between menstruation and purity. The Hanafis present three arguments for preponderance: (1) the explicit number 'three' requires three occurrences, which only works if it means menstruation; (2) 'quruu' is a plural, and the minimum of a plural is three, contradicting purity; (3) the root meaning of 'qur'' involves gathering and transition, fitting blood.
Each argument is a form of ta'ammul on the word itself and external context.
4
Respond to the opposing view
The Shafi'i school interprets 'qur'' as purity, citing that a plural can refer to a part (as in 'months' for Hajj). The Hanafi response refutes this by arguing that the number 'three' is explicit and the plural's partitive use requires a clear contextual indicator that is absent here.
The thamarah (practical consequence) is a different waiting period: three menstrual cycles vs. three purity periods.
5
Conclude with the operative rule
The mufta bihi (operative position) in the Hanafi school is that when encountering a mushtarak without a clear qarina, one must suspend until reflection provides a preponderant meaning for action. This is not for theoretical certainty but for practical application.
This rule applies broadly to all mushtarak words in the Quran and Sunnah.

وحكمه : التوقف فيه بشرط التأمل ليترجح بعض وجوهه للعمل به يعني التوقف عن اعتقاد معنى معين من المعاني والتأمل لأجل ترجّح بعض الوجوه لأجل العمل لا للعلم القطعي كما تأملنا في القرء بعدة أوجه أحدها بصيغة ثلاثة، والثاني: بكون أقل الجمع ثلاثة على ما مرّ، والثالث بأنه بمعنى الجمع والانتقال، والمجتمع: هو الدم في أيام الطهر، وكذا المنتقل هو الدم في أيام الحيض، وتحقيقه: أن الحيض إن كان هو الدم بشرط التأمل: توجيه العبارة : أن قول المصنف : ليترجح إلخ متعلق بالتأمل، وقوله: للعمل به متعلق بالشرط، والباء في قوله بشرط إلخ للتلبس وتقدير العبارة وهو أي المشترك متلبس بشرط إلخ، والمعنى أن التأمل لترجح بعض وجوهه أي معانيه شرط للعمل ،به وهذا المعنى ،حق وليس المراد ما يفهم من ظاهر عبارة المصنف أن التوقف مشروط بالتأمل كيف فإنه لو كان كذلك لزم تقدم التأمل على التوقف لتقدم الشرط على المشروط، واللازم باطل، فكذا الملزوم . (القمر) التوقف عن اعتقاد إلخ فإنه لا عموم للمشترك على ما سيجيء، فكان الثابت واحدًا من المعاني وهو غير معين عند السامع، ولا ترجيح لأحدها على الآخر فيجب التوقف.(القمر) والتأمل أي في نفس الصيغة، أو في غيرها من الأدلة والأمارات. (القمر) بصيغة ثلاثة فإنه لو أريد بالقرء الطهر كما هو عند الشافعي ، ووقع الطلاق في الطهر ويحتسب هذا الطهر كما هو عنده لزم أن يكون عدتها طهرين وبعضا لا ثلاثة، فيبطل موجب الثلاثة وقد مرّ مفصلاً. (القمر) بكون أقل الجمع إلخ يعني أن القروء جمع، وأقل الجمع ثلاث، ولو أريد بالقروء الأطهار يبطل معنى الجمع، وفيه: أن الجمع قد يراد به البعض كما في قوله تعالى: الْحَجَّ أَشْهُرُ مَعْلُومات) (البقرة: ۱۹۷)، فإنه يراد بالأشهر شهران -أي شوال وذو القعدة وعشرة أيام من ذي الحجة، فلا حجة على الشافعي باعتبار قوله تعالى: (البقرة: ۲۲۸) من غير قوله تعالى : ثَلاثَةِ (البقرة : ١٩٦) على ما قد مرّ مفصلا. (القمر) بمعنى الجمع يقال: قرأت الشيء قرآنا" أي جمعته، وضممت بعضه إلى بعض كذا قيل. (القمر) والانتقال : يقال : قرء النجم إذا انتقل من مكان . Statement of the ruling of the homonym: Its ruling is suspension with the condition of reflection so that some of its aspects become preponderant for acting upon it, meaning suspension from believing a specific meaning among the meanings, and reflection for the sake of preponderance of some aspects for the sake of action, not for certain knowledge, as we reflected upon 'qur'' in several aspects: one is the expression 'three', the second is that the minimum of a plural is three as has passed, the third is that it means 'gathering' and 'transition', and the gathered is the blood in the days of purity, and likewise the transitioning is the blood in the days of menstruation. Its verification: that if menstruation is blood, with the condition of reflection: interpretation of the expression: that the statement of the author: 'so that it becomes preponderant' etc. is related to reflection, and his statement: 'for acting upon it' is related to the condition, and the 'ba' in his statement 'with the condition' is for accompaniment, and the estimation of the expression: it (the homonym) is accompanied by a condition etc. The meaning is that reflection for the preponderance of some of its aspects (i.e., its meanings) is a condition for acting upon it, and this meaning is correct. And it is not that which is understood from the apparent expression of the author that the suspension is conditioned by reflection; how so? For if that were the case, reflection would have to precede suspension due to the precedence of the condition over the conditioned, and the consequent is false, so likewise the antecedent. (al-Qamar) Suspension from believing etc.: for there is no generality for the homonym as will come, so what is established is one of the meanings, but it is unspecified for the listener, and there is no preponderance of one over the other, so suspension is necessary. (al-Qamar) And reflection: i.e., in the word itself or in other evidence and indications. (al-Qamar) By the expression 'three': for if by 'qur'' is meant purity as is the case according to al-Shafi'i, and divorce occurred in purity and this purity is counted as he holds, then her waiting period would be two purities and a part, not three, thus the requirement of three would be nullified, and it has passed in detail. (al-Qamar) By the minimum of plural etc.: meaning that 'quru'' is a plural, and the minimum of a plural is three, and if by 'quru'' is meant purities, the meaning of plural would be invalidated. In it: that a plural may sometimes refer to a part, as in His statement: 'The Hajj is (in) known months' (Quran 2:197), for by 'months' is meant two months — Shawwal and Dhu al-Qa'dah and ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah, so there is no evidence against al-Shafi'i by considering His statement (2:228) without His statement 'three' (2:196) as has passed in detail. (al-Qamar) By meaning 'gathering': it is said: 'qara't al-shay' qur'anan' i.e., I gathered it, and I joined some of it to some, as was said. (al-Qamar) And 'transition': it is said: 'qar'a al-najm' when it moved from a place. (al-Qamar) And its verification etc.: The summary is that menstruation and purity have two meanings: as for menstruation, it is either blood or its days; likewise purity is either cleanliness or its days. Menstruation in both estimations is suitable for the meaning of 'qur'', unlike purity. (al-Sunbuli) That menstruation etc.: meaning that 'qur'' means menstruation, and menstruation if it is etc. (al-Qamar) So it is the gathered and the transitioning even if it is not gathering; unlike purity, for it is not gathering nor gathered nor transitioning. But if it is the days of blood, they are the place of gathering and transition; unlike the days of purity, for they are not a place of transition even if they are a place of gathering at first glance. And I have clarified that in 'al-Tafsir al-Ahmadi', and here there is no space for it.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling of the mushtarak (homonym) in Hanafi usul. The author states that the ruling is tawaqquf (suspension) with the condition of ta'ammul (reflection) to prefer one meaning for action, not for certain knowledge. The commentator then clarifies the wording of the matn, arguing that the condition is attached to the reflection, not to the suspension itself. This is important because if suspension were conditioned by reflection, then reflection would have to occur before suspension, which is not the case. Instead, the mushtarak is inherently suspended until reflection provides a preponderant meaning for practice. The passage then uses the example of the word 'qur'' (which can mean menstruation or purity) to illustrate how reflection operates. The Hanafis argue that 'qur'' means menstruation, and they provide three linguistic and legal arguments: (1) the expression 'three' in the Quranic verse about waiting periods, (2) the minimum of a plural is three, so 'quru'' as a plural requires at least three, and the Shafi'i interpretation leads to a contradiction, and (3) the root meaning of 'qur'' involves gathering and transition, which apply to blood (menstruation) and not to purity. The commentary goes into detail, citing previous discussions and addressing Shafi'i objections. The main point is that the mushtarak requires scholarly reflection to determine the intended meaning, and that reflection is a condition for acting on one of its possible meanings.

Key Terms
المشترك (al-mushtarak): A word that has more than one meaning in the language, used by the Lawgiver without preference.
التوقف (al-tawaqquf): To withhold judgment and not assign a specific meaning until after reflection.
التأمل (al-ta'ammul): Reflection on the word itself and external evidence to determine the preponderant meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Both meanings can be intended simultaneously.
B) One must suspend judgment until reflection preponderates one meaning for action.
C) The meaning closest to the literal sense is to be taken.
D) The word is considered general and covers all meanings.

Key Takeaway
A mushtarak word requires tawaqquf (suspension) and reflection (ta'ammul) to determine the most likely meaning for action, not for certainty.

Intending Both Meanings of a Homonym: The Hanafi–Shafi‘i Dispute
Presents a madhhab dispute on mushtarak and its generality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on intending both meanings of a mushtarak, contrast it with the Shafi'i view, and apply the Hanafi objection based on the requirement of unified action for emulation (iqta').

Core Idea
A mushtarak has no generality; intending both meanings simultaneously is impossible because it would invalidate the purpose of emulation.

This lesson examines a classic usul dispute: when a word has two equally possible meanings (a mushtarak), can a speaker intend both at once in a single utterance? The Hanafi school says no, while al-Shafi'i says yes, citing the Quranic verse 'Indeed, Allah and His angels send blessings upon the Prophet' (33:56), where 'yusalluna' conveys different meanings from Allah and the angels. We will explore the Hanafi rebuttal based on the verse's purpose of obligating emulation, and understand the practical consequence for usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
The core dispute: may a single utterance of a mushtarak intend both its meanings? The Hanafi school prohibits this; al-Shafi'i permits it. Read the opening lines of the Arabic passage to confirm each side.
The base text begins with 'ولا عموم له... عندنا فلا يجوز'. The Shafi'i view is introduced with 'وقال الشافعي'.
2
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Al-Shafi'i argues based on the Quranic verse where 'yusalluna' is used for both Allah (mercy) and the angels (seeking forgiveness). Identify the verse and note how the Shafi'i uses it as evidence that a single word can carry two meanings.
The verse is cited as: إِنَّ اللَّهَ وَمَلائِكَتَهُ يُصَلُّونَ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response does not deny that the word has two meanings; rather it rejects that both are intended simultaneously in one utterance. They argue that the verse commands believers to emulate (iqta') Allah and the angels, which requires that the action of 'salah' be one unified act. If 'yusalluna' had two different meanings, the emulation would be incoherent.
The Hanafi says: 'سيقت الآية لإيجاب اقتداء المؤمنين بالله والملائكة، ولا يصلح ذلك... فلابد من اتحاد الفعل'.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: when a mushtarak appears in a legal text without context, a Hanafi will not derive multiple rules from it but will seek evidence to determine the intended single meaning. A Shafi'i may consider both meanings applicable.
This shows how the dispute directly affects the derivation of ahkam.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text favors the Hanafi position, as it presents a logical refutation of the Shafi'i argument based on the requirement of unity in the object of emulation. The Hanafi objection is that if the two meanings were intended, the command to emulate would be absurd.
This is consistent with the broader Hanafi principle that a mushtarak has no generality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا عموم له أي للمشترك ،عندنا فلا يجوز إرادة معنييه معًا، وقال الشافعي له: يجوز أن يراد به المعنيان معا كما في قوله تعالى: إِنَّ اللَّهَ وَمَلائِكَتَهُ يُصَلُّونَ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ، فالصلاة من الله رحمة، ومن الملائكة استغفار، وقد أريدا بلفظ واحد وهو قوله: "يصلون"، ونحن نقول: سيقت الآية لإيجاب اقتداء المؤمنين بالله والملائكة، ولا يصلح ذلك وإن كان أيام الدم إلخ والحاصل أن الحيض اسم للدم على الحقيقة قد يطلق على الأيام مجازا، وكذلك الطهر فإن حالا على الحقيقة فالدم مجتمع ومنتقل، وإن كان ليس بجامع، بخلاف الطهر ، فإنه ليس بجامع ولا مجتمع ولا منتقل وإن حملا على الأيام، فأيام الحيض محل الاجتماع والانتقال والجمع وأما أيام الطهر فهي محل الاجتماع في الظاهر، ولكن الحق أن أيام الحيض هي محل لاجتماع الدم في الرحم من العروق فافهم. (السنبلي) في بادي الرأي وأما في نفس الأمر فمحل الاجتماع هي أيام الحيض كذا قيل. (القمر) وقد أوضحت إلخ في التفسير" الأحمدي : أن لفظ "القرء " مشترك بين الجمع والانتقال، وكلا المعنيين يناسب الحيض؛ لأن الجمع بمعنى المجهول يصف به الدم وإن لم يكن بمعنى المعروف كذلك ؛ لأنه المجتمع في الحقيقة وإن لم يكن جامعاً، بخلاف الطهر؛ فإنه ليس بجامع ولا مجتمع غايته أنه محل الاجتماع بل الحق أن أيام الحيض هي محل الاجتماع والخروج على ما قال البعض، وهكذا نقول في معنى الانتقال: إن المنتقل هو الدم، وأيضا الانتقال يكون بالدم لا بالطهر؛ لأن الطهر هو الأصل في بنات آدم والانتقال بالعوارض دون الأصول. (القمر) معنييه [أي في إطلاق واحد لا حقيقة، وإلا يلزم كون اللفظ المجموع المعنيين، ولا مجازا وإلا يلزم الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز . (المحشي) يجوز أن يراد إلخ: بل يجب الحمل على المعنيين عند التجرد عن القرائن ولا يحمل على أحد المعنيين خاصة لا بقرينة. (القمر) ولا يصلح ذلك إلخ لأنه لو قيل: "إن الله يرحم النبي والملائكة يستغفرون له يا أيها الذين آمنوا ادعوا له" لكان هذا الكلام في غاية الركاكة فإن إيجاب الاقتداء إنما هو بالتحريض على ما يصدر عمن يقتدي به، فلابد من اتحاد الفعل ألا ترى أنه ليس إيجاب الاقتداء في مثل قولنا: فلان يصوم فاقرؤوا القرآن. (القمر)
And there is no generality for it (i.e., the homonym) according to us, so it is not permissible to intend both its meanings together. Al-Shafi'i said: It is permissible for both meanings to be intended together, as in His statement: 'Indeed, Allah and His angels send blessings upon the Prophet' (Quran 33:56), for 'salah' from Allah is mercy, and from angels is seeking forgiveness, and both were intended by one word, which is His statement 'yusalluna'. And we say: The verse was brought to obligate the believers to emulate Allah and the angels, and that is not valid even if it is the days of blood, etc. The summary is that menstruation is a name for blood in reality, and may be applied metaphorically to days; and likewise purity, if it is applied to cleanliness in reality, then blood is gathered and transitioning, even if it is not gathering; unlike purity, for it is not gathering, gathered, or transitioning, even if both are applied to days. The days of menstruation are the place of gathering, transition, and collecting; as for the days of purity, they are a place of gathering in appearance, but the truth is that the days of menstruation are the place for the gathering of blood in the womb from the veins, so understand. (al-Sunbuli) In initial opinion, but in reality, the place of gathering is the days of menstruation, it was said. (al-Qamar) And I have clarified etc. in 'al-Tafsir al-Ahmadi': that the word 'qur'' is a homonym between gathering and transition, and both meanings are suitable for menstruation; because gathering in the sense of the passive participle describes blood, even if it is not in the sense of the active participle; because it is gathered in reality even if it does not gather; unlike purity, for it is not gathering nor gathered, at most it is a place of gathering, but the truth is that the days of menstruation are the place of gathering and exiting according to what some said. And likewise we say regarding the meaning of transition: the transitioning is the blood, and also transition occurs with blood, not with purity; because purity is the original state in daughters of Adam, and transition occurs through accidents, not through origins. (al-Qamar) Its two meanings (i.e., in a single literal sense, otherwise it would necessitate the word being the sum of the two meanings, and it is not metaphorical, otherwise it would necessitate combining the literal and metaphorical). (al-Muhashi) Permissible etc.: Rather, it is obligatory to apply both meanings in the absence of contextual indicators, and it should not be applied to one of the two meanings specifically without evidence. (al-Qamar) And that is not valid etc., because if it were said: 'Allah has mercy on the Prophet and the angels seek forgiveness for him, O you who believe, pray for him', this statement would be extremely ugly, for obligating emulation is only by urging what comes from the one being emulated, so the action must be unified. Do you not see that there is no obligating of emulation in our saying: 'So-and-so fasts, so recite the Quran'? (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage presents a key usul dispute between the Hanafis and al-Shafi'i concerning the mushtarak (homonym) and its 'umum (generality). The Hanafi position is that a mushtarak has no generality, meaning it cannot be used to intend multiple meanings simultaneously. The Shafi'i position is that it is permissible, citing the Quranic verse 'إِنَّ اللَّهَ وَمَلَائِكَتَهُ يُصَلُّونَ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ' where the word 'يصلون' means mercy from Allah and seeking forgiveness from angels—two different meanings intended by one word. The Hanafi response argues that the verse aims to obligate believers to emulate Allah and the angels, which requires a unified action. If 'يصلون' had two distinct meanings, the command to emulate would be incoherent. The passage then continues with further elaboration on the example of 'qur'', reinforcing that the root meanings of gathering and transition apply to menstruation, not purity, thus supporting the Hanafi interpretation. The commentary also includes a note from al-Muhashi that according to one view, intending both meanings is obligatory when there is no contextual evidence. Overall, the dispute illustrates the Hanafi principle that a homonym cannot be treated as general, and that its use requires careful reflection to determine a single intended meaning.

Key Terms
المشترك (al-mushtarak): A word with multiple meanings, each equally possible without context.
العموم (al-‘umum): Generality; the property of a word covering all its individual instances.
الاقتداء (al-iqtida'): Emulation; following someone's example in action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling regarding intending both meanings of a mushtarak (homonym) in one statement according to the passage?
A) It is obligatory.
B) It is permissible.
C) It is not permissible.
D) It depends on the context.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a mushtarak has no generality and cannot be used to intend both meanings simultaneously; the Shafi'i view is refuted by the requirement of a unified action for emulation.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
6 min
Conflict Between Mufassar and Muhkam and Between Nass and Mufassar
Examples of resolving textual conflicts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of tarjih between Mufassar and Muhkam, and between Nass and Mufassar, identifying which text prevails and why.

Core Idea
When textual categories conflict, Muhkam beats Mufassar, and Mufassar beats Nass.

Texts in Hanafi usul are classified by clarity. When two texts conflict, the clearer category prevails. This lesson unpacks two classic examples: a Quranic conflict between Mufassar and Muhkam, and a juristic conflict between Nass and Mufassar in a marriage case. You will learn how to navigate these hierarchies and respond to objections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two texts and their categories
For the Quranic example: Q 65:2 (Mufassar requiring just witnesses) vs Q 24:4 (Muhkam permanently rejecting testimony). For the marriage example: the word 'tazawwaj' (Nass in marriage) vs 'to a month' (Mufassar in mut'a).
Mufassar admits only abrogation as a figurative possibility; Muhkam admits nothing else. Nass is clear but may allow interpretation.
2
Determine the apparent conflict
In the Quranic example, the first verse seems to accept testimony of repentant slanderers, the second rejects it absolutely. In the marriage example, 'marriage' suggests permanence, 'to a month' suggests temporary union.
Conflict (ta'arud) means both texts cannot be applied simultaneously.
3
Apply the principle of tarjih
For the Quran: Muhkam takes precedence over Mufassar. For the marriage: Mufassar takes precedence over Nass. Additionally, explicit wording (ibara) outweighs implication (ishara).
Tarjih is based on the category hierarchy, not just the texts themselves.
4
Examine objections and responses
Al-Husami objects that Q 65:2 is not Mufassar due to possibilities (obligation/recommendation, blind/slaves). Answer: it is Mufassar in the specific meaning ('acceptance'), and absolute includes only perfect individuals. Another objection: no real conflict - ishhad ≠ qabul. Response: even if conflated, ibara > ishara.
These responses refine the application of the categories.
5
Derive the ruling
Ruling 1: Testimony of repentant slanderers is permanently rejected (Q 24:4 prevails). Ruling 2: A marriage with a fixed term is void (mut'a), because the Mufassar clause outweighs the Nass.
The practical result differs from Zufar's view.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مبحث المحكم
المثال للظاهر والنص
ومثال تعارض المفسر مع المحكم قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَشْهِدُوا ذَوَيْ عَدْلٍ مِنْكُمْ﴾ مع قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تَقْبَلُوا لَهُمْ شَهَادَةً أَبَدًا﴾، فإن الأول مفسر يقتضي قبول شهادة محدودين في القذف بعد التوبة؛ لأنهما صارا عدلين حينئذ، والثاني محكم يقتضي عدم قبولها؛ لوجود التأبيد فيه صريحًا، فإذا تعارض بينهما يعمل على المحكم هكذا في كتب الأصول، وما قيل: إنه أتى في عدم قبول الشهادة لم يوجد مثال تعارض المفسر مع المحكم، فمن قلة التتبع.
ثم أن المصنف ذكر مثالا لتعارض النص مع المفسر من المسائل الفقهية على سبيل التفريع. فقال: حتى قلنا: إنه إذا تزوج امرأة إلى شهر أنه يكون متعة يريد أن قوله: "تزوج" نص في النكاح فإن الأول مفسر إلخ أورد شارح الحسامي أي صاحب التحقيق إنا لا نسلم أن الأول مفسر؛ لأن المفسر ما لا يحتمل شيئا سوى مدلوله إلا النسخ، وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَشْهِدُوا ذَوَيْ عَدْلٍ مِنْكُمْ﴾ يحتمل الإيجاب والندب، ويتناول بإطلاقه الأعمى والعبيد، وهما ليسا بمرادين إجماعًا، فكيف يسمى مفسرًا مع هذه الاحتمالات. وأجيب من ملا محمد عرفان بأن الغرض أن الأول مفسر في القبول، فلا يضره هذه الاحتمالات، ولا يتناول الأعمى والعبيد لانصراف المطلق إلى الكمال ولا كمال لهما. القمر فإذا تعارض بينهما إلخ فيه أنه لا تعارض؛ لأن حكم الأول الإشهاد وحكم الثاني عدم قبول الشهادة عند الأداء، وليس القبول لازماً للإشهاد؛ ألا ترى أن إشهاد المحدودين في القذف والأعمى صحيح حتى ينعقد النكاح بشهادتهم، ولا يقبل شهادتهم عند الأداء، ولو سلمنا أن القبول لازم للإشهاد فالأول يدل على قبول شهادة المحدودين في القذف بطريق الإشارة، والثاني يدل على عدم قبولها بالعبارة والعبارة تترجح على الإشارة فصار الترجيح بهذا الاعتبار لا باعتبار كون الثاني محكما والأول مفسرًا تدبر. القمر أنه يكون متعة: خلافا لزفر الله فإنه يقول: إن التوقيت إلى شهر باطل، والنكاح يكون صحيحًا؛ لأن النكاح لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة بل تبطل الشروط. القمر أنه يكون متعة: لا نكاح؛ لأنّ التزوج نص في النكاح وإن كان محتملاً أن يراد به المتعة مجازا وقوله: إلى شهر مفسر في المتعة ليس فيه احتمال النكاح؛ إذ النكاح لا يحتمل التوقيت بحال، وإذا اجتمعا رجحنا المفسر، وحملنا النص عليه. السنبلي يريد أن قوله إلخ: هذا دفع دخل مقدر هو أن قول المصنف: إنه متعة ينادي بأعلى نداء أنه لا احتمال فيه لغير المتعة بل هو متعين له وليس كذلك، فقال: مراد المصنف أن في هذا الكلام قول القائل تزوجت امرأة نص في النكاح لكنه يحتمل كونه متعة، وقوله: "إلى شهر" مفسر في كونه متعة، فرجح كونه متعة؛ لأن وقت تعارض النص والمفسر يرجح = لكنه يحتمل تأويل أن يكون نكاحاً إلى أجل، فيكون متعة، وقوله: "إلى شهر" مفسر في هذا المعنى أي النكاح إلى أجل لا يحتمل إلا كونه متعة، فيحمل على المتعة، ولكن لا يخلو هذا من المسامحة؛ لأن قوله: "إلى شهر" متعلق بقوله: "تزوج"، وليس كلامًا مستقلاً بنفسه حتى يكون مفسراً يصلح معارضا له، فكأنه أراد أن هذا الكلام دائر بين كونه نكاحًا وبين كونه متعة، فرجحت المتعة. المفسر ثم بعد ذلك نظر الشارح في هذا الجواب بأن فيه مسامحة؛ لأن قوله : "إلى شهر" لا يصلح أن يكون مفسرا لكونه غير مستقل بنفسه، ثم بعد ذلك أزاح ذلك النظر، وقال: مراد المصنف أن هذا الكلام يحتمل أمرين نكاحا ومتعة فرجحت المتعة فلا غبار فيه؛ لأنه ليس فيه نسبة كونه متعة إلى قوله إلى شهر فتدبر. السنبلي فيكون متعة : أي فيكون نكاحاً مؤقتا فاسدًا كالمتعة؛ لأنه يكون متعة حقيقة، فإن المتعة تختص بلفظ التمتع كذا في كتب الفقه، ثم اعلم أن المتعة لا تجوز عند الأئمة الأربعة، وما في "الهداية" من نسبة حل المتعة إلى مالك فغلط كما ذكره الشارحون كذا في البحر الرائق. القمر إلا كونه متعة أي إلا كونه في حكم المتعة. القمر وليس كلامًا مستقلا إلخ بل الكل كلام واحد ولا معنى للتعارض بين أجزاء الكلام. القمر
Chapter on the Muhkam. The example for Zahir and Nass. And an example of conflict between the Mufassar and the Muhkam: His statement Exalted: 'and call to witness two just men from among you' (At-Talaq 2) compared with His statement Exalted: 'and never accept their testimony' (An-Nur 4). The first is Mufassar, requiring acceptance of the testimony of those who were lashed in qadhf (false accusation of adultery) after repentance because they have become just at that time. The second is Muhkam, requiring non-acceptance of their testimony due to the express eternity in it. So when they conflict, action is taken upon the Muhkam. Thus in the books of Usul. And what was said: 'It has come in non-acceptance of testimony, no example of conflict between Mufassar and Muhkam was found' is due to lack of research. Then the author mentioned an example of conflict between Nass and Mufassar from jurisprudential issues by way of derivation. He said: 'Until we said: If a man marries a woman for a month, that it is mut'a.' He intends that his saying 'he married' is Nass in marriage. For the first is Mufassar etc. The commentator al-Husami, i.e. the author of at-Tahqiq, objected: We do not accept that the first is Mufassar because the Mufassar is what does not admit anything other than its signification except abrogation, and His statement Exalted: 'and call to witness two just men from among you' admits obligation and recommendation, and in its absoluteness includes the blind and slaves, and these are not intended by consensus, so how is it called Mufassar with these possibilities? It was answered by Mulla Muhammad Irfan that the point is that the first is Mufassar in acceptance, so these possibilities do not harm it, and it does not include the blind and slaves because the absolute is diverted to perfection and they have no perfection. (Al-Qamar) 'So when they conflict between them etc.' There is no conflict because the legal effect of the first is witnessing (ishhad) and the legal effect of the second is non-acceptance of testimony at the time of performance, and acceptance is not necessary for witnessing; do you not see that the witnessing of those lashed in qadhf and the blind is valid such that marriage is concluded by their testimony, yet their testimony is not accepted at the time of performance? And if we concede that acceptance is necessary for witnessing, then the first indicates acceptance of the testimony of those lashed in qadhf by way of indication (ishara), and the second indicates non-acceptance by explicit wording (ibara), and explicit wording takes precedence over indication, so preponderance is by this consideration, not by considering the second as Muhkam and the first as Mufassar. Consider. (Al-Qamar) 'That it is mut'a': contrary to Zufar, may Allah have mercy on him, who says: The stipulation of a month is void, and the marriage is valid because marriage is not invalidated by invalid conditions, rather the conditions become void. (Al-Qamar) 'That it is mut'a': not marriage, because 'tazawwaj' is Nass in marriage, even though it can possibly be intended figuratively as mut'a, and his saying 'to a month' is Mufassar in mut'a, having no possibility of marriage because marriage does not admit a fixed time at all, and when they come together we give preponderance to the Mufassar and interpret the Nass in accordance with it. (As-Sunbuli) 'He intends that his saying etc.': This is a response to an anticipated objection: The author's saying 'it is mut'a' cries out loudly that there is no possibility other than mut'a, rather it is determined as such, but it is not so. He said: The author intends that in this statement, the speaker's saying 'I married a woman' is Nass in marriage, but it can possibly be mut'a, and his saying 'to a month' is Mufassar in it being mut'a, so he gave preponderance to it being mut'a because when Nass and Mufassar conflict, the Mufassar is given preponderance. (continued) But it admits an interpretation that it is a marriage for a term, so it is mut'a, and his saying 'to a month' is Mufassar in this meaning, i.e. marriage for a term, admitting only mut'a, so it is interpreted as mut'a. But this is not free from negligence because his saying 'to a month' is attached to his saying 'he married' and is not speech independent by itself so as to be a Mufassar validly opposing it. So it is as if he intended that this statement revolves between being marriage and being mut'a, so mut'a was given preponderance. (Al-Mufassar) Then after that, the commentator considered this answer as having negligence because his saying 'to a month' cannot be Mufassar due to being not independent. Then after that, he removed that consideration and said: The author's intent is that this statement admits two possibilities: marriage and mut'a, and mut'a was given preponderance, so there is no objection because there is no attribution of being mut'a to his saying 'to a month'. Reflect. (As-Sunbuli) '(fayakunu) mut'a': i.e. it is a temporary, invalid marriage like mut'a because it is truly mut'a. Indeed, mut'a is specific to the word 'tamattu' as in the books of fiqh. Then know that mut'a is not permissible according to the four imams, and what is in al-Hidayah attributing permissibility of mut'a to Malik is an error as mentioned by the commentators, thus in al-Bahr ar-Raiq. (Al-Qamar) 'except that it is mut'a' i.e. except that it is in the ruling of mut'a. (Al-Qamar) 'And it is not independent speech etc.' Rather the whole is one speech and there is no meaning to conflict between parts of speech. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage from Noorul Anwar, a Hanafi usul al-fiqh text, presents two key examples of how to resolve conflicts between different categories of clear texts (zahir, nass, mufassar, muhkam). The author first addresses the conflict between Mufassar (a text clear in meaning, admitting only the possibility of abrogation) and Muhkam (even clearer, beyond abrogation). He cites two Quranic verses: (Quran 65:2) 'and call to witness two just men from among you' which is Mufassar in requiring two just witnesses, and (Quran 24:4) 'and never accept their testimony' which is Muhkam in permanently rejecting the testimony of those who falsely accuse. The ruling is that the Muhkam takes precedence. The author notes that a claim that no such example exists is due to lack of research. The commentator al-Husami objects that the first verse is not Mufassar because it admits possibilities (obligation vs. recommendation, inclusion of blind/slaves). The answer by Mulla Muhammad Irfan clarifies that it is Mufassar in acceptance, and the absolute is interpreted as perfect individuals. Another objection raises that there is no actual conflict because the first deals with witnessing (ishhad) and the second with accepting testimony (qabul); even if acceptance is necessary, the first indicates by ishara (implication) and the second by ibara (explicit wording), and explicit wording outweighs implication. The second example involves conflict between Nass and Mufassar. If someone says 'I married a woman for one month,' the word 'tazawwajtu' is Nass (clear) in marriage, but 'to a month' is Mufassar in temporary marriage (mut'a). Since Mufassar outweighs Nass, the ruling is that it is mut'a (void). The text discusses objections from Zufar who holds the marriage valid with void condition, and addresses concerns about the independence of the temporal clause. Ultimately, the Hanafi position is that such a statement results in mut'a, which is forbidden by consensus of the four imams. The passage demonstrates the Hanafi usul principle of tarjih (preponderance) among textual categories.

Key Terms
المفسر (al-mufassar): A text that does not admit any meaning other than its literal signification except the possibility of abrogation.
المحكم (al-muhkam): A text that is definitive and cannot be abrogated; it is the highest level of clarity.
النص (al-nass): A text that is clear in its literal meaning but may admit interpretation or specification.
الإشارة (al-ishara): Implication or indirect indication; a text's meaning derived not from its wording but from context.
العبارة (al-ibara): Explicit wording; the direct meaning from the text's phrasing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the marriage example, why does 'to a month' take precedence over 'married'?
A) Because 'married' is a general term while 'to a month' is specific.
B) Because 'to a month' is Mufassar and 'married' is Nass, and Mufassar outweighs Nass.
C) Because the majority of jurists agree that temporary marriage is void.
D) Because 'to a month' is a condition that invalidates the contract.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, Muhkam prevails over Mufassar, and Mufassar prevails over Nass; additionally, explicit wording (ibara) outweighs implication (ishara).

Definition and Ruling of Mushkil
Definition and ruling of mushkil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mushkil in Hanafi usul, distinguish it from khafi, and apply the method of talab and ta'ammul to resolve ambiguous texts.

Core Idea
Mushkil is speech that has entered among similar meanings; its resolution requires belief in truth, then seeking possible meanings, then contemplation.

This passage introduces the Hanafi concept of mushkil—a level of textual ambiguity distinct from khafi and nass. Understanding mushkil is essential for correctly interpreting verses and hadiths that have multiple possible meanings. The passage gives a clear definition and a practical example from the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Definition of Mushkil
Read the definition: 'الداخل في أشكاله' meaning speech that has entered among its similar forms. Understand that this creates ambiguity because the word shares multiple meanings.
The term 'ashkal' means similar forms, not just any ambiguity.
2
Analyze the Analogy of the Stranger
The analogy of a stranger changing clothes to blend in illustrates that mushkil has more concealment than khafi. This is why it requires two steps: talab first, then ta'ammul.
Khafi is concealment due to external factors; mushkil is inherent in the word.
3
State the Ruling (Hukm) of Mushkil
The ruling is: first believe that the intended meaning is true, then undertake talab (seeking the possible meanings) and ta'ammul (contemplation) to determine the intended meaning.
Belief is a prerequisite, not a conclusion.
4
Apply to the Quranic Example (2:223)
Apply the three steps to 'anna' in 'fa'tu harthakum anna shi'tum': 1) Believe it is true. 2) Seek possible meanings (how/where). 3) Contemplate using 'harth' to see that 'how' is intended, forbidding anal intercourse.
Context (siyaq/sabaq) is crucial in ta'ammul.

وقال إنه منكر، وروى ابن أبي شيبة عن ابن عباس عم أنه قال: "ليس على النباش قطع" كذا في المحلى. تعريف المشكل وحكمه
أي حكم المشكل أولا هو اعتقاد الحقية فيما كان مراد الله تعالى بمجرد سماع الكلام، ثم : الإقبال على الطلب أي أنه لأي معان يستعمل هذا اللفظ ثم التأمل فيه بأنه أي معنى يراد ههنا من بين المعاني، فيتبين المراد، ومثاله: قوله تعالى: ﴿فَأْتُوا حَرْثَكُمْ أَنَّى شِئْتُمْ، فإن كلمة
(البقرة : ٢٢٣)
"أبى" مشكلة تجيء تارة بمعنى "من أين" كما في قوله تعالى: أَنَّى لَكِ هذا، أي من أين لك (آل عمران : (۳) هذا الرزق الآتي كل يوم، وتارة بمعنى "كيف" كما في قوله تعالى: أَنَّى يَكُونُ لِي غُلامٌ (آل عمران: ٤٠) أي كيف يكون لي غلام فاشتبه ههنا أنه بأي معنى هو، فإن كان بمعنى "أين" يكون المعنى
من أي مكان شئتم قبلاً أو دبرًا ، فتحل اللواطة من امرأته، وإن كان بمعنى "كيف"، فيكون المعنى بأية كيفية شئتم قائمًا أو قاعدًا أو مضطجعًا، فيدل على تعميم الأحوال دون المحال، فإذا تأملنا في لفظ الحرث علمنا أنه بمعنى "كيف"؛ لأن الدبر ليس بموضع الحرث بل موضع
الفرث، فتكون اللواطة من امرأته حرامًا، لكن حرمتها ظنية حتى لا يكفر مستحلها،
التأمل أي بالنظر إلى السياق والسباق. (القمر) فأتوا حرثكم إلخ شبه الله تعالى النطفة التي يخلق منها الأولاد بالبذر، وشبه رحمهن بالأرض، وشبه الأولاد بالغلة الحاصلة الأرض. (القمر) من كلمة أنى مشكلة إلخ : قيل: لا يتأتى الطلب والتأمل في كلمة أنى، فإن الإشكال فيه إما أن يكون بالنسبة إلى من هو عارف باللغة، أو إلى غيره، فالأول لا يحتاج إلى الطلب؛ لأنه يعلم أنه مشترك بين معنى "أين وكيف" بل يحتاج إلى التأمل فقط حتى يظهر أنها بمعنى كيف أو أين وأما الثاني فالخفي مشكل عنده أيضًا لاحتياجه إلى طلب معناه، ثم التأمل في المراد فتأمل (السنبلي) كما في قوله تعالى: أي حكاية عن قول زكريا لمريم على نبينا وعلية . (القمر) أن يكون إلخ: هذا قول زكريا عليه حين بشر بالولد (القمر) ههنا أي في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَأْتُوا حَرْثَكُمْ أَنَّى شتم (البقرة : ۲۲۳) (القمر) دون المحال : فإن المحل واحد وهو القبل. (القمر)
أنه بمعنى كيف إلخ: لا يقال: كونه بمعنى كيف يقتضي حل الإتيان في حالة الحيض؛ لأنها حال من الأحوال. أيضًا؛ لأنا نقول حرمة الإتيان في الحيض منصوصة بقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاعْتَزِلُوا النِّسَاء فِي الْمَحِيضِ (البقرة:۲۲۲)، وهو نص وهذه الآية مؤوّلة، فلا تعارضه. (السنبلي)
Explanation of the correspondences of the four previous divisions. 254. Definition of mushkil and its ruling. * The grave-robber (nabbash) is cut off (amputated hand) in all cases, because of his saying: 'Whoever digs up a grave, we cut off (his hand).' We said: It is carried upon policy (siyasa), because it is reported from 'Ali: 'No cutting off (amputation) for the grave-robber (mukhtafi),' and he is the nabbash in the language of the people of Madina. Definition of mushkil and its ruling: As for mushkil, it is that which enters among its forms (ashkal), i.e., speech that is ambiguous among its similars. It is like a stranger who mixes with other people by changing his clothes and appearance, so there is an increase of concealment over khafi. So it corresponds to nass which has an increase of clarity over zahir. Therefore it needs two considerations: request (talab) then contemplation (ta'ammul), as he said. That is, due to the increase of concealment. Its ruling: believing in the truth of what is intended, then undertaking request and contemplation until the intended meaning becomes clear, i.e., the intention of the Lawgiver. In all cases, i.e., whether the grave is in a locked house or not. (Al-Qamar): Because of his saying 'whoever digs up...' etc. The author of al-Hidayah mentioned it and said it is not marfu', and it is said that this hadith is munkar, al-Bayhaqi explicitly declared it weak. In al-Mahalli sharh al-Muwatta', it is narrated that Abu Yusuf said: Hajjaj narrated to us from al-Hakam from Ibrahim and al-Sha'bi that they said: The thief of our dead is cut off (amputated) like the thief of our living. Hajjaj said: And I asked 'Ata' about the grave-robber, so he said: He is cut off. And according to 'Abd al-Razzaq, 'Umar wrote to his governor in Yemen to cut off the hands of a people who were digging graves. (Al-Qamar): 'It is carried upon...' etc.: This is on the assumption of endorsement, otherwise you have known that that hadith is not marfu'. (Al-Qamar): For what was narrated from him ('Ali) 'no cutting off...' etc.: It is said: The author of Fath al-Qadir narrated this text and said it is munkar. And Ibn Abi Shayba narrated from Ibn 'Abbas that he said: 'There is no cutting off for the grave-robber.' Similarly in al-Mahalli. (Al-Qamar): 'So it is that which enters into its forms'—this alludes to the reason for the naming. And 'ashkal' is the plural of 'shikl' (with fatha), meaning 'example' (mithal), as in Muntaha al-Arab. And what is said that it is with two fathas is something I have not found. So 'mushkil' is derived from 'ashkala 'alayya kaza', i.e., it entered among its examples. And according to usuliyyun, it is an expression that bears multiple meanings, and the intended is one of them, but it has entered among its forms (the multiple meanings) and become hidden due to this entry. (Al-Qamar): al-Bayhaqi narrated it in al-Ma'rifah as marfu', from 'Imran ibn Yazid ibn al-Bara' ibn 'Azib, from his father, from his grandfather, in a hadith he mentioned that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever digs up (a grave), we cut off (his hand).' He said in al-Tanqih: In this chain are those whose condition is unknown, like Bishr ibn Hazim and others. [Nasb al-Raya 3/366, 367] He said in Fath al-Qadir: The hadith is munkar. [Ishraq al-Absar 9] Al-'Ayni said in Sharh al-Hidayah: Gharib, with no basis. And Ibn al-Humam said in Fath al-Qadir: This text is munkar. (Ishraq al-Absar) And Ibn Abi Shayba narrated in his Musannaf from Rawh ibn al-Qasim from Mutarrif from 'Ikrima from Ibn 'Abbas who said: There is no cutting off for the grave-robber. [6/531, Chapter: What has come about the grave-robber: is his hand cut off?] [Page 256] Explanation of the correspondences of the four previous divisions. 255. Definition of mushkil and its ruling. That is, the ruling of mushkil: first, believing in the truth of what is intended by Allah Almighty upon merely hearing the speech; then, undertaking the request (talab) for which meanings this word is used; then contemplation (ta'ammul) in it, which meaning is intended here among the meanings, so the intended becomes clear. An example is His statement: {So come to your tillage however you wish} (al-Baqarah: 223). For the word 'anna' is mushkil: it sometimes comes meaning 'from where' as in His statement: {From where (anna) is this to you?} (Aal 'Imran: 3), i.e., from where is this sustenance coming to you every day; and sometimes meaning 'how' as in His statement: {How (anna) can I have a son?} (Aal 'Imran: 40), i.e., how can I have a son. So it became ambiguous here which meaning it is. If it is with the meaning of 'where', then the meaning is 'from any place you wish, front or back', so sodomy with his wife becomes permissible. But if it is with the meaning of 'how', then the meaning is 'in whatever manner you wish, standing, sitting, or lying down', and it indicates generalization of states (ahwal) and not of place (mahall). So when we contemplate the word 'harth' (tillage), we know that it is with the meaning of 'how', because the back is not a place of tillage but rather a place of manure. So sodomy with his wife becomes forbidden, but its prohibition is speculative (zanni) such that one who considers it permissible is not deemed a disbeliever. Contemplation is by looking at the context (siyaq and sabaq). (Al-Qamar): {So come to your tillage...} etc.: Allah Almighty likened the sperm from which children are created to seed, and likened their wombs to earth, and likened children to the produce that comes from the earth. (Al-Qamar): From the word 'anna' being mushkil... etc.: It is said: Request and contemplation cannot be applied to the word 'anna'. For the ambiguity concerning it is either for someone who knows the language or for someone else. The first does not need request because he knows that it is shared between the meanings 'where' and 'how'; he only needs contemplation until it becomes clear that it means 'how' or 'where'. As for the second, khafi is also mushkil for him because he needs to seek its meaning, then contemplate the intended. So contemplate (al-Sunbuli). As in His statement: i.e., narrating the saying of Zakariyya to Maryam, peace be upon our Prophet and her. (Al-Qamar): 'To be' etc.: This is the saying of Zakariyya, peace be upon him, when he was given glad tidings of a child. (Al-Qamar): 'Here' i.e., in His statement: {So come to your tillage however you wish} (al-Baqarah: 223). (Al-Qamar): 'Not of place' (duna al-mahal): for the place is one, which is the front. (Al-Qamar): 'That it is with the meaning of 'how'...' etc.: It cannot be said: Its being with the meaning of 'how' implies permissibility of intercourse during menstruation because it is a state (hal) also. Because we say: Prohibition of intercourse during menstruation is textually stated in His statement: {So keep apart from women during menstruation} (al-Baqarah: 222), which is a nass, while this verse is subject to interpretation (ta'wil), so it does not contradict it. (al-Sunbuli)
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is an usul al-fiqh commentary defining the term 'mushkil' (ambiguous speech) and explaining its ruling within the Hanafi framework. The text opens with an example from fiqh—the ruling on cutting the hand of a grave-robber (nabbash)—to illustrate how a ruling can be ambiguous. The commentator cites a hadith attributed to 'Ali that the nabbash is not subject to amputation, but then discusses the weakness of the opposing hadith. This shows that the ruling on nabbash is not clear-cut, thus fitting the definition of mushkil. The core definition: mushkil is a term that has entered among its 'ashkal' (similar forms or meanings), causing confusion. It is like a stranger who changes his clothes to blend in. It has greater obscurity than khafi, and it corresponds to nass which has greater clarity. The ruling (hukm) of mushkil: first, one must believe that the intended meaning is true; then one must engage in talab (seeking the possible meanings) and ta'ammul (contemplation) until the intended meaning becomes clear. The commentator then provides a classic Hanafi example from Quran 2:223: {So come to your tillage however you wish}. The word 'anna' is mushkil because it can mean 'where' or 'how'. By contemplating the word 'harth' (tillage), which refers to the front, we understand that 'how' is intended, thus forbidding anal intercourse. The passage also addresses a potential objection about menstruation: the verse on tillage does not permit intercourse during menstruation because that is prohibited by a nass (2:222), and this verse is subject to ta'wil (interpretation). Throughout, the commentator follows the Hanafi method of relying on context (siyaq and sabaq) to resolve ambiguity. The discussion reflects the Hanafi text hierarchy where mushkil is above khafi in obscurity.

Key Terms
المشكل (al-mushkil): Speech that has entered among its similar forms (ashkal), bearing multiple meanings, with the intended being one, but hidden due to ambiguity
الخفي (al-khafi): The level of clarity below mushkil; less obscure than mushkil
النص (al-nass): A text that has increase of clarity over zahir, corresponding to mushkil's increase of obscurity
الطلب (al-talab): Request: seeking the possible meanings of a word
التأمل (al-ta'ammul): Contemplation: reflecting on the context to determine which meaning is intended

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition in the passage, what is the first step in dealing with mushkil?
A) Immediately apply qiyas
B) Believe that the intended meaning is true
C) Seek the possible meanings (talab)
D) Contemplate the context (ta'ammul)

Key Takeaway
Mushkil is speech with multiple possible meanings; its resolution requires belief, then talab (seeking meanings), then ta'ammul (contemplation) to identify the intended meaning.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Understanding Al-Mujmal and Its Clarification in Hanafi Usul
Explaining mujmal and its clarification through examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-mujmal, identify its examples, and explain how clarification (bayan) is achieved through prophetic statement, ijtihad, and linguistic analysis.

Core Idea
A mujmal text is ambiguous and requires clarification; if clarification is insufficient, ijtihad is needed.

This lesson explores the concept of al-mujmal (ambiguous) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author illustrates how components of salah and zakat rulings were mujmal until clarified by the Prophet ﷺ or through ijtihad. The riba example shows that when prophetic clarification is incomplete, scholars must engage in ijtihad to determine the effective cause, leading to legitimate ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Define mujmal linguistically and technically
Understand that mujmal is an expression whose intended meaning is not clear without external clarification. The Hanafi school requires evidence (bayan) from the Lawgiver or ijtihad.
Contrast with mufassar (explicitly clarified).
2
Identify the three examples provided
The passage gives examples from salah (components like qa'dah, ruku', etc.), zakat (the obligation and nisab), and riba (the prohibition). For each, note the original ambiguity and how it was resolved.
For salah, the rulings became mufassar through tafsil (detailed explanation) by the Prophet and ijtihad of the Companions.
3
Trace the process from mujmal to mufassar for each example
For salah: components were not explicitly categorized; through reflection, scholars distinguished fard, wajib, sunnah, mustahabb. For zakat: the Quranic command is mujmal; the Prophet clarified with hadith specifying nisab and conditions. For riba: the Quranic prohibition is mujmal; the Prophet gave a hadith listing six commodities but did not specify the illa, leaving it ambiguous.
The riba hadith is considered 'bayan ghayr shafi' (insufficient clarification).
4
Analyse the riba ikhtilaf: why the bayan was not shafi
The Prophet listed six items but did not state the effective cause (illa). Scholars thus deduced different illas: Hanafis: measure and genus; Shafi'is: edibility and monetary value; Malikis: staple and storage. This shows the clarification was not sufficient to remove ambiguity, leading to ijtihad.
Umar's statement confirms the difficulty.
5
Summarize the Hanafi position on the illa for riba
The Hanafi position is that the illa is being measured or weighed (kayl or wazn) and sharing the same genus (jins). This is derived from the common attributes of the listed items.
This illa is considered more comprehensive than the Shafi'i alternative.

Source Text

تعريف المجمل وحكمه: والقعود، والركوع والسجود، والتحريمة، والقراءة، والتسبيحات والأذكار، فلما تأملنا علمنا أن بعضها فرض، وبعضها واجب، وبعضها سنة، وبعضها مستحبة فصار مفسراً بعد أن كان مجملاً، وهكذا الزكاة معناها في اللغة النماء، وذلك غير مراد، فبينها النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بقوله: "هاتوا ربع عشر أموالكم"، وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: "ليس عليك في الذهب شيء حتى يبلغ عشرين مثقالاً، ليس عليك في الفضة شيء حتى يبلغ مائتي درهم"، وهكذا قال في باب السوائم، ثم طلبنا الأسباب والشروط والأوصاف والعلل، فعلمنا أن ملك النصاب علة، وحولان الحول شرط. وأما الكلام في الربا: فإنه مجمل في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَحَرَّمَ الرِّبا﴾ (البقرة:٢٧٥) فإنه مجمل بينه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بقوله: "الحنطة بالحنطة والشعير بالشعير، والتمر بالتمر، والملح بالملح، والذهب بالذهب، والفضة بالفضة مثلاً بمثل يدا بيد، والفضل ربا"، ثم طلبنا الأوصاف لأجل هذا التحريم حتى يعلم حال ما بقي سوى الأشياء الستة، فعلل بعضهم بالقدر والجنس، وبعضهم بالطعم والثمنية، وبعضهم بالاقتيات والاذخار، وفرع كل واحد منهم تفريعا على تعليله، وبالجملة لم يكن البيان شافيًا، فخرج من حيز الإجمال إلى حيز الأشكال، ولهذا قال عمر رضي الله عنه: خرج النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولم يبين لنا أبواب الربا.
Definition of the ambiguous and its ruling: The sitting, bowing, prostration, takbirat al-ihram, recitation, tasbihat and adhkar. When we reflected, we knew that some of them are obligatory (fard), some are necessary (wajib), some are sunnah, and some are recommended (mustahabb). So it became detailed after having been ambiguous. Likewise, zakat: its meaning in language is increase, but that is not intended. So the Prophet ﷺ clarified it by saying: 'Give a quarter of a tenth of your wealth,' and his saying: 'You are not liable for anything in gold until it reaches twenty mithqals, you are not liable for anything in silver until it reaches two hundred dirhams,' and likewise he said in the chapter on grazing livestock. Then we sought the causes, conditions, descriptions, and effective causes, and we learned that ownership of the nisab is the cause, and the passing of a year is the condition. As for the discussion on riba: it is ambiguous in the saying of Allah ﴿And He forbade riba﴾ (2:275), for it is ambiguous. The Prophet ﷺ clarified it by his saying: 'Wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, gold for gold, silver for silver, like for like, hand to hand, and any excess is riba.' Then we sought the descriptions for the sake of this prohibition to know the status of what remains besides the six items. Some reasoned by measure and genus, some by edibility and monetary value, and some by storage and staple, and each one derived subsidiary rulings according to his reasoning. In summary, the clarification was not sufficient, so it moved from the realm of ambiguity to the realm of difficulty. For this reason, Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) said: The Prophet ﷺ passed away and did not clarify for us the doors of riba.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed explanation of the definition of mujmal (ambiguous) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, using practical examples from salah and zakat. The author first lists components of salah (e.g., qa'dah, ruku', sujud, takbir, qira'ah, tasbihat, adhkar) and states that through reflection we know some are fard, some wajib, some sunnah, some mustahabb—thus the ruling becomes mufassar (explained) after being mujmal (ambiguous). Then for zakat, its linguistic meaning ('increase') is not intended; the Prophet clarified it with specific nisab amounts and conditions (ownership of nisab as cause, passing of year as condition). The passage then shifts to riba (usury/interest) as another example: the Quranic prohibition (2:275) is mujmal because it doesn't specify what riba entails. The Prophet clarified with the hadith of the six commodities, but this clarification was not fully sufficient, leading to ikhtilaf among scholars regarding the effective cause (illa). Hanafis adopted measure and genus; Shafi'is adopted edibility and monetary value; Malikis adopted staple and storage. Because the bayan was not shafi (sufficient), the text moved from ijmal (ambiguity) to ishkal (difficulty), as noted by Umar's statement. This demonstrates a key principle: when prophetic clarification is incomplete, ijtihad is required.

Key Terms
المجمل (al-mujmal): An expression that is ambiguous in its intended meaning, requiring clarification
المفسر (al-mufassar): An expression that has been clarified to remove ambiguity
البيان الشافي (al-bayan al-shafi): Sufficient clarification that removes all ambiguity and leaves no room for ijtihad

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the Hanafi scholars consider the hadith on riba to be a 'bayan ghayr shafi' (insufficient clarification)?
A) Because the hadith does not include all types of riba, such as interest on loans.
B) Because the hadith lists six items but does not specify the exact illa, leading to ikhtilaf.
C) Because the hadith is ahad and thus weak.
D) Because the hadith contradicts the Quranic verse on riba.

Key Takeaway
A mujmal text requires clarification; when the clarification is insufficient, ijtihad is necessary, and legitimate ikhtilaf may arise.

Definition of Majaz (Figurative Meaning) in Hanafi Usul
Definition of Majaz and its distinction from Haqiqah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of majaz, distinguish it from haqiqah, and apply the criteria of wad' and 'alaqah to classify words.

Core Idea
Majaz: a word used for other than its original meaning due to a valid connection, requiring no direct coining for that meaning.

In Hanafi usul, understanding majaz is essential for interpreting the Qur'an and Sunnah. This lesson provides the precise definition and illustrates how a single word can shift between haqiqah and majaz depending on the type of coining (wad'). We will explore the conditions and the key example of 'salat'.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the definition of majaz
Read the definition: majaz is a word used for other than its original meaning due to a connection (munasaba) between them. This excludes haqiqah.
The definition explicitly requires a connection; otherwise it would be error (khata).
2
Understand the role of munasaba
Munasaba (connection) is the relationship that justifies the figurative use, such as similarity, causality, or customary association. This distinguishes majaz from misusage.
Hanafis accept a broad range of connections, including custom-based ones.
3
Differentiate types of wad'
Wad' (coining) can be linguistic, legal, or customary. Haqiqah requires that the word is coined for its meaning in at least one of these. Majaz occurs when there is no coining for that meaning in any of these wad's.
For example, 'dabba' is coined in general custom for all quadrupeds.
4
Apply the definition to 'salat'
The word 'salat' is linguistically coined for supplication (du'a), so that is linguistic haqiqah. But the Lawgiver coined it for the ritual prayer, making that legal haqiqah. Thus, in a legal context, using 'salat' for supplication is a legal majaz.
This illustrates how context determines haqiqah vs. majaz.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المجاز فاسم لما أريد به غير ما وضع له لمناسبة بينهما أي اسم لكل لفظ أريد به أي بقيد المناسبة غير ما وضع له خرج به الحقيقة. (القمر) لكل لفظ إيماء إلى أن المراد بكلمة ما اللفظ. (القمر) فوضع عرفي عام كوضع الدابة لذوات القوائم الأربع (القمر) بشيء من الأوضاع أي بوضع من الأوضاع المذكورة، والغرض: أنه لا يشترط في الحقيقة أن يكون اللفظ موضوعًا للمعنى في جميع الأوضاع المذكورة، بل يكفي تحقق وضع ما من الأوضاع المذكورة. (القمر) وفي المجاز :إلخ أي المعتبر في المجاز عدم الوضع في الجملة لا أن لا يكون موضوعًا لمعناه في شيء من الأوضاع المذكورة، فالصلاة في الدعاء حقيقة لغوية، وفي الأركان المخصوصة مجاز لغوي، وعند أرباب الشرع ففي الأركان المخصوصة حقيقة وفي الدعاء ،مجاز، وقس على هذا. (القمر) فهما أي الحقيقة والمجاز، وهذا تفريع على أخذ اللفظ في تعريف الحقيقة والمجاز. (القمر) وقد يوصف إلخ كما يقال: المعنى الحقيقة والمعنى المجاز، والاستعمال الحقيقة والاستعمال المجاز. (القمر) إما مجازا لملابسة الظاهرة بين اللفظ والمعنى، وكذا بين اللفظ والاستعمال. (القمر) من خطأ إلخ لا يخفى عليك أن حمله على خطأ العوام من خطأ الخواص، ألا ترى أنه عند تحقق العلاقة كيف يتحقق الخطأ. (القمر) وجود إلخ ليس المراد بالوجود ما هو المتبادر منه وهو الوجود الخارجي، فإن الوجود الخارجي للموضوع له ليس بلازم؛ إذ قد يكون اعتباريًا بل سلبيًا محضا بل المراد منه الثبوت العلمي. (القمر) وجود ما وضع له أي ثبوت حكمه قطعا . [ إفاضة الأنوار: ۹۸] وأما المجاز من جاز المكان إذا تعداه، ووجه المناسبة: أن اللفظ إذا استعمل في غير الموضع له فقد تعدى عن المكان الأصلي (القمر) : غير ما وضع له خرج به الحقيقة. (القمر) لكل لفظ إيماء إلى أن المراد بكلمة ما اللفظ. (القمر)
As for majaz, it is a name for what is used for other than what it was coined for due to a connection between them — i.e., a name for every word used, with the condition of connection, for other than what it was coined for; this excludes haqiqah. (Al-Qamar) 'For every word' indicates that the intended meaning of 'ma' (what) is 'lafz' (word). (Al-Qamar) So general customary coining: like the coining of 'dabba' for quadrupedal animals. (Al-Qamar) 'By any of the coinings' — i.e., by a coining from the mentioned coinings. The purpose: that it is not a condition in haqiqah that the word is coined for the meaning in all the mentioned coinings; rather, the realization of some coining from the mentioned coinings suffices. (Al-Qamar) 'And in majaz' etc. — i.e., the criterion in majaz is the absence of coining in general, not that it is not coined for its meaning in any of the mentioned coinings. Thus 'salat' for supplication is a linguistic haqiqah, and for specific pillars it is a linguistic majaz; but according to the people of the Shari'ah, for the specific pillars it is a (legal) haqiqah, and for supplication it is (a legal) majaz. And measure similarly. (Al-Qamar) So both — i.e., haqiqah and majaz — and this is a branching upon taking the word in the definition of haqiqah and majaz. (Al-Qamar) 'And sometimes they are described' etc. — as it is said: the literal meaning and the figurative meaning, and literal usage and figurative usage. (Al-Qamar) 'Either figurative' due to an apparent connection between the word and the meaning, and likewise between the word and the usage. (Al-Qamar) 'Or from error' — it is not hidden from you that carrying it to the error of the common people is the error of the elite. Do you not see that when the relationship (al-alaqah) is realized, how can error occur? (Al-Qamar) 'Existence' etc. — what is intended by 'existence' is not the apparent meaning which is external existence, for the external existence of the coined thing is not necessary; it may be conceptual or even purely negative. Rather, the intended meaning is cognitive confirmation (al-thubut al-'ilmi). (Al-Qamar) 'Existence of what it was coined for' — i.e., confirmation of its ruling definitively. [From Ifaadat al-Anwar: 98] As for majaz, it is from 'jaza al-makan' (to pass beyond), and the aspect of appropriateness is that when the word is used for other than its (original) place, it has passed beyond its original place. (Al-Qamar) 'Other than what it was coined for' excludes haqiqah. (Al-Qamar) 'For every word' indicates that the intended meaning of 'ma' is 'lafz'. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage defines majaz (figurative meaning) in Hanafi usul. Majaz is a word used for other than its original meaning, but with a connection (munasaba) between the original and figurative meanings. The commentary from 'al-Qamar' clarifies: the criterion for majaz is the lack of a direct coining (wad') for that meaning. For example, the word 'salat' is linguistically coined for supplication (du'a) — so in that use it is haqiqah lughawiyyah. But the Lawgiver (Shari') coined it for the specific ritual prayer with pillars (arkan makhsusa). Therefore, in legal context, 'salat' for the ritual is haqiqah shar'iyyah, and for supplication it becomes a legal majaz. This illustrates how the same word can shift between haqiqah and majaz depending on the type of coining. The passage also emphasizes that existence of the meaning (actually, its cognitive confirmation) is sufficient: it does not require external concrete existence. The text notes that majaz is distinct from error (khata); error occurs when there is no valid 'alaqah (relationship). The Hanafi usul position is that majaz is permissible and widely used in Quran and Hadith, provided there is a proper connection recognized by Arabic speakers. The ruling (hukm) of majaz is that it conveys the intended figurative meaning, not the literal one, but its use is conditioned on a qarina (contextual indicator) to prevent ambiguity. This definition differs from the Shafi'i view in subtle ways: Hanafis consider 'urf (custom) as a source of wad', allowing for broader categories of haqiqah and majaz.

Key Terms
المجاز (al-majāz): A word used for other than its original meaning due to a suitable connection.
المناسبة (العلاقة) (al-munāsabah (al-ʿalāqah)): The suitable connection or relationship between the original meaning and the figurative meaning, such as similarity, causality, etc.
وضع عرفي عام (waḍʿ ʿurfī ʿāmm): General customary coining, like 'dabba' for all quadrupeds, though linguistically it might be for a specific type.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is 'salat' considered haqiqah shar'iyyah when used for the ritual prayer, but majaz when used for supplication (du'a)?
A) Because the Lawgiver coined it for the ritual, so that use is literal in legal context, while supplication is its linguistic original but not legal.
B) Because it is used for the ritual first and then transferred to supplication later.
C) Because the ritual prayer has pillars and supplication does not.
D) Because the word 'salat' originally meant 'prayer' in every language.

Key Takeaway
Majaz is a legitimate linguistic tool in the Shari'ah when there is a recognized connection and no direct coining for that meaning.
