بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث
بيان استحالة الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز
" في دار "فلان" في سكنى فلان، وهو معنى مجازي شامل للملك والإجارة والعارية فيحنث بعموم المجاز لا بالجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز لكن يرد عليه أنه ذكر في "الفتاوى": أنه إن لم تكن تلك الدار سكنى لفلان بل كانت ملكًا عاطلةً عن السكونة يحنث أيضًا إلا أن يقال: إن السكنى أعم من أن يكون تحقيقا أو تقديرًا. وإنما يحنث إذا قدم ليلاً أو نهارًا في قوله : عبده حر يوم يقدم فلان جواب سؤال آخر تقريره: أنه إذا حلف أحد فقال: عبدي حر يوم يقدم فلان، فاليوم حقيقة في النهار، ومجاز في الليل. وأنتم جمعتم بينهما وقلتم بأنه إن قدم فلان ليلاً أو نهارًا يعتق العبد، فأجاب بأنه إنما يحنث في هذا المثال بالقدوم ليلاً أو نهاراً؛ لأن المراد باليوم الوقت وهو عام أي الوقت معنى الملك في دار فلان إلخ هذا جواب نقض آخر تقريره أنه لو حلف "لا يدخل داره" يحنث بدخول دار سكناه إجارة مع أن الإضافة حقيقة في الملك، فدار السكنى داره مجازًا، ويحنث أيضًا بدار مسكونة مملوكة له، وهو داره حقيقة فيلزم الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز، وأنكم منعتموه وحاصل الجواب أن الإضافة للاختصاص المطلق إما حقيقة أو مجازا بدلالة القرينة هي أن الرجل لا يهجر الدار إلا للنفرة عن المالك، والاختصاص يعم والسكنى، فحينئذٍ تتناول المسكونة المملوكة وغيرها بطريق الحقيقة وعموم المجاز فلا جمع، وإذا أريد مطلق الاختصاص فيحنث بمملوكه غير مسكونة أي بدخوله فيها؛ لأن له أيضًا اختصاصا به وبهذا يظهر جواب ما أورد الشارح بعد ذلك بقول قاضي خان على جواب النقض. (السنبلي) أنه ذكر في "الفتاوى": أي فتاوى فخر الدين قاضي خان وفيه خلاف للسرخسي . له فإنه عنده يتبادر الاختصاص بالسكني، سواء كان ملكا أم لا، بقرينة الهجران فلا يحنث بالدخول في دار مملوكة غير مسكونة فتدبر . (السنبلي) عاطلة في "منتهى الأرب" يستعمل العطل في الخلو عن الشيء، وإن كان أصله في الخلو عن الحلي. (القمر) يحنث أيضا أي بالدخول فيها، وهذا عند قاضي خان، وأما عند شمس الأئمة، فلا يحنث لانقطاع نسبة السكني. (القمر)
أو تقديرًا بأن يتمكن من السكنى تمكنا تاما بخلاف ما إذا استأجر الدار أو استعارها و لم يسكنها فلا يحنث الحالف بالدخول فيها؛ لأن التمكن ههنا ضروري بضرورة العقد وليس تامًا كذا قيل. (القمر)
وإنما يحنث إلخ: اعلم أن اليمين شرعًا عبارة عن عقد قوي به عزم الحالف على الفعل أو الترك، فدخل فيه التعليق، وهو ربط حصول مضمون جملة بحصول مضمون جملة أخرى، فإنه يمين شرعًا، والحنث فيه هو وقوع ما علق. (القمر)

بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث مجازي شامل للنهار والليل، فيحنث باعتبار عموم المجاز لا باعتبار الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز، وقيل: هو مشترك بين النهار وبين مطلق الوقت، فأريد ههنا معنى الوقت، وبالجملة لابد ههنا من بيان ضابطة يعرف بها أنه في أي موضع يراد به النهار وفي أي موضع يراد به الوقت، فقيل: إذا كان الفعل ممتدا يراد به النهار؛ لأنه زمان ممتد يصلح أن يكون معيارا للفعل، وإن كان غير ممتد يراد به الوقت المطلق؛ لأنه يكفي لذلك الفعل جزء من الوقت، ولكنهم اختلفوا في أنه أيّ فعل يعتبر في هذا الباب المضاف إليه أو العامل، فالضابطة أنه إذا كانا الفعل وقيل إلخ إشارة بكلمة التمريض إلى أن كون لفظ اليوم مشتركا بين النهار ومطلق الوقت، ليس بجيد، وإن كان يشعر به كلام "المحيط"، وأقر به أعظم العلماء أي مولانا عبد السلام الله - والأصح أنه مجاز في مطلق الوقت ترجيحا للمجاز على الاشتراك كما تقرر في مقره كذا في "التحقق". (القمر) وقيل: هو مشترك إلخ هذا عند البعض، وعلى هذا فليس مما نحن فيه فلا يراد أصلاً، وعند الأكثر مجاز فيه، وفي الكشف وهو الأصح ترجيحا للمجاز على الاشتراك. (السنبلي) إذا كان الفعل ممتدا : هو ما يصح فيه ضرب المدة: أي يصح تقديره بمدة كالركوب، فإنه يصح أن يقال: ركبت هذه الدابة يوما، وغير الممتد بخلافه كالقدوم، وقال شارح "الوقاية": إن المراد بالفعل الممتد ممتد يمكن أن يستوعب امتداده النهار لا مطلق الامتداد؛ لأنهم جعلوا التكلم من قبيل غير الممتد، ولا شك أن المتكلم ممتد زمانًا طويلاً لكن لا يمتد بحيث يستوعب النهار عادة وعرفًا. (القمر) ممتدا إلخ وهذه الضابطة تؤيد بأن تقدير "في" يوجب الاستيعاب وههنا لما كان في مقدرة وجب استيعابه للمظروف، فإذا كان ممتدا فيمكن استيعاب النهار إياه، فأمكن المعنى الحقيقي، فيحمل عليه لأصالته، وأما إذا كان غير ممتد فلا يمكن استيعاب النهار إياه فلا يحمل عليه بل على مطلق الوقت الأعم من أجزائه وأجزاء الليل والعلامة العموم، فإن مطلق الوقت عام من النهار، وهذا يرشدك إلى أن العبرة لعامله المظروف لا لما أضيف إليه فتدبر. (السنبلي)
يراد به إلخ إلا إذا دل الدليل والقرينة على أن المراد باليوم الوقت كما تقول: "أركبوا يوم يأتيكم العدو". (القمر) لأنه أي لأن النهار زمان ممتد إلخ مع أنه معنى حقيقي للفظ اليوم، فكان أولى بالإرادة. (القمر) يراد به الوقت المطلق أي سواء كان من النهار أو من الليل إلا إذا دل الدليل والقرينة على أن المراد باليوم النهار كما تقول: "عبدي حر يوم ينكشف الشمس". (القمر) إذا كانا أي المضاف إليه والعامل. (القمر)
Explanation of the divisions of the third division. Explanation of the impossibility of combining literal (haqiqah) and figurative (majaz) meaning. "In the house of 'so-and-so' in the dwelling of so-and-so" - this is a figurative meaning inclusive of ownership, lease, and loan, so he violates the oath by the generality of the figurative meaning, not by combining literal and figurative. But it is objected that it is mentioned in al-Fatawa: if that house is not a dwelling for so-and-so but rather an unoccupied property free of dwelling, he also violates the oath. Unless it is said that dwelling is more general, either actually or virtually. And he only violates the oath if he comes at night or during the day in his statement: "his slave is free on the day so-and-so arrives" - answer to another question: if someone swears and says: "my slave is free on the day so-and-so arrives", then 'day' literally means daytime, and figuratively means night. And you have combined both and said that if so-and-so arrives at night or during the day, the slave is freed. He answered that he only violates the oath in this example by arriving at night or during the day because what is meant by 'day' is time, which is general - i.e., time in the sense of ownership. In the house of so-and-so etc. This is another rebuttal answer: if he swore "he will not enter his house", he violates the oath by entering a house he rents as a dwelling, even though the construct (idafa) literally means ownership, so the rented house is his figuratively, and he also violates by entering an occupied house he owns, which is his literally, so combining literal and figurative would be necessary, and you have prevented it. The gist of the answer is that the construct (idafa) is for absolute specific relationship (ikhtisas), either literally or figuratively indicated by context - which is that a man does not leave a house except due to aversion to the owner, and specific relationship (ikhtisas) includes both ownership and dwelling. Consequently, it includes both the occupied owned house and others by way of literal meaning and generality of figurative meaning, so there is no combination. And if absolute specific relationship is intended, he violates by entering his owned unoccupied house because he also has a specific relationship to it. By this, the answer to what the commentator (sharih) raised subsequently by the statement of Qadi Khan regarding the rebuttal's answer becomes clear. (al-Sunbuli) It is mentioned in al-Fatawa: i.e., Fatawa Fakhr al-Din Qadi Khan, and there is a disagreement with al-Sarakhsi. For he (al-Sarakhsi) holds that specific relationship to dwelling is what comes to mind, whether ownership or not, due to the context of leaving (the house), so he does not violate by entering an owned unoccupied house. So ponder. (al-Sunbuli) 'Atila (unoccupied) in Muntaha al-Arab: 'utl is used for emptiness of a thing, though its origin is emptiness of ornaments. (al-Qamar) He also violates i.e., by entering it - this is according to Qadi Khan. As for Shams al-A'imma, he does not violate due to the interruption of the attribution of dwelling. (al-Qamar) Or virtually, by being able to dwell fully, unlike if he leased or borrowed the house and did not dwell in it - then the swearer does not violate by entering it because the ability here is necessary by contract and not complete. Thus it is said. (al-Qamar) "And he only violates" etc.: Know that an oath legally is a strong contract by which the swearer resolves to do or not do something. So it includes ta'liq (suspension), which is linking the occurrence of the content of one clause to the occurrence of the content of another clause - it is an oath legally, and violating it is the occurrence of what was suspended. (al-Qamar) Explanation of the divisions of the third division: figurative inclusive of night and day, so he violates by the generality of the figurative meaning, not by combining literal and figurative. And it is said that it is a homonym (mushtarak) between daytime and absolute time, so here the meaning of time is intended. In summary, a rule must be established by which it is known when daytime is meant and when time is meant. It is said: if the action is extended (mumtadd), daytime is meant because it is an extended time suitable as a measure for the action; if it is non-extended, absolute time is meant because a part of time suffices for that action. But they differed as to which action is considered in this regard: the one attached to (the word 'day') or the operative (factor). The rule is that if both the action... etc. (al-Qamar) "It is said" etc. - an indication by the word of tamrid (suggestion of weakness) that the view that the word 'day' is homonymous between daytime and absolute time is not good, even if the wording of al-Muhit suggests it, and the greatest scholars, i.e., Mawlana Abd al-Salam Allah, affirmed it. The correct view is that it is figurative for absolute time, preferring figurative meaning over homonymy as established in its place. Thus in al-Tahqiq. (al-Qamar) "And it is said: it is homonymous" etc. - this according to some; on this view, it is not what we are discussing, so it is not intended at all. According to most, it is figurative for it, and in al-Kashshaf, the correct view is preferring figurative over homonymy. (al-Sunbuli) "If the action is extended" i.e., it is valid to specify a period, like riding, for it is valid to say: I rode this animal for a day; non-extended is the opposite, like arriving. The commentator of al-Wiqayah said: by extended action is meant that whose extension can encompass the entire daytime, not absolute extension, because they classified speaking as non-extended, and there is no doubt that a speaker extends over a long time but not so as to encompass the daytime usually and customarily. (al-Qamar) "Extended" etc. - This rule is supported by the fact that the estimation of 'fi' (in) necessitates encompassment, and here since 'fi' is estimated, it must encompass the container. So if the action is extended, it is possible for the daytime to encompass it, so the literal meaning is possible and is adopted due to its primacy. As for when it is non-extended, it is impossible for the daytime to encompass it, so it is not adopted; rather, absolute time which is more general than its parts and the parts of night, and the sign is generality. This guides you to consider the container (the action) not the thing attached (the word 'day'). So ponder. (al-Sunbuli) "Daytime is intended" etc. except if evidence and context indicate that what is meant by 'day' is time, as you say: "Ride on the day the enemy comes to you." (al-Qamar) Because daytime is extended time etc., and it is the literal meaning of the word 'day', so it is more deserving of being intended. (al-Qamar) "Absolute time is intended" i.e., whether from daytime or night, except if evidence and context indicate that what is meant by 'day' is daytime, as you say: "My slave is free on the day the sun rises." (al-Qamar) "If both" i.e., the thing attached (the word 'day') and the operative (factor). (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a matn from Noor al-Anwar, explaining the principle that one cannot simultaneously intend both the literal (haqiqah) and figurative (majaz) meaning of a word in a single context, specifically regarding oaths. The author presents two objections to this principle and their resolutions. The first objection involves the phrase 'in the house of so-and-so' in the sense of 'dwelling'—a figurative meaning covering ownership, lease, and loan. The response clarifies that the construct (idafa) indicates absolute specific relationship (ikhtisas), which can be literal (ownership) or figurative (dwelling) based on context. Thus, entering either an owned or rented house constitutes a violation (hanth) via the figurative meaning's generality, not by combining both. The second objection concerns the oath 'my slave is free on the day so-and-so arrives'—'day' literally means daytime and figuratively night. The response argues that 'day' here means absolute time, which is more general, so arriving at any time triggers the oath via figurative generality. The passage then establishes a rule: if the action is extended (e.g., riding), 'day' retains its literal meaning (daytime) because it can encompass the action; if non-extended (e.g., arriving), 'day' takes the figurative meaning of absolute time. Internal Hanafi differences are noted: Qadi Khan holds that a swore enters a house by entering any property he has a specific relationship to, while Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi limits it to actual dwelling due to the context of leaving. The commentary further clarifies that the preferable view is that 'day' is figurative for absolute time, not homonymous, prioritizing majaz over ishtirak (homonymy). The rule depends on the action's ability to be measured by the daytime: extended actions allow literal meaning; non-extended actions require figurative meaning. This is a foundational usul principle applied to oath cases.

Key Terms
حقيقة (haqiqah): Literal meaning of a word as originally coined, e.g., 'day' for daytime
مجاز (majaz): Figurative meaning used when literal is impossible or context indicates, e.g., 'day' for absolute time
حنث (hanth): Violation of an oath by the occurrence of the condition or action sworn against
إضافة (idafah): Construct phrase (e.g., 'daruhu') indicating ownership or relationship
اختصاص (ikhtisas): Specific relationship between a person and property, including ownership and dwelling rights
ممتدد (mumtadd): Extended action that can be measured by a period, e.g., riding
غير ممتدد (ghayr mumtadd): Non-extended action that does not occupy a full period, e.g., arrival

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rule in this lesson, if a man swears 'my horse is free on the day I race it' and races it at night, what is the ruling?
A) The horse is not freed because 'day' means daytime literally.
B) The horse is freed because racing is an extended action, so 'day' means absolute time figurative.
C) The horse is not freed because the oath is invalid due to ambiguity.
D) The horse is freed because 'day' is homonymous between day and night.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a word in an oath can only bear one meaning—literal or figurative—determined by context and the nature of the action; combining both is impossible.
